تشريح:- مصنف ، کتاب اللہ کی بحث سے فارغ ہو کر سنت کی بحث شروع کر رہے ہیں۔ سنت کے لغوی معنی طریقہ اور عادت“ کے ہیں، اور اصطلاح شرع میں سنت ان نفلی عبادتوں کو کہتے ہیں جن کے کرنے پر ثواب ہوتا ہے اور چھوڑنے پر عتاب نہیں ہوتا ہے، یہاں سنت سے مراد وہ ہے جو قران کے علاوہ رسول اللہ صلی ہی تم سے صادر ہوا ہو، قول، فعلاً یا تقريراً، تقرير صادر ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ آپ نے کسی فعل کو دیکھ کر یا کسی قول کو سنکر سکوت فرمایا ہو، نکیر نہ کی ہو اصولیین کے یہاں حدیث اور سنت میں فرق یہ ہے کہ حدیث کا اطلاق صرف آپ صلیہ السلام کے قول پر ہوتا ہے، اور سنت کا اطلاق آپ سال یا ایہام کے قول فعل اور سکوت پر ہوتا ہے، اسی طرح صحابہ کے اقوال وافعال پر ہوتا ہے، صاحب حسامی نے یہاں سنت کا لفظ اس لئے استعمال کیا ہے تا کہ یہ لفظ رسول اللہ صلی این ایم کے قول و فعل اور تقریر اور صحابہ کے اقوال و افعال کو شامل ہو جائے۔
اعلم ان سنة رسول الله : - مصنف سے فرماتے ہیں کہ کتاب اللہ کی جس طرح ہیں قسمیں بیان ہوئیں خاص، عام ،مشترک ،مؤول ، ظاہر، نص، مفسر، محکم، خفی، مشکل، مجمل، متشابہ وغیرہ یہ ساری قسمیں سنت میں بھی جاری ہوتی ہیں، ایسے ہی امر، نہی وغیرہ بھی کتاب اللہ کی طرح سنت میں بھی ہوتا ہے، کیونکہ کتاب اللہ کی طرح سنت بھی دلیل و حجت ہے، لہذا ان اقسام کو ان کے احکام کے ساتھ بیان کرنے میں کتاب اللہ اصل ہے اور سنت اس کی فرع ہے، تو ان اقسام کو الگ سے بیان کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، کتاب اللہ پر قیاس کر لیں ،۔۔البتہ طریق اتصال میں سنت کتاب اللہ سے الگ ہے، کیونکہ کتاب اللہ کے ہم تک پہنچنے کا ایک راستہ متعین ہے، یعنی تو اتر اور سنت رسول کے بہت سے طریقے ہیں ، صرف تواتر نہیں ہے، اور یہ باب خاص طور پر اسی طرق کو بیان کرنے کے لئے منعقد کیا گیا ہے، خلاصہ یہ کہ اس باب میں صرف وہ چیز میں بیان کی جائے گی جو سنت کے ساتھ خاص ہیں ، کتاب اللہ میں نہیں پائی جاتیں، وہ چار چیزیں ہیں، (۱) کیفیت اتصال کا بیان (۲) انقطاع کا بیان (۳) محل خبر کا بیان (۴) نفس خبر کا بیان، وغیرہ۔ السنة نوعان : - مصنف ، اللہ کہتے ہیں کہ سنت کی دو قسمیں ہیں، (۱) مرسل (۲) مسند۔ مرسل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں تابعی اپنے اور رسول اللہ صلی سی ایم کے درمیان واسطہ چھوڑ دے اور یوں کہے ”قال رسول الله صلى الله علیه وسلم كذا سنت مرسل کی چار قسمیں ہیں، (۱) مرسل صحابی (۲) مرسل تابعی (۳) مرسل تبع تابعی (۴) مرسل من وجه دون وجه
مرسل صحابی اس وقت ہوتی ہے جب صحابی نے وہ حدیث رسول اللہ صل علیہ السلام سے براہ راست نہ سنی ہو، بلکہ کسی صحابی سے سنی ہو، اور روایت کرتے وقت صحابی کا نام ترک کر دے۔
Commentary: The author, after finishing the discussion of the Book of Allah, begins the discussion of Sunnah. The lexical meaning of Sunnah is 'way' and 'custom'. In legal terminology, Sunnah refers to supererogatory acts of worship for which there is reward but no punishment for leaving. Here, Sunnah is intended to be what emanated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) besides the Qur'an: saying, action, or tacit approval. Tacit approval means he saw an action or heard a statement and remained silent, not disapproving. According to usuliyyun, the difference between hadith and Sunnah is that hadith applies only to the saying of the Prophet, while Sunnah applies to his saying, action, and silence, and similarly to the sayings and actions of the Companions. The author (Sahib al-Husami) used the word Sunnah here so that it includes the saying, action, and tacit approval of the Prophet and the sayings and actions of the Companions. He said: 'Know that the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah...' The author states that just as the divisions of the Book were explained: specific, general, common, interpreted, manifest, text, explained, clear, hidden, difficult, summary, ambiguous etc., all these divisions also apply to the Sunnah. Likewise, command, prohibition etc. also occur in the Sunnah as in the Book. Because the Sunnah is also a proof and evidence like the Book. Therefore, the Book is the origin and the Sunnah is its branch in explaining these divisions with their rulings. So there is no need to explain these divisions separately; one can analogize from the Book. However, in the manner of transmission, the Sunnah is different from the Book because the Book has a single path of transmission to us (tawatur), while the Sunnah has many paths, not only tawatur. This chapter is specifically devoted to explaining these paths. In summary, this chapter will only discuss what is specific to the Sunnah and not found in the Book: four things: (1) the quality of connection, (2) the quality of disconnection, (3) the place of the report, (4) the report itself, etc. The Sunnah is of two types: Mursal and Musnad. Mursal is a hadith in which the Tabi'i omits the intermediary between himself and the Prophet and says 'the Messenger of Allah said such and such.' There are four types of Mursal: (1) Mursal of a Companion, (2) Mursal of a Tabi'i, (3) Mursal of a Tab' Tabi'i, (4) Mursal from one aspect but not another. The Mursal of a Companion occurs when a Companion did not hear that hadith directly from the Prophet but heard it from another Companion, and when narrating he omits the name of that Companion.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This pasage is an expansion (sharh) on the definition of Sunnah and the divisions of Mursal. The commentator begins by explaining the term Sunnah: lexically it means 'way', and legally it refers to supererogatory acts. However, in this usul work, Sunnah is used in a broader sense: everything that issued from the Prophet (peace be upon him) besides the Qur'an, including his sayings, actions, and tacit approvals. Tacit approval is when he saw or heard something and did not object. The commentator then clarifies the difference between hadith and Sunnah according to the usuliyyun: hadith is specific to the Prophet's sayings, while Sunnah includes his sayings, actions, and silences, and also the sayings and actions of the Companions. The author of Husami used 'Sunnah' to encompass all of this. Next, the commentator reiterates that all the textual categories found in the Qur'an (specific, general, etc.) also apply to the Sunnah, because the Sunnah is also a proof. Hence, the chapter only covers what is unique to the Sunnah: the ways of transmission (ittisal and ingita'), the subject of the report, and the report itself. Finally, the commentator details the types of Mursal: the Mursal of a Companion (when a Companion omits the name of the Companion he heard it from), Mursal of a Tabi'i, Mursal of a Tab' Tabi'i, and Mursal from one aspect but not another. The explanation is limited to defining these terms and setting the framework for further discussion.

Key Terms
حَدِيث (hadith): According to usuliyyun, hadith is specifically the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him), not his actions or tacit approvals.
مُرْسَل صَحَابِي (mursal sahabi): A hadith where a Companion narrates from another Companion but omits the intermediary's name, so it appears as if from the Prophet.
تَقْرِير (taqrir): The Prophet's tacit approval: he saw or heard something and remained silent, indicating permissibility or approval.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the usuliyyun as explained in this passage, how does 'Sunnah' differ from 'hadith'?
A) Hadith includes actions and approvals, while Sunnah is only sayings.
B) Sunnah is only supererogatory acts, while hadith is all reports.
C) Hadith is only the Prophet's sayings, while Sunnah includes sayings, actions, and approvals, and also Companion statements.
D) They are synonyms with no difference.

Key Takeaway
In usul al-fiqh, Sunnah is broader than hadith, encompassing prophetic sayings, actions, and approvals, and Mursal is a type of non-continuous report with four subcategories.

Definition of Sunnah in Hanafi Usul
Defining Sunnah and its relation to the Quran's textual categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Sunnah in Hanafi usul and distinguish it from hadith and from the fiqh meaning of sunnah.

Core Idea
Sunnah is the Prophet's words, actions, and approvals — a source of law alongside the Quran, with its own transmission rules.

This passage opens the chapter on Sunnah after the discussion of the Book of Allah. The commentator clarifies that here 'Sunnah' does not mean recommended acts but the prophetic revelation beyond the Quran. The passage then explains that all Quranic textual categories apply to Sunnah, so the only new topics are transmission-related.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the shift from Quran to Sunnah
The author has completed the discussion of the Book of Allah and now begins the discussion of Sunnah. Note that Sunnah, like the Quran, is a source of legislation.
The term 'Sunnah' here is used in its usul sense, not the fiqh sense of a recommended act.
2
Define Sunnah terminologically
Identify the three components of Sunnah: the Prophet's statements (qawl), actions (fi'l), and tacit approvals (taqrir). Also, the Hanafi school includes the statements and actions of the Companions.
Taqrir means the Prophet remained silent upon witnessing something, thereby approving it.
3
Distinguish Sunnah from hadith
According to the passage, hadith is limited to the Prophet's statements, while Sunnah is broader, covering actions and approvals as well. This distinction is crucial for source classification.
Some later scholars use the terms interchangeably, but this passage maintains a clear difference.
4
Note the relationship to Quranic categories
All the textual categories of the Quran (specific, general, apparent, etc.) apply equally to Sunnah. Therefore, the chapter will not repeat them but will focus on what is unique to Sunnah: the ways it is transmitted to us.
The Quran reaches us only through tawatur (mass transmission), while Sunnah can be transmitted through multiple modes including ahad.

اعلم ان سنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : - مصنف سے فرماتے ہیں کہ کتاب اللہ کی جس طرح ہیں قسمیں بیان ہوئیں خاص، عام ،مشترک ،مؤول ، ظاہر، نص، مفسر، محکم، خفی، مشکل، مجمل، متشابہ وغیرہ یہ ساری قسمیں سنت میں بھی جاری ہوتی ہیں، ایسے ہی امر، نہی وغیرہ بھی کتاب اللہ کی طرح سنت میں بھی ہوتا ہے، کیونکہ کتاب اللہ کی طرح سنت بھی دلیل و حجت ہے، لہذا ان اقسام کو ان کے احکام کے ساتھ بیان کرنے میں کتاب اللہ اصل ہے اور سنت اس کی فرع ہے، تو ان اقسام کو الگ سے بیان کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، کتاب اللہ پر قیاس کر لیں،۔۔البتہ طریق اتصال میں سنت کتاب اللہ سے الگ ہے، کیونکہ کتاب اللہ کے ہم تک پہنچنے کا ایک راستہ متعین ہے، یعنی تواتر اور سنت رسول کے بہت سے طریقے ہیں ، صرف تواتر نہیں ہے، اور یہ باب خاص طور پر اسی طرق کو بیان کرنے کے لئے منعقد کیا گیا ہے، خلاصہ یہ کہ اس باب میں صرف وہ چیز میں بیان کی جائے گی جو سنت کے ساتھ خاص ہیں ، کتاب اللہ میں نہیں پائی جاتیں، وہ چار چیزیں ہیں، (۱) کیفیت اتصال کا بیان (۲) انقطاع کا بیان (۳) محل خبر کا بیان (۴) نفس خبر کا بیان، وغیرہ۔
Commentary: The author, having finished the discussion of the Book of Allah, begins the discussion of Sunnah. The lexical meaning of Sunnah is 'path' and 'custom', and in the technical sense of Sharia, Sunnah refers to those supererogatory acts of worship for which there is reward for doing and no punishment for leaving. Here, Sunnah means that which, besides the Quran, issued from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, whether by statement, action, or tacit approval. Tacit approval means that he saw an action or heard a statement and remained silent, not expressing disapproval. According to the usuliyun, the difference between hadith and Sunnah is that hadith applies only to the statement of the Prophet, while Sunnah applies to his statement, action, and silence, and similarly to the statements and actions of the Companions. The author of al-Husami used the term Sunnah so that it would include the statement, action, and tacit approval of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and the statements and actions of the Companions.

Know that the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah... The author says that just as the Book of Allah has categories: specific, general, common, interpreted, apparent, explicit, explained, definitive, hidden, problematic, concise, ambiguous, etc., all these categories also apply to the Sunnah. Similarly, command, prohibition, etc., also exist in the Sunnah as in the Book of Allah, because the Sunnah, like the Book of Allah, is proof and evidence. Therefore, the Book of Allah is the origin in explaining these categories with their rulings, and the Sunnah is its branch. So there is no need to explain these categories separately; they are analogized from the Book of Allah. However, in the manner of transmission (ittisal), the Sunnah is distinct from the Book of Allah, because there is one defined path for the Book of Allah reaching us, namely tawatur, whereas the Sunnah of the Messenger has many paths, not only tawatur. This chapter (bab) is specifically established to explain these paths. In summary, in this chapter only those matters specific to the Sunnah and not found in the Book of Allah will be discussed: (1) the description of connectedness (kayfiyyat al-ittisal), (2) the description of disconnection (inqita'), (3) the description of the subject of the report (mahall al-khabar), (4) the description of the report itself (nafs al-khabar), etc.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is an introductory definition (ta'rīf) of Sunnah as a source of law in usul al-fiqh. The commentator clarifies that the term 'Sunnah' here does not refer to recommended acts (sunnah in fiqh) but to the prophetic revelation alongside the Quran: the Prophet's words, actions, and tacit approvals. The author distinguishes Sunnah from hadith: hadith is only the Prophet's speech, while Sunnah includes speech, action, and approval, and even the sayings and doings of the Companions when traced back to the Prophet. The commentary then explains that all Quranic textual categories (general, specific, apparent, etc.) apply equally to Sunnah, so they need not be repeated. The only difference lies in transmission: the Quran is only mutawatir, while Sunnah has multiple transmission types (mutawatir, ahad, etc.). This chapter will focus on transmission issues unique to Sunnah: connectedness, disconnection, the subject of the report, and the report itself.

Key Terms
السنة (al-Sunnah): In usul, the Prophet's words, actions, and tacit approvals, and by extension the sayings and actions of the Companions, as a source of law beyond the Quran.
الحديث (al-Hadith): Specifically the Prophet's statements, as distinct from Sunnah which includes actions and approvals.
التقرير (al-Taqrir): The Prophet's silent approval of an action or statement witnessed by him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The Prophet's statements
B) The Prophet's actions
C) The Prophet's tacit approvals
D) The Quran

Key Takeaway
Sunnah in Hanafi usul includes the Prophet's words, actions, and tacit approvals, and its textual categories mirror those of the Quran.

Mursal and Musnad: Classification and Acceptability in Hanafi Usul
Classifying transmitted reports as mursal or musnad with subcategories and acceptance rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four subtypes of mursal hadith, explain why the Hanafi school accepts mursal as a proof, and contrast this with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The mursal narrator's certainty makes his report superior to a single-chained musnad in Hanafi usul.

This passage introduces two key categories of transmitted reports (sunnah): mursal (where an intermediary is omitted) and musnad (fully chained). We will define their subtypes, examine the Hanafi rule that mursal is acceptable as a proof without external corroboration, and understand why the Shafi'i school disagrees. The discussion will sharpen your ability to evaluate the evidentiary weight of hadith transmissions in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Define the two core terms: Mursal and Musnad
Identify the basic meaning of mursal (omission of an intermediary) and musnad (complete chain). Note that in Hanafi usul, mursal includes what muhaddithun call munqati' and mu'dal.
The author equates the terminology of fuqaha' and usuliyun.
2
List the four subtypes of Mursal
From the passage, identify: (1) Mursal of a Companion, (2) Mursal of a Tabi'i, (3) Mursal of a Taba' al-Tabi'i, (4) Mursal from one aspect but not another. Understand each definition.
The fourth type is not discussed by the author of al-Husami.
3
Analyze the acceptance of Mursal by school
Note that the mursal of a Companion is accepted by consensus. For mursal of a Tabi'i and Taba' al-Tabi'i, the Hanafi (and Maliki/Hanbali) school accepts them; the Shafi'i/Zahiri school does not unless supported by external proof.
The key difference hinges on the narrator's certainty.
4
Understand the Hanafi reasoning (talil)
The Hanafi argument: the mursal narrator omits the chain out of certainty; if he had doubt, he would have mentioned it. This certainty makes the report trustworthy.
This is a logical inference based on the narrator's behavior.
5
Apply the rule: Mursal vs. Musnad in conflict
The passage states that mursal is superior in degree to a single-chain musnad. Hence, in conflict, mursal is given preference. The proof is the same: the mursal's greater certainty.
This applies only to musnad wahid, not mashhur or mutawatir.

السنة نوعان : - مصنف، اللہ کہتے ہیں کہ سنت کی دو قسمیں ہیں، (۱) مرسل (۲) مسند۔ مرسل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں تابعی اپنے اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے درمیان واسطہ چھوڑ دے اور یوں کہے ”قال رسول الله صلى الله علیه وسلم كذا سنت مرسل کی چار قسمیں ہیں، (۱) مرسل صحابی (۲) مرسل تابعی (۳) مرسل تبع تابعی (۴) مرسل من وجه دون وجه

مرسل صحابی اس وقت ہوتی ہے جب صحابی نے وہ حدیث رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے براہ راست نہ سنی ہو، بلکہ کسی صحابی سے سنی ہو، اور روایت کرتے وقت صحابی کا نام ترک کر دے۔

مرسل تابعی وہ ہے جس میں تابعی اپنے اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے درمیان صحابی کا واسطہ چھوڑ کر کہے قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كذا

مرسل تبع تابعی جس میں راوی تابعی اور صحابی کا واسطہ ترک کر دے اور کہے قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كذا

مرسل من وجہ دون وجہ یہ ہے کہ سنت ایک جہت سے مسند ہو اور دوسری جہت سے مرسل ہو یعنی ایک راوی نے ارسال کیا ہو، اور دوسرے راوی نے اتصال کیا ہو، یا ایک راوی نے ایک مرتبہ اسناد کیا ہو اور ایک مرتبہ ارسال کیا ہو، مصنف نے اس چوتھی قسم کا ذکر نہیں کیا ہے اگر شروع سے آخر تک تمام واسطوں کو ذکر کیا گیا ہو تو یہ حدیث مسند ہے، اور محدثین کی اصطلاح میں مرسل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں تابعی صحابی کا واسطہ چھوڑ دے، پھر اس مرسل کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) منقطع (۲) معضل ، اگر راوی نے دو راویوں کے درمیان کے کسی واسطہ کو ترک کرد یا مثلاً جو شخص ابوہریرہ کا معاصر نہیں ہے وہ کہے قال ابو هریرة جسے تو اس کو حدیث منقطع کہا جاتا ہے، اور اگر ایک سے زائد راویوں کو ترک کیا ہے تو اس کو حدیث معضل کہتے ہیں، مگر اصولیین کے نزدیک یہ تمام احادیث مرسل کہی جائیں گی یہاں فقہاء اور اصولیین کی اصطلاح مراد ہے، نہ کہ محدثین کی۔ فالمرسل من الصحابي : - مرسل کی پہلی قسم یعنی مرسل صحابی سماع پر محمول ہے، یعنی یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ صحابی نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے حدیث کو سنا ہے، اور بالا جماع مرسل صحابی مقبول ہے۔ اور دوسری اور تیسری قسم یعنی مرسل تابعی اور تبع تابعی بھی ہمارے نزدیک اور امام مالک ، امام احمد ابن حنبل وغیرہ کے نزدیک مقبول ہے، کیونکہ ارسال کرنے والے پر حدیث کے ثبوت کا معاملہ واضح ہو گیا ہے یعنی یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ مرسل کو اس کے حدیث ہونے میں کوئی شبہ نہیں ہے، اس کو یقین ہے اسی لئے اس نے اپنے سے اوپر کے راوی کو ترک کر دیا ہے، اگر اس کو ثبوت حدیث میں شبہ ہوتا تو راوی کو ترک نہ کرتا ، لہذا یہ دونوں بھی مقبول ہیں البتہ امام شافعی اور اصحاب ظواہر کے نزدیک یہ دونوں مقبول نہیں ہیں ، ہاں اگر کسی حجت قطعیہ یا قیاس صحیح سے اس کی تائید ہو جائے یا مرسل کو امت کی طرف سے قبولیت عام حاصل ہو ، یا مرسل کی حالت سے یہ بات معلوم ہو کہ وہ صرف ثقہ لوگوں سے روایت کرتا ہے تو قبول ہے ورنہ نہیں۔

مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ یہ حدیث مرسل درجہ میں مسند سے بڑھ کر ہے، یہاں مسند سے مراد مسندِ واحد ہے ،مسندِ مشہور یا مسند متواتر مراد نہیں ہے، لہذا مرسل و مسند میں تعارض کے وقت مرسل کو تر جیح ہوگی ، اور مرسل کے فائق ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرسل کو اس کے حدیث ہونے میں پورا وثوق و اعتماد ہے اسی لئے وہ اپنے اوپر کے راوی کا ذکر چھوڑ
Sunnah is of two types: (1) Mursal (2) Musnad. Mursal is that hadith in which a tabi'i drops the intermediary between himself and the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and says 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said such and such.' Mursal Sunnah has four types: (1) Mursal of a Companion, (2) Mursal of a Tabi'i, (3) Mursal of a Taba' al-Tabi'i, (4) Mursal from one aspect but not from another.

Mursal of a Companion is when a Companion did not hear that hadith directly from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, but heard it from another Companion, and when narrating, drops the name of that Companion.

Mursal of a Tabi'i is when a Tabi'i drops the intermediary of the Companion between himself and the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and says 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said such and such.'

Mursal of a Taba' al-Tabi'i is when a narrator drops the intermediary of both the Tabi'i and the Companion and says 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said such and such.'

Mursal from one aspect but not from another is when a Sunnah is musnad from one direction and mursal from another direction, i.e., one narrator made it mursal and another narrator made it connected, or one narrator at one time made it musnad and at another time mursal. The author did not mention this fourth type. If all intermediaries are mentioned from beginning to end, that hadith is musnad. In the terminology of the muhaddithun, mursal is that hadith in which a Tabi'i drops the intermediary of the Companion. Then this mursal has two types: (1) Munqati', (2) Mu'dal. If a narrator drops any intermediary between two narrators, e.g., someone who is not a contemporary of Abu Hurayrah says 'Abu Hurayrah said', that is called munqati'. If more than one narrator are dropped, that is called mu'dal. However, according to the usuliyun, all these hadiths will be called mursal. Here the terminology of the fuqaha' and usuliyun is intended, not that of the muhaddithun.

So the mursal of the Companion: The first type, i.e., the mursal of a Companion, is considered as heard (sama') – i.e., it will be understood that the Companion heard the hadith from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and by consensus the mursal of a Companion is acceptable.

And the second and third types, i.e., mursal of a Tabi'i and Taba' al-Tabi'i, are acceptable according to us (Hanafis) and according to Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, etc., because the matter of the hadith's authenticity has become clear to the one who sends it mursal – i.e., it will be understood that the mursal has no doubt about it being a hadith; he is certain. That is why he dropped the narrator above him. If he had doubt about the authenticity of the hadith, he would not have dropped the narrator. Therefore, both of these are acceptable. However, according to Imam al-Shafi'i and the Zahiris, these two are not acceptable. Yes, if it is supported by a definitive proof (hujjah qat'iyyah) or a valid analogy (qiyas sahih), or if the mursal has received general acceptance by the Ummah, or if it is known from the condition of the one who sends it mursal that he only narrates from trustworthy people, then it is acceptable; otherwise not.

The author says that this mursal hadith is superior in degree to musnad. Here 'musnad' refers to musnad wahid (single-chain musnad), not musnad mashhur or musnad mutawatir. Therefore, when there is conflict between a mursal and a musnad, the mursal will be given preference. The proof of mursal's superiority is that the one who sends it mursal has full confidence and trust in its being a hadith; that is why he omitted mentioning the narrator above him.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage explains the classification of transmitted reports (sunnah) into mursal (loose-ended) and musnad (fully chained). The commentator defines mursal broadly to include any report where a narrator omits one or more intermediaries, and lists four subtypes: mursal of a Companion (a Companion omitting another Companion), mursal of a Tabi'i (a Tabi'i omitting the Companion), mursal of a Taba' al-Tabi'i (a later narrator omitting both), and mursal from one aspect but not another (where the report has both a connected and disconnected chain). The commentator notes that the author of al-Husami did not mention the fourth subtype. He clarifies that in usul al-fiqh, the term mursal includes what muhaddithun call munqati' and mu'dal; but the discussion here uses the terminology of fuqaha' and usuliyun.

The passage then addresses the acceptability of mursal reports. The mursal of a Companion is accepted by consensus, as it is assumed the Companion heard it from the Prophet. For mursal of a Tabi'i and Taba' al-Tabi'i, the Hanafi school (and Maliki, Hanbali schools) accept them as valid proofs. Their reasoning: the narrator who sends it mursal is so confident in its authenticity that he does not bother to mention the chain. If he had any doubt, he would have mentioned it. In contrast, the Shafi'i school and the Zahiris generally reject such mursal unless supported by an external proof (like a definitive text or valid analogy), general acceptance by the Ummah, or the known reliability of the narrator's sources.

Finally, the commentator states that, in the Hanafi view, a mursal report is superior in degree to a musnad report (specifically a single-chain musnad, not a well-known or mutawatir one). Therefore, in case of conflict, the mursal should be preponderated (tarjih) over the musnad. The reasoning: the mursal narrator's confidence in the report is so strong that he omitted the chain, indicating a higher degree of certainty.

Key Terms
المرسل (al-Mursal): A report in which a narrator (Tabi'i or later) omits the intermediary between himself and the Prophet, or between narrators, according to usul terminology.
المسند (al-Musnad): A report with a complete chain of narrators from beginning to end.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the mursal of a Tabi'i considered acceptable in the Hanafi school?
A) Because the Prophet himself approved such reports
B) Because the narrator's omission of the chain shows his certainty in the report's authenticity
C) Because it is supported by a consensus of all scholars
D) Because it is equal to a mutawatir report

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a mursal report (by a reliable narrator) is not only accepted as proof but is deemed superior to a single-chain musnad due to the narrator's implicit certainty.

Mursal Hadith in Hanafi Usul
Defines mursal hadith and subtypes according to Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi definition of mursal hadith, distinguish its three types (tabi'i, taba' tabi'i, min wajh duna wajh), and differentiate Hanafi usul terminology from muhaddithin terminology.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, mursal includes any omission of a link, regardless of how many links are dropped.

This lesson defines mursal hadith as used by Hanafi usuliyyin. Unlike the narrow definition of muhaddithin, where mursal is only when a Tabi'i drops the Sahaba, Hanafi usul broadens the term to include munqati' (one link dropped) and mu'dal (multiple links dropped). Understanding this difference is crucial for evaluating hadith evidence in Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
Read the first two sentences: 'Mursal of a Tabi'i is that in which the Tabi'i drops the intermediary of the Companion ... Mursal of a Taba' Tabi'i is that in which the narrator drops the intermediary of the Tabi'i and the Companion.' Note that the key is any omission of a link between the narrator and the Prophet.
The omission can be of one or more links.
2
Recognize the three types
The passage mentions three types: (1) mursal tabi'i, (2) mursal taba' tabi'i, and (3) mursal min wajh duna wajh (from one path but not another). The fourth type is noted as not mentioned.
The third type refers to a hadith that is musnad via one chain and mursal via another.
3
Differentiate from muhaddithin terminology
In muhaddithin terminology, mursal is only when a Tabi'i drops the Sahaba. They further divide omissions into munqati' (one link dropped) and mu'dal (multiple links dropped). However, Hanafi usul treats all these as mursal.
This is a key difference: Hanafis use a broader category.
4
Understand the implication
Because Hanafis classify any omission as mursal, they evaluate such hadith based on the trustworthiness of the omitted narrators and other criteria, rather than rejecting them outright.
This affects how hadith are used as evidence in deriving rulings.

Source Text

مرسل تابعی وہ ہے جس میں تابعی اپنے اور رسول اللہ صلی ہی ایم کے درمیان صحابی کا واسطہ چھوڑ کر کہے قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كذا مرسل تبع تابعی جس میں راوی تابعی اور صحابی کا واسطہ ترک کر دے اور کہے قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كذا مرسل من وجہ دون وجہ یہ ہے کہ سنت ایک جہت سے مسند ہو اور دوسری جہت سے مرسل ہو یعنی ایک راوی نے ارسال کیا ہو، اور دوسرے راوی نے اتصال کیا ہو، یا ایک راوی نے ایک مرتبہ اسناد کیا ہو اور ایک مرتبہ ارسال کیا ہو، مصنف نے اس چوتھی قسم کا ذکر نہیں کیا ہے اگر شروع سے آخر تک تمام واسطوں کو ذکر کیا گیا ہو تو یہ حدیث مسند ہے، اور محدثین کی اصطلاح میں مرسل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں تابعی صحابی کا واسطہ چھوڑ دے، پھر اس مرسل کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) منقطع (۲) معضل ، اگر راوی نے دو راویوں کے درمیان کے کسی واسطہ کو ترک کرد یا مثلاً جو شخص ابوہریرہ کا معاصر نہیں ہے وہ کہے قال ابو هریرة جسے تو اس کو حدیث منقطع کہا جاتا ہے، اور اگر ایک سے زائد راویوں کو ترک کیا ہے تو اس کو حدیث معضل کہتے ہیں، مگر اصولیین کے نزدیک یہ تمام احادیث مرسل کہی جائیں گی یہاں فقہاء اور اصولیین کی اصطلاح مراد ہے، نہ کہ محدثین کی۔
Mursal of a Tabi'i is that in which the Tabi'i drops the intermediary of the Companion between himself and the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and says: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said such-and-such. Mursal of a Taba' Tabi'i is that in which the narrator drops the intermediary of the Tabi'i and the Companion and says: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said such-and-such. Mursal from one path but not another is that the sunnah is musnad from one aspect and mursal from another, meaning one narrator made it mursal and another narrator made it connected, or one narrator sometimes gave an isnad and sometimes made it mursal. The author did not mention this fourth type. If all intermediaries from beginning to end are mentioned, then this hadith is musnad. In the terminology of the muhaddithin, mursal is a hadith in which the Tabi'i drops the intermediary of the Companion. Then this mursal has two types: (1) munqati' (disconnected), (2) mu'dal (perplexing). If the narrator drops some intermediary between two narrators, for example, someone who is not a contemporary of Abu Hurayrah says 'Abu Hurayrah said', then it is called munqati', and if he drops more than one narrator, it is called mu'dal. However, according to the usuliyyin, all these hadiths are called mursal. Here the terminology of the fuqaha' and usuliyyin is intended, not that of the muhaddithin.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage defines the types of mursal hadith according to Hanafi usul. It first defines mursal of a Tabi'i (who drops the Sahaba), mursal of a Taba' Tabi'i (who drops both Sahaba and Tabi'i), and mursal from one path but not another (where one narrator reports it as mursal and another as musnad). The author notes that the fourth type (mursal from one aspect but not another) is not mentioned. It then clarifies that when all links are mentioned, it is musnad. In muhaddithin terminology, mursal is restricted to when a Tabi'i drops the Sahaba, and they further divide it into munqati' (one link dropped) and mu'dal (multiple links dropped). However, Hanafi usul considers all such omissions as mursal, and this is the terminology used here. The key point: Hanafi usul broadens the definition of mursal to include any omission of a link, whereas muhaddithin have narrower categories.

Key Terms
مرسل (mursal): Hadith in which a narrator (Tabi'i or later) omits the intermediary between himself and the Prophet ﷺ; Hanafi usul includes any omission of a link.
مسند (musnad): Hadith with a complete, continuous chain of narrators from beginning to end.
منقطع (munqati'): In muhaddithin terms, a hadith where one link is dropped between two narrators; in Hanafi usul, encompassed under mursal.
معضل (mu'dal): In muhaddithin terms, a hadith where two or more successive links are dropped; in Hanafi usul, also encompassed under mursal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, how many types of mursal are mentioned in the text?
A) Two: mursal tabi'i and mursal taba' tabi'i
B) Three: mursal tabi'i, mursal taba' tabi'i, and mursal min wajh duna wajh
C) Four: including mursal sahabi
D) Only one: mursal tabi'i

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, mursal is any hadith with an omitted link, regardless of how many links are dropped, unlike the narrower muhaddithin definition.

Definition of Mutawatir Hadith as a Type of Musnad
Defines mutawatir hadith with conditions and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mutawatir hadith, list its conditions, and explain why it produces certain (qat'i) knowledge.

Core Idea
A mutawatir hadith yields certain knowledge because its narrators are too numerous and trustworthy to have colluded in lying.

The Hanafi school, like other Sunni schools, classifies hadith into types based on the number and reliability of narrators. Among the highest categories is the mutawatir — a report whose transmission is so widespread that it generates certainty akin to direct observation. This lesson unpacks the definition and conditions of mutawatir hadith as presented in this classical usul text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its context
Recognize that mutawatir is a type of musnad (hadith with a complete chain). The passage defines it after discussing mursal.
Musnad has three types: mutawatir, mashhur, khabar wahid.
2
List the conditions for mutawatir
From the Arabic: narrators whose number cannot be counted, impossibility of collusion in lying due to multitude, justice, and diverse locations; continuity throughout the chain until the Prophet.
The Urdu translation notes that 'number cannot be counted' is a condition of the majority, not all.
3
Recognize examples given
Examples include the transmission of the Quran, the five daily prayers and their rak'at counts, and the amounts of zakat.
These are matters known by tawatur in practice.
4
Understand the epistemological effect
The passage states that mutawatir yields 'ilm al-yaqin (certain knowledge) equivalent to direct observation (bi-manzilat al-'iyan), as necessary knowledge ('ilman daruriyan).
This means the knowledge is immediate and cannot be denied.
5
Distinguish from other types
Note that mutawatir is the highest level; mashhur and khabar wahid yield probable (zanni) knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمُسْنَدُ  َأقْسَامُ الْمُتَوَاتِرَ وَهُوَ مَا يَرُوِيْهِ قَوْمْ لَا يُحْصى عَدَدْهُمْ وَلَا يَتَوَهَّمْ تَوَاطُوْهُمْ عَلَى الْكَذِبِ لِكَثْرَتِهِمْ وَعَدَالَتِهِمْ وَتَبَايْنِ أَمَاكِنِهِمْ وَيَدُومُ هَذَا الْحَد إِلَى أَنْ يَتَّصِلَ بِرَسُولِ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَذَلِكَ مِثْلُ نَقُلِ الْقُرْآنِ وَالصَّلَوَاتِ الْخَمْسِ وَأَعْدَادِ الرَّكْعَاتِ وَمَقَادِيرِ الزَّكوة وَمَا اَشْبَهَ ذَلِكَ وَإِنَّهُ يُوجِبْ عِلْمَ الْيَقِيْنِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْعِيَانِ عِلْمًا ضَرُوْرِيًا ۔
ترجمہ :۔ اور مسند کی چند قسمیں ہیں، متواتر ، متواتر وہ ہے جس کو اتنے لوگ روایت کریں جن کی تعداد شمار نہ ہو سکے ( یہ جمہور کے نزدیک شرط نہیں ہے ) اور ان کے جھوٹ پر متفق ہونے کا وہم نہ ہو، ان کی کثرت ، ان کی عدالت اور ان کی جگہوں کے الگ الگ ہونے کی وجہ سے ، اور یہ حد یہاں تک دائم ( برابر) رہے کہ مروی رسول اللہ صلی شیا کی تم تک پہنچ جائے ، اور یہ جیسے قران کا نقل ، پانچوں نمازوں اور ان کی رکعتوں کی تعداد، اور زکوۃ کی مقدار اور جو اس کے مشابہ ہے، اور خبر متواتر علم بدیہی کے طور پر مشاہدہ کے درجہ میں علم یقین کو واجب کرتی ہے۔ تشریح:- مصنف حدیث مرسل اور اس کے احکام سے فارغ ہو کر حدیث مسند کو بیان کر رہے ہیں، مسند کی تین قسمیں ہیں (۱) متواتر (۲) مشہور (۳) خبر واحد۔
خبر متواتر اس خبر کو کہتے ہیں جس کے روایت کرنے والے ہر زمانہ میں اتنے لوگ ہوں کہ ان کی تعداد شمار نہ کی جاسکے، اور ان کی کثرت کی وجہ سے، ان کی عدالت کی وجہ سے اور ان کے مکانوں کی دوری کی وجہ سے ان کے جھوٹ پر متفق ہونے کا وہم نہ ہو سکے۔
مسند کی تین قسمیں ہیں (۱) متواتر (۲) مشہور (۳) خبر واحد۔
متواتر اس حدیث کو کہتے ہیں جس کو روایت کرنے والے ہر دور میں اتنے لوگ ہوں کہ ان کی تعداد کو شمار نہ کیا
And the musnad: its types include mutawatir. It is what a group narrates whose number cannot be counted, and it is not imagined that they could conspire to lie due to their multitude, their justice, and their places being separate. This condition continues until it reaches the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Examples include the transmission of the Quran, the five prayers and their numbers of rak'ats, and the amounts of zakat and similar things. And it necessitates certain knowledge equivalent to direct observation, as necessary knowledge. Translation: And the musnad has several types: mutawatir. Mutawatir is that which so many people narrate that their number cannot be counted (according to the majority, this is not a condition), and it is not imagined that they could agree on a lie due to their multitude, their justice, and their places being separate. And this condition continues until the narrated matter reaches the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Examples include the transmission of the Quran, the five prayers and their numbers of rak'ats, the amounts of zakat and similar things. And the mutawatir report necessitates certainty of knowledge, like direct observation, as necessary knowledge. Commentary: The author, having finished discussing mursal hadith and its rulings, now discusses musnad hadith. Musnad has three types: (1) mutawatir, (2) mashhur, (3) khabar wahid. Khabar mutawatir is that report whose narrators in every era are so many that their number cannot be counted, and due to their multitude, their justice, and the distance of their places, it cannot be imagined that they could agree on a lie. Musnad has three types: (1) mutawatir, (2) mashhur, (3) khabar wahid. Mutawatir is a hadith whose narrators in every era are so many that their number cannot be counted.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of mutawatir hadith as a type of musnad. The author provides the Arabic text followed by Urdu translation and commentary. The key elements of mutawatir are: narrators whose number cannot be counted, impossibility of collusion in lying due to large numbers, justice, and geographical dispersion, continuity of these conditions throughout the chain until the Prophet. Examples include the Quran and established sunnah practices. The effect of mutawatir is that it produces necessary (daruri) knowledge, like direct observation. The commentary clarifies that musnad has three types: mutawatir, mashhur, and khabar wahid. This is foundational usul al-hadith material important for understanding how certain types of reports are epistemologically weightier than others.

Key Terms
متواتر (mutawātir): A hadith narrated at each level by a number that cannot be counted, whose collusion in lying is inconceivable due to their numbers, justice, and geographical diversity, producing certain knowledge
مسند (musnad): A hadith with a complete chain of narrators reaching the Prophet; includes mutawatir, mashhur, and khabar wahid

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for a hadith to be considered mutawatir according to the definition in this passage?
A) The narrators must be from the first three generations.
B) The narrators must be numerous and their collusion in lying inconceivable due to their numbers, justice, and diverse locations.
C) The hadith must be transmitted by only one narrator in each generation.
D) The narration must not involve matters of worship.

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir hadith is the highest category of musnad, producing certain knowledge (ilm al-yaqin) due to overwhelming transmission that precludes collusion in lying.

The Fourth Type of Mursal Hadith and Its Acceptance
Explains the fourth type of mursal (partially musnad) and its ruling of acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fourth type of mursal (min wajh mursal min wajh musnad) and explain why it is accepted according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A hadith that is mursal in one chain and musnad in another is accepted because there is no real contradiction—the musnad is given precedence.

This lesson explores a nuanced type of hadith transmission where a narration reaches us through two different chains: one mursal (missing the Companion) and one musnad (complete chain). The commentator clarifies that such a hadith is considered acceptable by the majority of scholars, including the Hanafi school, because the mursal chain merely lacks information while the musnad provides it, so no contradiction exists. Understanding this principle helps us navigate apparent variations in hadith chains and apply the correct weight to different transmissions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two chains
Determine that one chain is mursal (the tabi'i narrates directly without mentioning the Companion) and another chain is musnad (the chain is complete to the Prophet).
This is the defining feature of the fourth type.
2
Recognize the nature of mursal and musnad
Mursal is silent about the state of the narrator (the Companion), while musnad provides that information. Silence does not equal contradiction.
This distinction is crucial for the principle.
3
Conclude there is no real contradiction
Since mursal does not deny the Companion, but merely omits him, and musnad includes him, there is no conflict between the two chains.
If there were a direct contradiction (e.g., different ruling), the hadith would be problematic.
4
Apply the principle of precedence
Give precedence to the musnad chain over the mursal, because the musnad provides complete information. Thus, the hadith is accepted.
This is the Hanafi methodology for resolving such variations.
5
Study the example
The hadith 'لا نکاح الا بولی' (No marriage without a guardian) is narrated musnad by Isra'il ibn Yunus and mursal by Shu'bah. Following the principle, it is accepted.
This example illustrates the practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدہ: - مرسل کی چوتھی قسم من وجہ مرسل من وجہ مسند، عام علماء کے نزدیک مقبول ہے، کیونکہ مرسل راوی کے حال سے ساکت ہے اور مسند راوی کے حال کو بتاتی ہے، تو ان دونوں میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے، لہذا اسناد کو ارسال پر غلبہ دیکر قبول کر لیں گے جیسے " لا نکاح الا بولی " اس کو اسرائیل ابن یونس نے مسند ا روایت کیا ہے اور شعبہ نے مرسلاً بیان کیا ہے، یہ چوتھی قسم ہے جس کو مصنف نے متن میں ذکر نہیں کیا ہے۔
Benefit: The fourth type of mursal: from one aspect mursal and from another aspect musnad. It is accepted according to the majority of scholars, because mursal is silent about the state of the narrator, while musnad informs about the narrator's state, so there is no contradiction between these two. Therefore, we give precedence to the aspect of isnaad over irsal and accept it, like the hadith 'There is no marriage without a guardian' which Isra'il ibn Yunus narrated as musnad and Shu'bah narrated as mursal. This is the fourth type which the author did not mention in the text.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage discusses a particular type of hadith transmission. The commentator explains that there is a fourth type of mursal hadith that was not mentioned in the original matn. This type is narrated as mursal by one chain and as musnad by another. Since there is no real contradiction—mursal merely lacks information about the narrator, while musnad provides it—the narration is accepted by giving preference to the musnad version. The example given is the hadith about marriage requiring a guardian. This shows the Hanafi methodology of weighing different chains of transmission.

Key Terms
مرسل (Mursal): حدیث جس کی سند میں تابعی صحابی کا نام چھوڑ دے اور براہ راست نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے روایت کرے
مسند (Musnad): حدیث جس کی سند رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم تک متصل ہو

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the fourth type of mursal (min wajh mursal min wajh musnad) accepted?
A) Because the mursal chain is stronger than the musnad.
B) Because there is no actual contradiction; the mursal is silent while the musnad provides information, so the musnad is preferred.
C) Because the majority of scholars reject mursal completely.
D) Because the author of the matn included it as acceptable.

Key Takeaway
A hadith transmitted as mursal in one chain and musnad in another is accepted by giving precedence to the musnad, as there is no real contradiction.

Definition and Conditions of Mutawatir Hadith
Defines mutawatir, lists conditions and examples, and states its epistemological status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mutawatir hadith, identify its conditions, and explain how it yields certain knowledge.

Core Idea
A mutawatir hadith is transmitted by so many narrators in every generation that collusion on falsehood is impossible, producing certain knowledge like direct observation.

This passage introduces the first and most authoritative category of musnad hadith: mutawatir. Understanding its definition and conditions is essential for any student of usul al-fiqh because mutawatir reports provide the foundation of certain knowledge in Islamic law. We will dissect the text to see the precise conditions and the epistemological weight of such reports.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition of mutawatir
Read the first part of the text carefully. Identify the key phrase: 'what a group narrates whose number cannot be counted, and there is no suspicion of them conspiring upon falsehood due to their large number, their uprightness, and their different locations.' This is the core definition.
Note that the definition includes both quantitative and qualitative conditions.
2
List the conditions mentioned
From the definition, pick out the conditions: (1) large number (uncountable), (2) uprightness ('adalah) of narrators, (3) different locations (tabayun al-amakin), (4) continuity of these conditions from the first generation until the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The text adds that these conditions must persist throughout the chain.
3
Understand the ikhtilaf on fixed number
The commentary notes that the majority of scholars do not fix a specific number. Some require 5, 7, 12, 40, or 70. The correct view is that the number must be such that it generates certain knowledge without recourse to reasoning.
This is a key point: the condition is the result (certainty), not an arbitrary number.
4
Recognize examples and scope
The text gives examples: transmission of the Quran, the five daily prayers, numbers of rak'ahs, amounts of zakat, etc. These are matters of common knowledge among Muslims. Note that some scholars deny the existence of mutawatir among the Prophet's sayings (hadith), accepting only mutawatir of actions.
This distinction is important for later debates on the authority of hadith.
5
Grasp the epistemological outcome
The passage concludes that mutawatir yields 'ilm al-yaqin (certain knowledge) that is daruri (necessary, immediate) like direct observation. No reasoning or reflection is needed; the mind accepts it necessarily.
This places mutawatir at the highest level of certainty in Islamic epistemology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وَيَدُومُ هَذَا الْحَد إِلَى أَنْ يَتَّصِلَ بِرَسُولِ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَذَلِكَ مِثْلُ نَقُلِ الْقُرْآنِ وَالصَّلَوَاتِ الْخَمْسِ وَأَعْدَادِ الرَّكْعَاتِ وَمَقَادِيرِ الزَّكوة وَمَا اَشْبَهَ ذَلِكَ وَإِنَّهُ يُوجِبْ عِلْمَ الْيَقِيْنِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْعِيَانِ عِلْمًا ضَرُوْرِيًا ۔ ترجمہ :۔ اور مسند کی چند قسمیں ہیں، متواتر ، متواتر وہ ہے جس کو اتنے لوگ روایت کریں جن کی تعداد شمار نہ ہو سکے ( یہ جمہور کے نزدیک شرط نہیں ہے ) اور ان کے جھوٹ پر متفق ہونے کا وہم نہ ہو، ان کی کثرت ، ان کی عدالت اور ان کی جگہوں کے الگ الگ ہونے کی وجہ سے ، اور یہ حد یہاں تک دائم ( برابر) رہے کہ مروی رسول اللہ صلی شیا کی تم تک پہنچ جائے ، اور یہ جیسے قران کا نقل ، پانچوں نمازوں اور ان کی رکعتوں کی تعداد، اور زکوۃ کی مقدار اور جو اس کے مشابہ ہے، اور خبر متواتر علم بدیہی کے طور پر مشاہدہ کے درجہ میں کے روایت کرنے والے ہر زمانہ میں اتنے لوگ ہوں کہ ان کی تعداد شمار نہ کی جاسکے، اور ان کی کثرت کی وجہ سے، ان کی عدالت کی وجہ سے اور ان کے مکانوں کی دوری کی وجہ سے ان کے جھوٹ پر متفق ہونے کا وہم نہ ہو سکے۔ مسند کی تین قسمیں ہیں (۱) متواتر (۲) مشہور (۳) خبر واحد۔ متواتر اس حدیث کو کہتے ہیں جس کو روایت کرنے والے ہر دور میں اتنے لوگ ہوں کہ ان کی تعداد کو شمار نہ کیا جا سکے اور پھر ان کی کثرت وجہ سے اور عدالت کی وجہ سے اور ان کے مکانوں کی دوری کی وجہ سے ان سب کے جھوٹ پر متفق ہونے کو عقل جائز نہ قرار دے جمہور کے نزدیک ان رواۃ کی کوئی تعداد متعین نہیں اور نہ عدم احصار شرط ہے ، بعض لوگ تواتر میں عدد کی شرط لگاتے ہیں، عدد کے بارے میں مختلف اقوال ہیں، بعض نے پانچ راوی ہونے کی شرط لگائی یعنی قرن اول سے آخری ناقل تک ہر دور میں پانچ راوی کم از کم ہوں تو اس کو متواتر کہتے ہیں ، بعض نے سات کی بعض نے بارہ کی بعض نے ہیں کی ، بعض نے چالیس کی بعض نے ستر کی شرط لگائی ، ہر ایک کے پاس پنے اپنے دلائل ہیں، مگر صحیح بات یہی ہے کہ متواتر کے لئے عدد شرط نہیں بلکہ ہر دور میں اتنی تعداد ہو کہ جس سے علم یقیہ بدیہی حاصل ہو جائے۔ پھر مصنف نے عدالت اور تباین اماکن سے اشارہ کیا کہ تواتر کے لئے راویوں کا عادل ہونا اور ان کے مکانوں کی دوری شرط ہے، حالانکہ جمہور کے نزدیک یہ شرط نہیں ہے، البتہ یہ شرط ہے کہ راویوں کی یہ حد رسول اللہ سال لیا کہ تم تیک پہنچی ہوئی ہو جتی کہ یہ تعداد دور صحابہ میں بھی ختم ہوگئی تو اس خبر کو مشہور کہیں گے، متواتر نہ کہیں گے متواتر کی مثال جیسے قران کی نقل ، پانچ نمازیں، رکعات کی تعداد، زکوۃ کی مقدار میں اور نصاب زکوۃ، حج ، اور روزہ وغیرہ، مگر یہ مطلق متواتر کی مثال ہے نہ کہ متواتر السنہ کی، کیونکہ حدیث متواتر اور سنت متواتر کے وجود میں اختلاف ہے، بعض حضرات کا خیال ہے کہ متواتر السنہ کا وجود ہی نہیں ہے، بعض نے انما الاعمال بالنیات اور البینة على المدعى واليمين على من انکر کو متواتر مانا ہے۔ وانه يوجب علم الیقین : خبر متواتر کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اس سے علم یقینی بدیہی حاصل ہوتا ہے جیسے کسی چیز کے مشاہدہ سے علم بدیہی حاصل ہوتا ہے، اس میں عقل اور کسب و نظر کا دخل نہیں ہوتا ہے،
And Musnad [has] types: Mutawatir, and it is what a group narrates whose number cannot be counted, and there is no suspicion of them conspiring upon falsehood due to their large number, their uprightness, and their different locations, and this condition continues until it reaches the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). That is like the transmission of the Quran, the five prayers, the numbers of rak'ahs, the amounts of Zakat, and similar things. And it necessitates certain knowledge in the manner of direct observation, as necessary knowledge. Translation: And Musnad has several types: Mutawatir. Mutawatir is that which is narrated by so many people that their count cannot be taken (this is not a condition according to the majority) and there is no suspicion of them agreeing upon falsehood, due to their large number, their uprightness, and the separation of their places. And this condition continues until the narrated [hadith] reaches the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). This is like the transmission of the Quran, the five prayers, the numbers of rak'ahs, the amounts of Zakat, and similar things. And the mutawatir report makes necessary certain knowledge as necessary knowledge in the level of observation. Commentary: The author, after finishing the discussion of mursal hadith and its rulings, is now discussing musnad hadith. Musnad has three types: (1) Mutawatir, (2) Mashhur, (3) Khabar Wahid. Mutawatir is that report the narrators of which in every age are so many that their number cannot be counted, and due to their large number, their uprightness, and the distance of their locations, one cannot suspect that they have conspired upon falsehood. The majority of scholars do not fix a specific number nor is the condition of uncountability a requirement. Some people do set conditions for number; there are various opinions: some require five narrators in every generation, some seven, some twelve, some twenty, some forty, some seventy. Each has its own proofs, but the correct view is that number is not a condition per se; rather, in every age there should be such a number that yields necessary certain knowledge. Then the author indicated by 'uprightness' and 'different locations' that for tawatur it is necessary that the narrators be upright and their locations separate, whereas the majority hold that these are not conditions. However, it is a condition that this chain of narrators reaches the Messenger of Allah; if the count ends in the generation of the Companions, then that report is called 'mashhur', not mutawatir. Examples of mutawatir: transmission of the Quran, the five prayers, the numbers of rak'ahs, the amounts of Zakat, and Nisab of Zakat, Hajj, fasting, etc. However, these are examples of absolute mutawatir, not of mutawatir sunnah, because there is disagreement about the existence of mutawatir sunnah. Some scholars hold that there is no mutawatir sunnah at all; some have accepted 'Innama al-a'malu bil niyyat' and 'Al-bayyinatu 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yaminu 'ala man ankara' as mutawatir. And it necessitates certain knowledge: The ruling of mutawatir report is that it produces necessary certain knowledge just as direct observation produces necessary knowledge; reason and acquisition/reflection have no part in it.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage defines mutawatir hadith and its conditions. The matn states that mutawatir is narrated by a group whose number is uncountable, with no possibility of collusion due to their large number, uprightness, and different locations. This condition continues from the first generation to the Prophet. Examples include the Quran, the five daily prayers, numbers of rak'ahs, Zakat amounts, and similar matters of common knowledge. The commentator explains that the majority do not require a specific number; the key is that the narration yields certain knowledge necessarily, like seeing with one's own eyes. There is a discussion about whether 'adalah and separation of locations are conditions; the author implies they are, but the majority disagrees. The commentator also clarifies the difference between mutawatir of the Quran and mutawatir of the Sunnah, noting disagreement on the latter. Finally, it is emphasized that mutawatir produces 'ilm al-yaqin daruri, which is immediate and does not require reasoning.

Key Terms
متواتر (Mutawatir): خبر جسے ہر دور میں اتنے لوگ روایت کریں کہ ان کے جھوٹ پر متفق ہونے کا وہم نہ ہو، اور یہ علم یقینی بدیہی پیدا کرے۔
علم یقینی ('Ilm al-Yaqin): یقین جو بدیہی ہو، مشاہدہ کی طرح، جس میں عقل و نظر کی ضرورت نہ ہو۔

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main condition for a hadith to be considered mutawatir according to the passage?
A) There must be at least five narrators in each generation.
B) The narrators must all be from the same location.
C) There must be such a large number of narrators in every generation that collusion on falsehood is inconceivable, and the narration produces certain knowledge.
D) The hadith must be narrated by at least forty narrators.

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir hadith is the strongest category of transmitted reports, producing certain knowledge without need for scrutiny.

The Mashhur Hadith: Definition and Authority
Defines mashhur hadith, its authority, and ruling on denier.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mashhur hadith, explain its authority as a proof (hujja) akin to mutawatir, and state the Hanafi ruling on one who denies it.

Core Idea
Mashhur is like mutawatir in authority but its denier is misguided, not a disbeliever.

In Hanafi usul, hadith are categorized by transmission strength. The mashhur holds a special station: it starts as ahad but later becomes so widely transmitted that collusion on falsehood is impossible. This lesson unpacks its definition, its binding force, and the critical nuance that while it is like mutawatir, denying it does not entail takfir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition
Find the defining characteristics: originally ahad, then spread, transmitted by a group whose collusion on falsehood is inconceivable.
The narrators are trustworthy and from the second generation onward.
2
Understand its Authority
Note that the text equates mashhur to mutawatir in authority, citing al-Jassas and 'Isa ibn Aban.
Al-Jassas even considered it a division of mutawatir.
3
Analyze the Ruling on the Denier
The denier is yudallal (misguided), not yukaffar (disbeliever). The reason is that mashhur, despite its high authority, does not reach the absolute certainty of mutawatir in all respects.
This is a key difference from mutawatir, whose denier is a disbeliever.
4
Apply to Naskh and Ziyada
Mashhur can abrogate the Quran (naskh) and add to its rulings (ziyada 'ala al-kitab) according to Hanafis. Examples: stoning penalty, wiping over leather socks, consecutive fasts.
These examples show practical implications of mashhur's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمَشْهُورُ وَهُوَمَا كَانَ مِنَ الْأَحَادِ فِى الْأَصْلِ ثُمَّ انْتَشَرَ فَصَارَ يَنْقُلُهُ قَوْمٌ لَا يُتَوَهَمْ تَوَاطُوهُمْ عَلَى الْكَذِبِ وَهُمُ الْقَرْنُ الثَّانِي وَمَنْ بَعْدَهُمْ وَأَوْلَئِكَ قَوْمٌ ثِقَاتْ أَئِمَةٌ لَا يَتَهَمُوْنَ فَصَارَ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ وَتَصْدِيقِهِمْ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْمُتَوَاتِرِ حَتَّى قَالَ الْجَصَّاصُ إِنَّهُ أَحَدٌ قِسْمَى الْمُتَوَاتِرِ وَقَالَ عِيْسَى بْنُ أَبَانَ يُضَلَّلُ جَاحِدُهُ وَلَا يُكَفَرُ وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ عِنْدَنَا لِاَنَّ الْمَشْهُورَ بِشَهَادَةِ السَّلَفِ صَارَحُجَةً لِلْعَمَلِ بِهِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْمُتَوَاتِرِ فَصَحَتِ الرِّيَادَةُ بِه عَلَى كِتَابِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَهُوَنَسْخٌ عِنْدَنَا وَذَلِكَ مِثْلُ زِيَادَةِ الرَّجُمِ وَالْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْخُفَيْنِ وَالتَّتَابِعِ فِي صِيَامٍ
And Al-Mashhur: it is that which was [originally] among the ahad [narrations] then spread, so that a group began to transmit it that one cannot suspect of collusion upon falsehood, and they are the second generation and those after them. Those are trustworthy people, leaders, not accused. Thus it became, by their testimony and verification, in the rank of mutawatir, until al-Jassas said that it is one of the two divisions of mutawatir. And 'Isa ibn Aban said: Its denier is misguided but not a disbeliever, and this is the correct view in our school, because the mashhur, through the testimony of the salaf, became a definitive proof for acting upon it akin to mutawatir. Therefore, making an addition upon the Book of Allah is valid through it, and it is abrogation according to us. That is like the addition of stoning, wiping over leather socks, and consecutive fasts.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage defines mashhur hadith. It is a hadith that was originally narrated as ahad but later gained widespread transmission such that its narrators in the later generations are so numerous that collusion on falsehood is inconceivable. These narrators are trustworthy and reliable. Because of the testimony and verification of the early generations (the salaf), it becomes like mutawatir in its authority. There is a disagreement: al-Jassas considered it a type of mutawatir, while 'Isa ibn Aban held that its denier is guilty of error (tadlil) but not disbelief (takfir). The correct Hanafi view is that the denier is misguided (yudallal) but not a disbeliever, because the mashhur is a proof (hujja) for action like mutawatir. It can even be used to make an addition to the Quran (ziyada 'ala al-kitab) and can abrogate (naskh) according to the Hanafi school. Examples include the punishment of stoning for adulterers, wiping over leather socks during wudu, and the requirement of consecutive fasts for expiation.

Key Terms
مشہور (Mashhur): جو حدیث پہلے واحد تھی پھر پھیلی اور اسے اتنے لوگ نقل کریں کہ ان کے جھوٹ پر تواطؤ کا وہم نہ ہو۔
جاحد (Jahid): انکار کرنے والا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct Hanafi ruling on the denier of a mashhur hadith?
A) He becomes a disbeliever because mashhur is like mutawatir.
B) He is considered misguided but not a disbeliever.
C) He is not considered misguided because mashhur is no different from ahad.
D) He is considered a fasiq but his belief remains intact.

Key Takeaway
Mashhur hadith is a proof (hujja) like mutawatir in authority, but its denier is only considered misguided (yudallal), not a disbeliever, and it can abrogate the Quran in the Hanafi school.

Khabar Mashhur: Definition and Evidentiary Value
Defining khabar mashhur and its evidentiary value in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar mashhur, distinguish it from mutawatir and ahad, and apply the Hanafi ruling that it is a binding proof for action but does not yield certain knowledge.

Core Idea
Khabar mashhur is like mutawatir for action but deficient for certainty.

In Hanafi usul, transmitted reports (akhbar) are classified into mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad. This lesson explains the category of khabar mashhur: its definition, how it becomes authoritative, and the scholarly disagreement about its epistemological status. Understanding this classification is essential for evaluating the strength of hadith evidence in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Find the statement in the passage that defines khabar mashhur. Note that it is originally ahad and becomes widespread in the second generation.
The definition is: 'khabar that was among the ahad in origin, then spread, transmitted by a group whose collusion on falsehood is inconceivable.'
2
Distinguish from mutawatir and ahad
Khabar mashhur starts as ahad but attains widespread transmission like mutawatir. However, it does not reach the level of mutawatir in the first generation, creating a doubt.
This doubt prevents certain knowledge (ilm al-yaqin).
3
Analyze its evidentiary value
Because the later transmitters are trustworthy, it becomes a proof (hujja) for action, but due to its ahad origin, it does not produce certainty.
It is binding for practice but not for creed.
4
Examine the internal dispute
Compare the views of al-Jassas (who considered it a type of mutawatir) and 'Isa ibn Aban (who held it is not but the denier is misguided, not a disbeliever).
The text states 'wa huwa al-sahih 'indana' for 'Isa ibn Aban's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمَشْهُورُ وَهُوَمَا كَانَ مِنَ الْأَحَادِ فِى الْأَصْلِ ثُمَّ انْتَشَرَ فَصَارَ يَنْقُلُهُ قَوْمٌ لَا يُتَوَهَمْ تَوَاطُوهُمْ عَلَى الْكَذِبِ وَهُمُ الْقَرْنُ الثَّانِي وَمَنْ بَعْدَهُمْ وَأَوْلَئِكَ قَوْمٌ ثِقَاتْ أَئِمَةٌ لَا يَتَهَمُوْنَ فَصَارَ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ وَتَصْدِيقِهِمْ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْمُتَوَاتِرِ حَتَّى قَالَ الْجَصَّاصُ إِنَّهُ أَحَدٌ قِسْمَى الْمُتَوَاتِرِ وَقَالَ عِيْسَى بْنُ أَبَانَ يُضَلَّلُ جَاحِدُهُ وَلَا يُكَفَرُ وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ عِنْدَنَا لِاَنَّ الْمَشْهُورَ بِشَهَادَةِ السَّلَفِ صَارَحُجَةً لِلْعَمَلِ بِهِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْمُتَوَاتِرِ فَصَحَتِ الرِّيَادَةُ بِه عَلَى كِتَابِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَهُوَنَسْخٌ عِنْدَنَا وَذَلِكَ مِثْلُ زِيَادَةِ الرَّجُمِ وَالْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْخُفَيْنِ وَالتَّتَابِعِ فِي صِيَامِ كَفَّارَةِ الْيَمِيْن لكِنَّهُ لَمَا كَانَ مِنَ الْأَحَادِ فِي الْاَصْلِ ثَبَتَ بِهِ شُبُهَةٌ سَقَطَ بِهَا عِلْمَ الْيَقِينِ
And Al-Mashhur: it is what was among the Ahad in origin, then spread, so that a group whose collusion upon falsehood cannot be imagined began to transmit it, and they are the second generation and those after them. And those people are trustworthy, imams, not accused of lying. So it became, due to their testimony and confirmation, like the Mutawatir, until Al-Jassas said: 'It is one of the two divisions of Mutawatir.' And 'Isa ibn Aban said: 'The denier of it is led astray and not deemed an unbeliever,' and this is the correct view in our school, because the Mashhur, through the testimony of the Salaf, became a proof for acting upon it like the Mutawatir. So an addition upon the Book of Allah Almighty is valid by it, and it is abrogation (naskh) in our view. That is like the addition of stoning (rajm), wiping over the socks (masah 'ala al-khuffayn), and consecutive fasting in the expiation of an oath. However, since it was Ahad in origin, a doubt was established by it that caused certain knowledge to fall.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage from Al-Husami defines Khabar Mashhur, which is the second type of transmitted report (after Mutawatir). The definition: it is a report that was initially khabar wahid (ahad) during the era of the Companions (first generation), but then became widespread so that in the second generation (Tabi'un) and third generation (Taba' Tabi'in) it is transmitted by such a large number that their collusion on a lie is inconceivable. These narrators are reliable imams. Because of their testimony, it attains the status of mutawatir in terms of being a proof for action. However, it does not produce certain knowledge (ilm al-yaqin) because of its ahad origin; it only produces speculative knowledge (zann) but is binding for practice. The text then discusses ikhtilaf: Imam al-Jassas considered it a type of mutawatir, while 'Isa ibn Aban held that its denier is misguided but not a disbeliever. The relied-upon Hanafi position is the latter: it is not full tawatur but of higher authority than khabar wahid. The Hanafi proofs include the fact that such reports are accepted as additions to the Qur'an (ziyada 'ala al-kitab), which are considered naskh (abrogation) in the Hanafi school. Examples: the stoning penalty for married adulterers (rajm), wiping over leather socks, and consecutive fasting in expiation of an oath. These are established by mashhur hadith even though not explicitly in the Qur'an. The authority_weight: This is from Zahir al-Riwayah as transmitted in the Hanafi usul works.

Key Terms
خبر مشہور (khabar mashhur): A report that was originally solitary (ahad) in the first generation but became widely transmitted in the second and third generations such that collusion on falsehood is inconceivable.
زیادۃ علی الکتاب (ziyada 'ala al-kitab): An addition to the Qur'anic ruling by a hadith, considered abrogation (naskh) in Hanafi usul when the hadith is mashhur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding the denier of a khabar mashhur?
A) He is declared an unbeliever.
B) He is led astray but not declared an unbeliever.
C) He is considered a sinner but still a believer.
D) He is not held accountable.

Key Takeaway
Khabar mashhur is a binding proof for action and can abrogate the Quran, but its denier is not declared a disbeliever.

Khabar Mashhur: Definition and Evidentiary Value in Hanafi Usul
Defining khabar mashhur and its evidentiary status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar mashhur, state its conditions, and explain the Hanafi dispute regarding its epistemic value and the ruling on its denier.

Core Idea
Khabar mashhur: solitary in origin, authoritative through Salaf testimony, but below mutawatir in belief.

Khabar mashhur is a unique category of report in Hanafi usul: it starts as a solitary report (khabar wahid) but later becomes widely transmitted by trustworthy narrators in the second and third generations. This passage explains its definition, the condition for its classification, and a key intra-Hanafi disagreement about whether it yields certain knowledge or merely reassurance, and whether its denier is a disbeliever or just misguided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of khabar mashhur
Extract from the text the definition: a report that was originally khabar wahid in the Companion generation but then spread in the second and third generations to the level of tawatur in terms of transmitters.
Note the condition: fame must occur specifically in the second and third generations; later fame from codification does not count.
2
Understand the basis for its elevation
The text cites the hadith 'Khayr al-qurun qarni' as evidence for the reliability of the Followers and their successors. Their unanimous transmission upgrades the report to mutawatir in terms of practice.
This is the Hanafi justification for why mashhur is not like ordinary ahad.
3
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify the two positions: (1) Imam Jassas: khabar mashhur yields theoretical certainty (yaqin nazari) and its denier is a disbeliever. (2) Isa ibn Aban: it yields reassurance (tumaninah) and its denier is misguided and sinful but not a disbeliever.
The author sides with Isa ibn Aban, distinguishing practice (amal) from belief (i'tiqad).
4
Analyze the concept of ziyadah (addition)
The text explains that khabar mashhur can add to the Quran in a way that is partly explanatory and partly abrogating (naskh). There are three types of ziyadah: (1) mere explanation (permissible by any report), (2) mere abrogation (only by mutawatir), (3) combination (by mashhur).
This resolves the apparent contradiction between saying mashhur can add to the Quran but cannot abrogate absolutely.
5
Apply the concept to examples
The text begins examples: stoning for the married adulterer (rajm), wiping over socks, consecutive fasts for oath expiation. Recognize that these are rulings established by khabar mashhur according to the Hanafi school.
The stoning example shows how mashhur adds to the Quranic verse on lashes.

Source Text
