The Four Conditions of the Narrator in Khabar Wahid: Islam, Justice, Intellect, Precision
Specifying the four conditions of the narrator and the ruling of mustawir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions required in a narrator of khabar wahid, explain the rationale for each, and apply the rulings for the mustawir narrator, including the exception for early generations.

Core Idea
A khabar wahid is binding only if its narrator is Muslim, just, fully intellective, and precise.

In the Hanafi usul system, not every report from a single narrator carries binding authority. The text you are about to read specifies four conditions that the narrator must fulfill. Understanding these conditions is essential for evaluating the reliability of hadith and for distinguishing between accepted and rejected reports. We will also examine the special case of the mustawir narrator and the differences in treatment between hadith and judicial testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions and their opposites
Read the passage and list the four conditions: Islam, justice ('adala), complete intellect ('aql kamil), and precision (dabt). For each, identify the disqualifying counterpart: kafir (disbeliever), fasiq (sinner), sabiyy (minor)/ma'tuh (feeble-minded), and one with severe negligence (ghafla).
The ma'tuh is a person whose speech is confused, neither fully sane nor insane.
2
Understand the rationale behind each condition
For each condition, determine why it is necessary. The text explains: a disbeliever is an enemy of Islam; a sinner does not care about lying; incomplete intellect impairs proper conveyance; lack of precision undermines truthfulness.
Complete intellect is attained at puberty; the condition excludes minors and the mentally deficient.
3
Analyze the ruling of the mustawir narrator
The mustawir is one whose justice is unknown. In the context of hadith, his report is not a proof (hujja) until his justice becomes apparent. However, there is an exception: narrators from the early generations (sadr awwal: Companions, Successors, and their successors) are presumed just based on the Prophet's testimony, so mustawir reports from them are accepted.
The phrase 'except in the early period' indicates this exception. The text also notes that in judicial testimony (qada'), Abu Hanifa accepts a mustawir's testimony based on the default assumption that a Muslim is just.
4
Recognize the other categories of unknowns
The text clarifies that if a narrator is mustawir in Islam, intellect, or precision (not just justice), then his report is rejected in both hadith and judicial testimony. This shows that the default assumption of Islam and intellect only applies to the condition of justice.
This distinction is important: the exception for early generations applies only to unknown justice, not to unknown Islam or intellect.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi variation on mustawir
A narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that Abu Hanifa considered the mustawir like a just person regarding reports about the impurity of water. This is a rare transmission (nawadir) and not the general position, but it shows nuanced treatment in specific fiqh matters.
This demonstrates that the Madhhab allows exceptions in certain contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهِيَ أَرْبَعَةُ الْإِسْلَامُ وَالْعَدَالَة وَالْعَقْلُ الْكَامِل وَالضَّبْطُ فَلَا يَجِبُ الْعَمَلُ بِخَيْر الْكَافِرِ وَالْفَاسِقِ وَالصَّبِى وَالْمَعْتُوهِ وَالَّذِئ اِشْتَدَّتْ غَفْلَتُهُ خِلْقَةً أَوْ مُسَامَحَةً اَوْ مُجَازَفَةً وَالْمَسْتَور كَالْفَاسِقِ لَا يَكُونُ خَبَرْهُ حَجَةً فِى بَابِ الْحَدِيثِ مَالَمْ يَظْهَرُ عَدَ اللَّهُ إِلَّا فِي الصَّدْر الْأَوَّلِ عَلَى مَانُبَين - ترجمہ: اور وہ شرطیں چار ہیں، مسلمان ہونا، عادل ہونا، عقل کامل والا ہونا، اور ضبط کا ہونا پس واجب نہ ہوگا عمل کرنا کافر، فاسق، نابالغ اور معتوہ کی خبر پر اور اس شخص کی خبر پر جس کی غفلت زیادہ ہو پیدائشی طور پر، یالا پرواہی کی جہ سے یا انکل سے بک بک کرنے سے، اور مستور الحال فاسق کی طرح ہے، اس کی خبر حجت نہ ہوگی حدیث کے باب میں، جب تک اس کی عدالت ظاہر نہ ہو جائے مگر صد ر اول میں، اس تفصیل کی بنا پر جس کو ہم بیان کریں گے۔ تشریح:- خبر واحد پر عمل کے لئے آٹھ شرطیں ہیں، چار نفس خبر میں، جس کو بیان کر چکے، دوسری چار جو مخیر سے متعلق ہیں، اس کو بیان کر رہے ہیں، پہلی شرط مخبر کا مسلمان ہونا، دوسری شرط عادل ہونا، تیسری شرط اس کا کامل عقل والا ہونا، اور چوتھی شرط اس کا ضبط والا ہونا، یعنی کما حقہ بات سننا، پھر اس کو یا درکھنا پھر اس کو بیان کرنا۔ اسلام کی شرط اس لئے لگائی کہ کافر کی خبر کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وہ اسلام کا دشمن ہوتا ہے، عدالت یعنی دین پر جماؤ کی شرط اس لئے لگائی کہ فاسق جھوٹ کی پرواہ نہیں کرتا، دین دار آدمی سچ جھوٹ میں تمیز کرتا ہے، کامل عقل ہونا جو بلوغ کے بعد ہوتا ہے، یہ شرط اس لئے لگائی کہ کم عقل یا بے عقل بات کو خصوصا دین کے معاملہ میں اچھی طرح پہنچانے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے۔ اور ضبط کی شرط اس لئے لگائی کہ بغیر محفوظ کئے خبر میں سچائی نہیں ہوسکتی۔ لہذا اسلام نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے کافر کی خبر قبول نہ ہوگی، اور عدالت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے فاسق کی خبر معتبر نہ ہوگی اور کامل العقل نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے بچہ کی اور معتوہ کی خبر بھی قابل قبول نہ ہوگی، معتوہ اس کو کہتے ہیں جو نہ پاگل ہو نہ عقلمند ہو، اس کا کلام خلط ملط ہو کبھی عقلمندوں جیسی بات کرے کبھی پاگلوں جیسی، اور ضبط نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس شخص کی خبر بھی قبول نہ ہوگی جس کی غفلت بہت بڑھ گئی ہو، اور یہ کبھی پیدائشی ہوتا ہے اور کبھی غفلت کا بڑھ جانا مسامحۂ ہوتا ہے یعنی اس کو غلطی کی پروا نہیں ہوتی جو چاہتا ہے بک دیتا ہے، اور کبھی مجازفہ ہوتا ہے یعنی انکل بے سوچے سمجھے جو منہ میں آیا بک دیتا ہے، بہر حال غفلت کے بڑھ جانے میں ضبط نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے خبر قبول نہ کیجائے گی۔ اور مستور الحال (جس کا فاسق، عادل ہونا معلوم نہ ہو) اس کی خبر حدیث کے باب میں بلاشبہ حجت نہ ہوگی، وہ فاسق کی طرح ہے، جب تک اس کی عدالت ظاہر نہ ہو جائے لیکن اگر صدر اول یعنی عہد صحابہ و تابعین اور تبع تابعین میں کوئی راوی مستور الحال ہو تو اس کی خبر حجت ہوگی کیونکہ ان تینوں طبقوں کی عدالت کی شہادت حضور صلی ہی ایم نے دی ہے، خیر القرون قرنی الخ سے۔ باب حدیث کی قید سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر باب قضا میں قاضی مستور الحال کی شہادت پر فیصلہ کر دے تو امام حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کی ظاہری حالت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے فیصلہ جائز ہوگا کیونکہ مسلمان کا ظاہری حال یہی ہے کہ وہ عادل ہوگا۔ البتہ اگر وہ راوی مستور الاسلام یا مستور اعقل یا مستور الضبط ہے تو اس کی خبر حجت نہ ہوگی، نہ باب حدیث میں، نہ باب قضاء میں۔ وَرَوَى الْحَسَنُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ أَنَّهُ مِثْلُ الْعَدْلِ فِيْمَا يُخْبِرُ عَنْ نَجَاسَةِ الْمَاءِ وَذَكَرَ
And they are four: Islam, justice, complete intellect, and precision. So it is not obligatory to act upon the report of a disbeliever, a sinner, a minor, an insane person, and one whose negligence is severe, whether by nature, carelessness, or recklessness. And the mustawir (whose state is unknown) is like a sinner; his report is not a proof in the chapter of hadith as long as his justice does not become apparent, except in the early period (sadr awwal) according to the detail we will mention. Translation: And those conditions are four: being Muslim, being just, being of complete intellect, and having precision. So it will not be obligatory to act upon the report of a disbeliever, a sinner, a minor, and an insane person, and upon the report of one whose negligence is severe, whether by nature, or due to carelessness, or due to reckless speech. And the mustawir is like a sinner; his report will not be a proof in the chapter of hadith until his justice becomes apparent, except in the early period, according to the detail we will explain. Commentary: For acting upon khabar wahid, there are eight conditions: four in the report itself, which we have already explained, and four related to the narrator, which we are now explaining. The first condition is that the narrator be Muslim, second just, third of complete intellect, and fourth having precision, i.e., hearing properly, then memorizing, then expressing. The condition of Islam is placed because the report of a disbeliever has no weight, as he is an enemy of Islam. The condition of justice (steadfastness in religion) is placed because a sinner does not care about lying; a religious person distinguishes truth from falsehood. Complete intellect, which occurs after puberty, is placed because one with weak or no intellect does not have the ability to properly convey matters, especially religious matters. The condition of precision is placed because without preservation, truth cannot be in the report. Therefore, due to lack of Islam, the report of a disbeliever will not be accepted; due to lack of justice, the report of a sinner is not credible; due to lack of complete intellect, the report of a child and the ma'tuh (one who is neither insane nor sane, his speech mixed) will not be acceptable; and due to lack of precision, the report of one whose negligence is very great will not be accepted. This negligence is sometimes innate, sometimes it is due to carelessness (he does not care about mistakes, he says whatever he wants), and sometimes it is due to recklessness (he speaks without thinking, whatever comes to his mouth). In any case, when negligence becomes excessive, the report will not be accepted due to lack of precision. As for the mustawir (one whose state of sinfulness or justice is not known), his report in the chapter of hadith is without a doubt not a proof; he is like a sinner until his justice becomes apparent. But if in the early period (sadr awwal), i.e., the era of the Companions, Successors, and Followers of the Successors, a narrator is mustawir, his report will be a proof, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) testified to the justice of these three generations in the hadith 'Khayr al-qurun qarni' etc. The restriction 'in the chapter of hadith' indicates that if a judge in the chapter of qada' (judgment) decides based on the testimony of a mustawir, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is permissible because the apparent state of a Muslim is that he is just. However, if the narrator is mustawir al-Islam (unknown Islam) or mustawir al-'aql (unknown intellect) or mustawir al-dabt (unknown precision), his report will not be a proof, neither in the chapter of hadith nor in the chapter of qada'. And Hasan (ibn Ziyad) narrated from Abu Hanifa that he (the mustawir) is like a just person in what he reports about the impurity of water, and he mentioned...
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage enumerates and explains the four conditions that must be present in the narrator of a khabar wahid. These are: (1) Islam – the report of a disbeliever is rejected because he is hostile to Islam; (2) 'Adala (justice) – a sinner (fasiq) is not reliable; (3) Complete intellect ('aql kamil) – attained at puberty; lacking intellect includes minors and the ma'tuh (one whose speech is incoherent); (4) Dabt (precision) – the ability to hear, memorize, and transmit accurately; severe negligence (due to nature, carelessness, or recklessness) invalidates the report. The text also discusses the mustawir al-hal narrator (whose justice is unknown). In the context of hadith, such a narrator is like a fasiq and his report is not accepted unless his justice becomes apparent. However, for narrators of the first three generations (Companions, Successors, and their successors), they are presumed just due to the Prophet's testimony, so the reports of mustawir narrators from those generations are accepted. In the context of qada' (judicial testimony), a mustawir's testimony is acceptable to Abu Hanifa because the default for a Muslim is justice. But if the narrator is unknown in Islam, intellect, or precision, his report is not accepted in either field. Finally, a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that Abu Hanifa considered a mustawir narrator like a just person regarding reports about the impurity of water (i.e., accepting his report in that specific fiqh matter). This is a rare transmission (nawadir) and not the general position.

Key Terms
عدالت (ʿadālah): Moral integrity and steadfastness in religious obligations, avoiding major sins and persistence in minor ones.
ضبط (ḍabṭ): Precision in hearing, memorizing, and transmitting the report without errors.
معتوہ (maʿtūh): A person who is neither insane nor of sound intellect, with confused speech.
مستور الحال (mustawir al-ḥāl): A person whose state of justice or sinfulness is unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school accept the report of a mustawir narrator from the early generations (صدر اول) in hadith?
A) Because all mustawir are considered just
B) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) testified to the justice of those generations
C) Because their reports are mutawatir
D) Because they were all Companions

Key Takeaway
A khabar wahid requires a narrator who is Muslim, just, fully intellectual, and precise; a mustawir is rejected in hadith unless from the early generations or in judicial context.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Rule: Reports of Any Mumayyiz in Non-Binding Transactions
Explains acceptance of reports in non-binding transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that in transactions free from obligation, the report of any discerning person (mumayyiz) is accepted due to general necessity, and apply it to identify which conditions are dropped.

Core Idea
Necessity relaxes conditions: in non-obligatory transactions, any mumayyiz's report suffices.

This lesson explores a core Hanafi usul principle: the admissibility of reports (khabar) depends on whether the report creates a legal obligation. In transactions like agency (wakalah), mudarabah, and permission for trade (idhn fi al-tijarah), where no obligation is imposed on the listener, the strict conditions required for testimony (shahadah) are relaxed. The report of any discerning person (mumayyiz) is accepted, regardless of justice, number, or religion. The reason is general necessity (darurah ammah), as requiring ideal reporters would cause hardship and impede everyday commerce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope
Determine which transactions are covered: those that are 'free from the meaning of obligation' (tanfakku 'an ma'na al-ilzam). Examples given: wakalah, mudarabah, idhn fi al-tijarah.
These are non-binding; the listener has an option to accept or reject the report.
2
State the ruling
For such transactions, the report of every mumayyiz is accepted (yu'tabaru khabaru kulli mumayyiz). The mumayyiz is a person who has reached the age of discernment and can understand speech and intent.
This includes children, non-Muslims, and those not necessarily just (adil).
3
Understand the first proof: general necessity
The text cites a general necessity (darurah ammah) that necessitates dropping all conditions. Why? People rarely find reporters who combine all strict conditions, and the listener has no other evidence to act upon besides this report. Imposing conditions would render many transactions inoperative (ta'til).
This is a common-sense reasoning: if only two just witnesses were accepted, most agencies would fail due to lack of available reporters.
4
Understand the second proof: teleological
The strict conditions (number, justice) are meant to ensure truthfulness so that the report becomes binding (mulzim). In non-binding transactions, no such binding effect occurs; therefore, the strict conditions are unnecessary. The purpose is absent, so the conditions are dropped.
This is a 'mafhum al-'illah' reasoning: the condition follows the purpose; when the purpose is absent, the condition is not required.
5
Contrast with binding reports
In reports that create obligation (e.g., establishing a debt or a crime), the strict conditions (two just witnesses) are required. These are called 'umur al-din' (matters of religion) or pure obligation transactions.
This contrast highlights the flexibility of Hanafi usul: the same type of evidence (khabar) is treated differently based on its legal effect.

ہونے کی ، اور یہ (اعتبار شرائط) اس خبر میں ہے جس کے ساتھ لزوم متعلق ہوتا ہے تو ہم نے ان شرائط کی شرط لگادی امور دین میں ، نہ کہ ان معاملات میں جن کے ساتھ لزوم متعلق نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح : - معاملات تین طرح کے ہیں، (۱) ایک وہ جن میں الزام محض ہوتا ہے، یعنی کسی پر کسی حق کو ثابت کرنے کی خبر دینا جیسے یہ خبر دینا کہ فلاں کا فلاں پر دین ہے، یا فلاں نے چوری کی ہے ، اس قسم کی خبر میں عدد اور عدالت دونوں ضروری ہیں ، یعنی دو گواہ ہوں اور عادل ہوں، (۲) وہ معاملات جن میں من وجہ الزام ہوتا ہے جیسے وکیل کو معزول کرنے کی یا غلام کو تجارت سے روکنے کی خبر دینا تو ان میں من وجہ الزام ہے، اور من وجہ نہیں ہے، اس اعتبار سے تو الزام علی الغیر نہیں ہے کہ مؤکل نے وکیل کو معزول کر کے اور مولی نے عبد ماذون پر حجر کر کے اپنے حق میں تصرف کیا ہے، نہ کہ غیر کے حق میں ،مگر اس اعتبار سے الزام علی الغیر ہے، کہ اب وکیل اور عبد ماذون عزل وحجر کے بعد جو تصرف کریں گے، اس کے ذمہ دار یہ خود ہوں گے، مثلاً بیع کی تو اس کے ثمن کے اور نفع و نقصان کے یہ خود ذمہ دار ہوں گے، اس لحاظ سے الزام علی الغیر ہے، اسی وجہ سے ان میں الزام اور عدم الزام دونوں جہتیں ہیں تو شہادت کی دو شرطوں یعنی عدد یا عدالت میں سے ایک کا ہونا ضروری ہے، یا تو دو گواہ ہوں یا ایک ہو تو عادل ہو،(۳) تیسرے وہ معاملات جن میں الزام کے معنی بالکل نہیں ہوتے جیسے وکالت کسی نے کسی سے کہا کہ فلاں نے تجھے وکیل بنایا ہے اور مضاربت ، جیسے کسی نے کسی کہا کہ فلاں نے تجھے مضارب بنایا ہے اور اذن فی التجارۃ مثلا کسی نے غلام سے کہا کہ تجھے تیرے آقا نے تجارت کی اجازت دی ہے تو اس خبر سے مخاطب پر کوئی چیز لازم نہیں ہوتی ہے، کیوں کہ مخاطب کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اس خبر کو قبول کرے یا نہ کرے اس تیسری قسم کے معاملات میں ہر تمیز وشعور رکھنے والے کی خبر معتبر ہوگی ، چاہے وہ عادل ہو یا نہ ہو، بچہ ہو یا بالغ ، مسلمان ہو یا کافر سب کی خبر قبول کی جائیگی ، اس کی دو دلیلیں ہیں۔ پہلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس میں ضرورت عام ہے جو تمام شرائط کے ساقط ہونے کا تقاضا کرتی ہے کیوں کہ آدمی کو عام طور پر ضرورت پڑتی ہے کہ وکالت یا مضاربت یا اذن فی التجارة کی خبر لے کر کسی کو بھیجے ، اب اگر اس میں وہ شرائط لگائی جائیں گی تو لوگ حرج میں پڑینگے، کیوں کہ بروقت ایسا آدمی ملنا مشکل ہے جو تمام شرائط کا جامع ہو، اور جس کے پاس خبر پہنچی ہے اس کے پاس بھی عمل کے لئے اس خبر کے علاوہ کوئی دلیل بھی نہیں ہے، اگر یہ شرطیں لگائی جائیں گی تو بہت سارے کام معطل جائینگے ، لہذا عمومی ضرورت کی وجہ سے ہر عقل وشعور رکھنے والے کی خبر مانی جائے گی۔ دوسری دلیل ہے کہ خبر دینے والے میں مذکورہ شرائط کا اعتبار صرف اس لئے کیا گیا ہے تا کہ خبر میں سچائی کی جہت راحج ہو اور خبر ملزم بنے یعنی سامع پر ایک چیز لازم کرے، لہذا جن خبروں میں لزوم ہوتا ہے جیسے امور
And in transactions that are free from the meaning of obligation, such as agencies, mudarabahs, and permission for trade, the report of every discerning person is considered due to the generality of necessity which necessitates the falling away of all conditions. For a person rarely finds one who combines those conditions to send to his agent or slave, and the listener has no proof to act upon except this report. And because the consideration of these conditions is so that the aspect of truth may prevail in the report and it becomes binding. That is in what obligation pertains to, so we stipulated these conditions in matters of religion, not in those transactions to which obligation does not pertain. Translation: And in those transactions that are separate from the meaning of obligation, such as agencies, mudarabahs, and permission for trade, the report of every discerning person is acceptable, due to the generality of necessity which requires the dropping of all conditions, because a person rarely finds a person who combines those conditions to send to his agent or slave, and the listener has no proof to act upon except this report. And because the consideration of these conditions is so that the aspect of truth may become predominant in the report and it becomes binding. And this (consideration of conditions) is in the report to which obligation pertains, so we stipulated these conditions in matters of religion, not in those transactions in which obligation does not pertain. Elucidation: Transactions are of three types: (1) Those in which pure obligation occurs, i.e., informing to establish a right on someone, e.g., informing that Zaid owes a debt to someone, or that so-and-so committed theft. In this type, both number and justice are necessary, i.e., two witnesses and they must be just. (2) Those transactions in which obligation exists from one aspect, e.g., informing about the dismissal of a wakil or restraining a slave from trade. In these, obligation from one aspect and not from another. From this perspective, there is no obligation on others because the principal dismissed the agent and the master placed restriction on the authorized slave, acting in his own right, not in the right of others. But from that perspective, there is obligation on others, because now the agent and the authorized slave, after dismissal and restriction, whatever dispositions they make, they themselves will be responsible. For example, if they sell, they will be responsible for the price and profit/loss. From this aspect, there is obligation on others. Therefore, in these, both aspects of obligation and non-obligation exist. So it is necessary to have one of the two conditions of testimony: either two witnesses or one who is just. (3) Those transactions in which the meaning of obligation is completely absent, e.g., agency: someone says to another, 'So-and-so has appointed you as agent,' or mudarabah: someone says, 'So-and-so has made you an investor,' or permission for trade: e.g., someone says to a slave, 'Your master has permitted you for trade.' This report does not impose anything on the addressee, because the addressee has the option to accept or reject the report. In this third type of transaction, the report of every person of discernment and intelligence is acceptable, whether they are just or not, child or adult, Muslim or disbeliever. There are two proofs for this. The first proof is that there is general necessity which requires the dropping of all conditions, because a person generally needs to send someone with news of agency, mudarabah, or permission for trade. If these conditions are imposed, people will be in difficulty, because it is difficult to find a person who combines all conditions immediately, and the recipient of the news has no other proof to act upon except this report. If these conditions are imposed, many tasks will be rendered inoperative. Therefore, due to general necessity, the report of every rational and conscious person is accepted. The second proof is that the consideration of the mentioned conditions in the reporter is only so that truthfulness may prevail in the report and the report becomes binding, i.e., imposes something on the listener. Therefore, in reports where there is obligation, like in religious matters, we stipulated these conditions.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage establishes a key usul principle: the conditions for accepting a report (khabar) vary based on whether the report creates an obligation (ilzam) or not. In muamalat (transactions) that do not involve obligation, such as agency (wakalat), mudarabah, and permission for trade (idhn fi al-tijarah), the report of any discerning person (mumayyiz) is acceptable, even if they are not just (adil) or not two in number. The reason is general necessity (darurah ammah): people need to conduct such transactions frequently and cannot always find reporters who meet the strict conditions required for testimony (shahadah) in obligatory matters. The text then elaborates a three-fold classification of transactions: (1) those with pure obligation (e.g., establishing debts or crimes) requiring two just witnesses; (2) those with partial obligation (e.g., dismissing an agent or restraining a slave) requiring either two witnesses or one just witness; and (3) those with no obligation (the subject of this passage) where any mumayyiz's report suffices. This classification is Hanafi and shows the flexibility of the madhhab in accommodating practical needs while maintaining strictness where obligations are created.

Key Terms
مميز (mumayyiz): A person who has reached the age of discernment (tamyiz) and can understand speech and intent.
ضرورة عامة (darurah ammah): A general necessity that applies to a broad class of situations, requiring relaxation of standard legal conditions.
لزوم (luzum): Obligation; the quality of a report that imposes a legal duty on the listener.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are conditions like justice and number dropped in non-obligatory transactions?
A) Because the reporter is always truthful.
B) Because of general necessity and the absence of binding effect.
C) Because Islamic law does not care about truth in such matters.
D) Because non-Muslims have lower standards of evidence.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the conditions for accepting a report are tied to whether the report creates an obligation; general necessity relaxes these conditions in non-binding transactions.

Accepting a Fasiq's Report in Food and Water Matters
Explains when a fasiq's report is accepted with predominant opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition for accepting a fasiq's report in food and water matters, and apply the Hanafi usul rule distinguishing it from hadith narration.

Core Idea
A fasiq's report in food/water matters requires predominant opinion due to necessity; in hadith it is wholly rejected.

In Hanafi usul, the reliability of a reporter depends on context. Religious matters demand a just narrator, but specific worldly necessities allow acceptance of a fasiq's statement when supported by predominant opinion. This lesson unpacks that rule and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for reports in religious matters
Recall that in matters with binding effect (umur al-din), the reporter must be Muslim, upright, of complete intellect, and precise. A fasiq lacks uprightness.
This is the default principle.
2
Identify the exception: food and water matters
The text carves out an exception for matters of permissibility/prohibition of food and purity/impurity of water, where a fasiq's report can be considered.
These are classified as worldly matters despite touching on religious concepts.
3
Explain the condition: predominant opinion
The report is accepted only when supported by predominant opinion (ẓann ghālib) obtained through precautionary search (taḥarrī).
Without this condition, the original permissibility/purity remains.
4
Analyze the reasons
Three reasons: (a) necessity – just people are not commonly found in these contexts; (b) the fasiq is eligible for testimony despite his sin; (c) no suspicion of lying because the ruling applies equally to him.
These reasons justify the exception but do not make it absolute.
5
Contrast with hadith narration
In hadith, just narrators are abundant, so there is no necessity; hence a fasiq's report is never accepted, even with predominant opinion.
This shows the rule is context-sensitive, not a blanket concession.

اعتبار کیا جائے گا فاسق کی خبر کا کھانے کے حلال اور اس کے حرام ہونے میں، پانی کی نجاست اور اس کی طہارت میں جب کہ وہ مؤید ہوظن غالب سے، اس لئے کہ یہ ایک خاص معاملہ ہے جس کا حاصل کرنا عادل لوگوں سے ممکن نہ ہوگا ، پس فاسق کی خبر میں تحری واجب ہوگی ضرورت کی وجہ سے، اور فاسق کے شہادت کا اہل ہونے کی وجہ سے فسق کے باوجود، اور تہمت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس لیے کہ فاسق پر لازم ہوگی اس کی خبر سے وہ چیز جو لازم بلکہ اس کی خبر کے بغیر اصل پر عمل ممکن ہے، اور پانی اصل کے اعتبار سے پاک ہے، اسی طرح کھانا بھی اصل کے اعتبار سے پاک ہے، جب کھانے اور پانی میں شبہ پیدا ہو کہ حلال ہے یا حرام، پاک ہے نا پاک؟ اور کوئی جائے تو خبر معتبر ہوگی۔ ولاضرورة فى المصير :- سوال یہ پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ جب فاسق کی خبر تحری کے ساتھ آپ نے تسلیم کر لی تو پھر روایت حدیث میں بھی اس کی خبر حری کے ساتھ قبول کر لینی چاہیے۔ اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں کہ روایت حدیث میں عادل بہت کثرت سے مل جاتے ہیں، اس لئے دینی امور میں فاسق سے بے نیازی ہو جاتی ہے، لہذا دینی امور یعنی روایت حدیث میں فاسق کی خبر تحری کے ساتھ بھی معتبر نہ ہوگی ، بر خلاف کھانے کی حلت و حرمت اور پانی کی نجاست و طہارت کے کہ یہاں عام طور پر واسطہ فاسقوں سے ہی پڑتا
And the report of a sinner is considered regarding the permissibility of food and its prohibition, and the purity of water and its impurity, when it is supported by predominant opinion, because that is a specific matter that cannot properly be received from just people. So precautionary search (taharri) regarding his report is obligatory due to necessity, and because despite his sin, he is eligible for testimony, and due to the absence of suspicion, because what becomes binding on others by his report also becomes binding on him. But this necessity is not absolute, because acting on the original principle is possible, and that is that water is originally pure. So sin is not made irrelevant, and there is no necessity at all to resort to his narration in matters of religion, because there is an abundance of just narrators and they suffice, so one does not resort to him by precautionary search. Explanation: This is a response to an objection. The objection states: You laid down the principle that in religious matters there is bindingness, so every person's report is not reliable; rather the narrator must have four conditions (Islam, uprightness, complete intellect, precision). But you accept the report of a sinner regarding the permissibility/prohibition of food and purity/impurity of water, even though permissibility/prohibition and purity/impurity are religious matters, and the sinner lacks the condition of uprightness. So his report should not be reliable; you are contradicting your principle. The response: We only accept the sinner's report in matters of permissibility/prohibition and purity/impurity when the listener also has predominant opinion that the sinner's report is correct; we do not decide solely on his report. And in hadith narration, the sinner's report is absolutely not reliable, even if the listener obtains predominant opinion through precautionary search. The difference between the two is that the permissibility/prohibition of food and the purity/impurity of water are specific matters that generally occur in markets, jungles, and such places where sinners are commonly present, and they are the ones who know about them. So out of necessity, the sinner's report is accepted with precautionary search. And this necessity is not present in hadith narration. Besides necessity, the sinner, despite his sin, is eligible for testimony, and also there is no suspicion of lying because the sinner would not lie for personal gain, since what becomes binding on others by his report also becomes binding on him. So his report is accepted with the condition of precautionary search. As for 'but this necessity' – it is a response to a question: When out of necessity you have accepted the sinner's report, why do you need precautionary search? Why not accept it without precautionary search? The response: Undoubtedly necessity exists, but this necessity is not absolute, meaning the matter cannot proceed without his report. Rather, acting on the original principle is possible without his report. Water is originally pure, and similarly food is originally pure. So when doubt arises about food and water, and no informant is available, they are considered permissible and pure. In short, when necessity is not absolute, we neither fully accept the sinner's report such that no need for precautionary search remains, nor do we completely disregard it; rather we give it some consideration. Therefore, we combine it with precautionary search: when his report is supported by predominant opinion, it becomes reliable. As for 'and there is no necessity to resort' – a question arises: If you accept the sinner's report with precautionary search in these matters, why not also accept his report in hadith narration with precautionary search? The answer: In hadith narration, just narrators are abundantly available, so there is no need for sinners in religious matters. Therefore, in religious matters i.e., hadith narration, the sinner's report is not reliable even with precautionary search, unlike the permissibility/prohibition of food and purity/impurity of water, where one generally encounters sinners.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a rule regarding the acceptance of a report from a sinful person (fasiq) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The text begins by stating the general principle: in religious matters (umur al-din) that have binding effect (luzum), the reporter must have four conditions: Islam, uprightness (adala), complete intellect, and precision (dabt). However, in certain specific worldly matters such as the permissibility/haram of food and the purity/najasa of water, the report of a fasiq is accepted provided it is supported by predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) through precautionary search (taharri). The reason is that these matters often arise in places where trustworthy people are not commonly found, so there is necessity. Additionally, the fasiq is eligible for testimony despite his sin, and there is no suspicion of lying because the ruling (e.g., forbidding food) applies equally to him. However, this necessity is not absolute; one could rely on the original principle (al-asl) that things are permissible and pure. Hence, precautionary search is required to ensure predominant opinion. In contrast, in religious matters like hadith narration, there is no such necessity because just narrators are abundant, so a fasiq's report is not accepted at all, even with precautionary search. The commentary then elaborates by answering hypothetical objections and clarifying the distinction between the two contexts.

Key Terms
فاسق (fāsiq): A person who commits major sins or persists on minor sins, lacking 'adala (uprightness) in the legal sense.
ظن غالب (ẓann ghālib): Predominant opinion; a high degree of certainty that falls short of absolute certainty but outweighs doubt.
تحري (taḥarrī): Precautionary search or effort to determine the correct ruling, often by seeking predominant opinion.
عدالت (ʿadāla): Uprightness; a quality of a person who refrains from major sins and does not persist on minor sins, necessary for testimony and narration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition is the report of a fasiq accepted in matters of food permissibility and water purity?
A) It is always accepted without any condition.
B) It is accepted only if supported by predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) through precautionary search.
C) It is accepted only if the fasiq repents.
D) It is never accepted in such matters.

Key Takeaway
A fasiq's report in food/water matters is accepted only when supported by predominant opinion, due to necessity; in hadith narration, it is never accepted because just narrators suffice.

Rejection of Narrations from Active Heretics
Ruling on narrations from propagators of desires

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the narration of an active propagator of heresy and identify the illa (cause) for its rejection.

Core Idea
An active heretic's narration is rejected because his arguing leads to fabricating hadith.

This lesson examines a foundational principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the reliability of narrators. The text establishes that a person who adopts heretical beliefs and actively invites others to them cannot be trusted in transmitting hadith. We will unpack the reasoning (illa) and the scholarly disagreement surrounding this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the explicit statement of the preferred opinion (al-madhhab al-mukhtar) regarding the narration of a person who adopts his desires as a religion and invites others to it.
The text begins: 'وَأَمَّا صَاحِبَ الْهَوَى فَالْمَذْهَبْ الْمُخْتَارُ أنه لا تُقْبَلْ رِوَايَةُ...'
2
Extract the illa
Find the reason given for rejecting the narration. The text states it is because argumentation and invitation to desires lead to fabrication (التَقَولِ). Understand how this illa connects to untrustworthiness.
The illa is: 'لانَ الْمَحَاجَةَ وَالدَّعْوَةَ إِلَى الْهَوَى سَبَبْ دَاعِ إِلَى التَقَولِ'
3
Distinguish the two categories of ahl al-hawa
The text divides ahl al-hawa into those whose beliefs reach kufr and those whose beliefs do not. Note how the ruling on narration and testimony differs for each category according to various scholars.
First type: extreme Rawafid, Mujassima, Qadianis. Second type: those with lesser deviations.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view (some usul scholars accept their narration) and the muhaqqiqun's response (they are kafir, so rejected). Understand the basis of each argument.
The dispute hinges on whether such individuals are considered ahl al-qibla or actually kafir.

وَأَمَّا صَاحِبَ الْهَوَى فَالْمَذْهَبْ الْمُخْتَارُ أنه لا تُقْبَلْ رِوَايَةُ مَنْ إِنْتَحَلَ الْهَوى وَدَعَا النَّاسَ إِلَيْهِ لانَ الْمَحَاجَةَ وَالدَّعْوَةَ إِلَى الْهَوَى سَبَبْ دَاعِ إِلَى التَقَولِ فَلَا يُؤْتَمَنْ عَلَى حَدِيثِ رَسُولِ الله صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ-
ترجمہ : ۔ اور بہر حال نفسانی خواہش والا تو مذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ اس شخص کی روایت قبول نہیں کی جائے گی جس نے خواہشات نفسانی کو دین بنالیا ہو، اور لوگوں کو اس کی جانب دعوت دیتا ہو، اس لئے کہ اس کا حجت پکڑنا اور خواہشات کی طرف دعوت دینا ایسا سبب ہے جو داعی ہے بات کو گھڑنے کی طرف تو اس پر اعتماد نہیں کیا جائے گا رسول اللہ صلی ال اسلام کی حدیث کے بارے میں ۔
تشریح : جو شخص خواہش نفس کا پجاری ہو، اور اہل حق کے عقائد سے ہٹ کر خواہشات نفسانی کو اپنا دین و مذہب بنالیا ہو، اور لوگوں کو اپنے مذہب کی دعوت و ترغیب بھی دیتا ہو اور اپنے دین و مذہب کی حقانیت پر حجت بازی کرتا ہو، ایسا آدمی اگر حدیث روایت کرے تو مذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ اس کی روایت قبول نہیں کیجائے گی جیسے غالی روافض ، قادیانی وغیرہ کیونکہ ان کا اپنے دین کو حق سمجھنا اور اہل حق کے ساتھ بحث و مباحثہ کرنا ، یہ ان کو حدیثیں گھڑنے تک پہنچائے گا، تو ایسے لوگوں پر حدیث رسول کے بارے میں کیسے اعتماد کیا جاسکتا ہے۔
فائدہ : - اہل ہوی دو طرح کے ہیں ، بعض وہ ہیں جن کے عقائد کفر تک پہنچ چکے ہیں، جیسے خالی روافض ، فرقۂ مجسمہ، قادیانی، ان کے بارے میں بعض اہل اصول کہتے ہیں کہ ان کی روایت و شہادت سب مقبول ہیں کیونکہ یہ اہل قبلہ ہیں اور اپنے آپ کو مسلمان سمجھتے ہیں، لیکن محققین علماء اس پر متفق ہیں کہ یہ کافر ہیں، ان کی روایت و شہادت سب ناقابل قبول ہیں۔ دوسرے وہ جن کے عقائد کفر تک نہ پہنچے ہوں ، تو ان کے بارے میں علماء کی ایک جماعت کہتی ہے کہ ان کی روایت و شہادت سب مردود ہیں، کیونکہ یہ فاسق ہیں جن کو جھوٹ اور گناہوں کی پروا نہیں ہے ، مگر جمہور کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ شہادت تو قبول ہوگی مگر روایت میں بعض کے نزدیک مطلقا قبول ہے، اور بعض علماء جن میں صاحب حسامی بھی ہے کہ اگر وہ متعصب ہے اور اس نے اپنی خواہشات کو دین و مذہب بنالیا ہے اور لوگوں کو کھلے عام اس کی دعوت بھی دے رہا ہے تو اس کی خبر معتبر نہ ہوگی۔
And as for the follower of desire, the chosen madhhab is that the narration of one who adopts desire [as his religion] and calls people to it is not accepted, because argumentation and invitation to desire is a cause that leads to fabrication, so he is not to be trusted concerning the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Translation: And in any case, the follower of carnal desire, the chosen madhhab is that the narration of that person is not accepted who has made carnal desires his religion and calls people to it, because his argumentation and invitation to desires is a cause that drives to fabrication, so he will not be trusted concerning the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, may peace be upon him. Explanation: A person who is a worshiper of carnal desire, and deviating from the beliefs of the people of truth, has made carnal desires his religion and madhhab, and also invites and encourages people to his madhhab and argues for the truthfulness of his religion and madhhab, such a person, if he narrates a hadith, then the chosen madhhab is that his narration will not be accepted, like the extreme Rawafid, Qadianis, etc. Because their considering their religion as true and debating with the people of truth will lead them to fabricate hadiths, so how can such people be trusted concerning the hadith of the Messenger? Benefit: The people of desire are of two types: some are those whose beliefs have reached kufr, like the extreme Rawafid, the Mujassima sect, Qadianis. Regarding them, some usul scholars say that their narration and testimony are all accepted because they are ahl al-qibla and consider themselves Muslims. But the muhaqqiqun scholars agree that they are kafir, and their narration and testimony are all unacceptable. The second type are those whose beliefs have not reached kufr. Regarding them, a group of scholars say that their narration and testimony are all rejected because they are fasiq who do not care about lies and sins. But the majority madhhab is that testimony will be accepted, but regarding narration, some absolutely accept it, and some scholars, among them Sahib al-Husami, say that if he is a bigot and has made his desires a religion and madhhab and is openly inviting people to it, then his report is not reliable.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi usul al-fiqh concerning the acceptance of narrations from a person who is a follower of desires (sahib al-hawa) and actively propagates them. The author states the preferred opinion (al-madhhab al-mukhtar): such a person's narration is rejected. The reason (illa) given is that his argumentation and invitation to his heretical views create an incentive to fabricate hadith to support his position. The commentary then expands on this: if such a person narrates a hadith, it is not accepted, citing examples like the extreme Rawafid and Qadianis. The author then provides a beneficial note (fa'idah) classifying ahl al-hawa into two categories: those whose beliefs reach kufr (like extreme sects) and those whose beliefs do not reach kufr. For the first category, there is a disagreement: some usul scholars accept their narration and testimony because they consider themselves Muslims (ahl al-qibla), but the verifying scholars (muhaqqiqun) consider them kafir and reject their narration and testimony entirely. For the second category (beliefs not reaching kufr), a group of scholars consider them fasiq and reject both narration and testimony; but the majority hold that testimony is accepted, while narration is either absolutely accepted by some, or accepted only if the person is not a bigoted propagator. The author inclines towards the view of Sahib al-Husami: if he is a bigot and openly propagates, his report is unreliable. Throughout, the Hanafi position is clear: active heretics are not trustworthy in hadith transmission.

Key Terms
صاحب الهوى (sahib al-hawa): A person who adopts carnal desires as his religion and calls others to it, actively arguing for it.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits sins and does not care about lying or sins; used for the second type of ahl al-hawa whose beliefs have not reached kufr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His narration is absolutely accepted.
B) His narration is rejected.
C) His narration is accepted only if he is also just.
D) His narration is rejected only if he is a known liar.

Key Takeaway
The narration of an active heretic who propagates his views is rejected because his argumentation incentivizes fabricating hadith.

The Authority of Hadith from Faqih vs Non-Faqih Narrators
Differentiating the authority of hadith based on narrator's fiqh expertise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a hadith from a faqih narrator overrides qiyas, while a hadith from a non-faqih narrator is only accepted contrary to qiyas in cases of necessity.

Core Idea
A narrator's fiqh expertise determines whether his hadith can override qiyas; a mere just narrator's hadith cannot.

This passage from Al-Husami establishes a key principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: not all reliable narrators are equal when their hadith conflict with qiyas. The author distinguishes between narrators known for fiqh and ijtihad—such as the Rightly Guided Caliphs and leading Companions—and those known only for justice and memory, like Abu Hurayra. The ruling affects how a mufti weighs hadith against analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of narrators
Read the passage and list the two types: 'ma'ruf bi al-fiqh' (known for fiqh) and 'ma'ruf bi al-'adala' (known for justice but not fiqh). Note the examples provided for each.
The faqih category includes the Caliphs, the Abdallahs, Zaid, Mu'adh, Abu Musa, and Aisha; the non-faqih category includes Abu Hurayra and Anas.
2
State the ruling for faqih narrators
According to the passage, if a narrator is a faqih and his hadith contradicts qiyas, qiyas is abandoned (yutraku bihi al-qiyas). This is the default ruling.
No additional condition is needed; the hadith is given full authority.
3
State the ruling for non-faqih narrators
If the narrator is only known for justice and precision (not fiqh), then if his hadith agrees with qiyas, it is acted upon; if it contradicts qiyas, it is not abandoned except for necessity (darura) and when the door of ra'y is closed (insidad bab al-ra'y).
The hadith does not automatically override qiyas; it is only accepted in exceptional circumstances.
4
Examine the example of al-musarrah
The passage references the hadith of Abu Hurayra on musarrah (tying the udder to deceive). This hadith contradicts qiyas (which would normally allow the sale), but it is accepted due to necessity because the door of ra'y is closed on this specific ruling.
This illustrates the exception for non-faqih narrators.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Imagine a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar (a faqih) prohibiting a certain sale that qiyas permits. Qiyas is abandoned. If the same hadith came from Abu Hurayra, you would need to check if necessity exists to accept it against qiyas.
The practical outcome depends on the narrator's fiqh status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا ثَبَتَ أَنَّ خَبَرَ الْوَاحِدِ حُجَةٌ قُلْنَا اِنْ كَانَ الرَّاوِئ مَعْرُوفًا بِالْفِقْهِ وَالتَّقَدِّم فِي الْإِجْتِهَادِ كَالْخُلَفَاءِ الرَّاشِدِينَ وَالْعَبَادِلَةِ الثَّلْثَةِ وَزَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ وَمُعَاذِ بْنِ جَبَلٍ وَأَبِى مُؤسَى الْأَشْعَرِئ وَعَائِشَةَ رِضْوَانَ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِمْ أَجْمَعِيْنَ وَغَيْرِهِمْ مِمَّنْ اشْتَهَرَ بِالْفِقْهِ وَالنَّظْرِكَانَ حَدِيثُهُمْ حُجَّةً يُتْرَكَ بِهِ الْقِيَاسُ وَإِنْ كَانَ الرَّاوِى مَعْرُوفًا بِالْعَدَالَةِ وَالْحِفْظِ وَالضَّبْطِ دُونَ الْفِقْهِ مِثْلُ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ وَأَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَإِنْ وَافَقَ حَدِيثُهُ الْقِيَاسَ عُمِلَ بِهِ وَإِنْ خَالَفَهُ لَمْ يُتْرَكْ إِلَّا لِلضَّرُورَةِ وَانْسِدَادِ بَابِ الرَّأْيِ وَذَلِكَ مِثْلُ حَدِيثِ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ فِي الْمُصَرَاةِ
ترجمہ : ۔ اور جب یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ خبر واحد حجت ہے تو ہم کہیں گے کہ اگر راوی معروف ہو فقہ کے ساتھ اور اجتہاد میں تقدم حاصل ہونے کے ساتھ جیسے خلفاء راشدین اور تینوں عبداللہ، اور زید بن ثابت اور معاذ بن جبل اور ابو موسی اشعری اور عائشہ رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین، اور ان کے علاوہ ان لوگوں میں سے جو فقہ ونظر کے ساتھ مشہور ہیں ، تو ان کی حدیث حجت ہوگی جس کی وجہ سے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر راوی عدالت ، حفظ اور ضبط کے ساتھ معروف ہو نہ کہ فقہ کے ساتھ جیسے ابو ہریرہ، اور انس بن مالک پس اگر ان کی حدیث قیاس کے موافق ہو تو اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا اور اگر قیاس کے خلاف ہو تو ترک نہیں کیا جائے گا مگر ضرورت کی وجہ سے اور رائے وقیاس کے دروازے کے بند ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ جیسے ابو ہریرہ کی حدیث ہے مُصر اۃ کے سلسلہ میں ۔
شریح:- مصنف روایت پر کلام سے فارغ ہو کر اب راوی پر گفتگو کر رہے ہیں ،فرماتے ہیں کہ راوی یا تو معروف ہوگا یا مجہول ،اگر معروف ہے تو اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں ، معروف بالفقہ ہے یا معروف بالعدالت ہے، اور اگر مجہول ہے تو اس کی پانچ قسمیں ہیں، مصنف اس کو آگے بیان کر رہے ہیں بہر حال پہلی قسم یعنی راوی (صحابی ) اگر فقہ میں مشہور ہو اور اجتہاد کی وجہ سے اس کو دوسرے صحابہ پر فوقیت حاصل ہو اور ان کے علاوہ جو فقہ اور نظر وفکر میں مشہور ہو گئے ہوں جیسے خلفاء راشدین ، تینوں عبداللہ عبد اللہ بن عمر، عبد اللہ بن مسعود، عبداللہ بن عباس، بعض کے نزدیک عبد اللہ بن مسعود کی جگہ عبداللہ بن زبیر ہیں ، بعض کہتے ہیں کہ عبداللہ چار ہیں، عبداللہ بن عمر، عبد اللہ بن زبیر، عبد اللہ بن عباس اور عبداللہ بن عمرو بن العاص، رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین ، اسی طرح زید بن ثابت ، ابوموسی اشعری ، معاذ بن جبل اور حضرت عائشہ رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین یہ تمام صحابہ فقہ میں بھی معروف ہیں اور اجتہاد میں بھی سب پر فائق
And when it is established that khabar al-wahid is a proof, we say: if the narrator is known for fiqh and precedence in ijtihad like the Rightly Guided Caliphs, the three Abdallahs, Zaid bin Thabit, Mu'adh bin Jabal, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them all) and others who are famous for fiqh and reflection, then their hadith is a proof by which qiyas is abandoned. And if the narrator is known for justice ('adala), memory (hifdh), and precision (dabt) but not fiqh, like Abu Hurayra and Anas bin Malik (may Allah be pleased with them), then if his hadith agrees with qiyas, it is acted upon; and if it contradicts qiyas, it is not abandoned except for necessity and when the door of ra'y is closed. And that is like the hadith of Abu Hurayra concerning al-musarrah. Translation: And when it is established that khabar wahid is a proof, we will say: if the narrator is known for fiqh and has precedence in ijtihad, like the Rightly Guided Caliphs, the three Abdallahs, Zaid bin Thabit, Mu'adh bin Jabal, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Aisha, may Allah be pleased with them all, and others among those who are famous for fiqh and reflection, then their hadith is a proof, due to which qiyas will be abandoned. And if the narrator is known for justice, memory, and precision, not for fiqh, like Abu Hurayra and Anas bin Malik, then if their hadith agrees with qiyas, it will be acted upon; and if it contradicts qiyas, it will not be abandoned except for necessity and because the door of ra'y and qiyas is closed. And that is like the hadith of Abu Hurayra concerning al-musarrah. Explanation: The author, after finishing discussion on narration, now talks about the narrator. He says: the narrator is either known or unknown. If known, it has two types: known for fiqh or known for justice. And if unknown, it has five types, which the author will explain later. In any case, the first type, i.e., a narrator (companion) if he is famous in fiqh and due to ijtihad he has precedence over other companions, and besides them, those who became famous for fiqh and reflection, like the Rightly Guided Caliphs, the three Abdallahs: Abdullah bin Umar, Abdullah bin Mas'ud, Abdullah bin Abbas (some say instead of Abdullah bin Mas'ud it is Abdullah bin Zubair; some say the Abdallahs are four: Abdullah bin Umar, Abdullah bin Zubair, Abdullah bin Abbas, and Abdullah bin Amr bin al-Aas), and similarly Zaid bin Thabit, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Mu'adh bin Jabal, and Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them all). All these companions are famous in fiqh and superior in ijtihad.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage states a rule in Hanafi usul al-fiqh regarding the acceptance of khabar al-wahid and its relationship with qiyas. It begins by affirming that khabar wahid is a proof. Then it classifies narrators into two categories: (1) Those known for fiqh and precedence in ijtihad, like the Rightly Guided Caliphs, the three (or four) Abdallahs, Zaid bin Thabit, Mu'adh bin Jabal, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Aisha. Their hadith is a proof that can override qiyas; if their hadith contradicts qiyas, qiyas is abandoned. (2) Those known for 'adala (justice), hifdh (memory), and dabt (precision) but not necessarily fiqh, like Abu Hurayra and Anas bin Malik. For such narrators, if their hadith agrees with qiyas, it is acted upon. If it contradicts qiyas, it is not abandoned except in cases of necessity (darura) and when the door of ra'y and qiyas is closed (insidad bab al-ra'y). An example is the hadith of Abu Hurayra on al-musarrah (a she-camel whose udder is tied to increase milk yield), which is a well-known hadith that seems to contradict qiyas but is accepted as an exception due to the strength of the narration. The author's commentary (sharh) then explains that narrators are either known or unknown; the known ones are of two types as above, and the unknown have five types to be explained later. The passage enumerates the specific companions who are considered fuqaha' and muqaddimin in ijtihad, with a note of variation on the identity of the three Abdallahs. The overall point is that the authority of a hadith over qiyas depends not merely on the narrator's reliability in transmission but also on his juristic understanding.

Key Terms
معروف بالفقہ (ma'ruf bi al-fiqh): Known for deep understanding of Islamic law and for precedence in ijtihad; such narrators include the Rightly Guided Caliphs and leading Companions.
معروف بالعدالة (ma'ruf bi al-'adala): Known for justice, memory, and precision in transmission, but not for fiqh; such narrators include Abu Hurayra and Anas.
خبر واحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by a single or a few narrators; established as a proof (hujja) in Hanafi usul.
مصراة (musarrah): A she-camel whose udder is tied to give an impression of abundant milk; the hadith of Abu Hurayra on this topic is an example of a hadith that contradicts qiyas but is accepted due to necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a narrator known for justice and memory (but not fiqh) narrates a hadith that contradicts qiyas, what do the Hanafis do according to this passage?
A) Accept the hadith and abandon qiyas unconditionally.
B) Reject the hadith entirely.
C) Act on the hadith only if there is necessity and the door of ra'y is closed.
D) Prefer qiyas over the hadith in all cases.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a hadith from a faqih narrator overrides qiyas, while a hadith from a non-faqih narrator only does so in cases of necessity.

Classifying Narrators of Khabar Wahid Opposing Qiyas
Classification and dispute on khabar wahid vs qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi classification of narrators to determine whether a khabar wahid overrides qiyas or requires necessity.

Core Idea
A narrator's juristic expertise, not just reliability, decides if khabar wahid supersedes qiyas.

When a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) contradicts analogical reasoning (qiyas), does the hadith or the qiyas prevail? The Hanafi school answers that it depends on the narrator's qualifications. In this passage from a sharh of al-Husami, we learn two categories of narrators: those known for fiqh and ijtihad, whose hadith overrides qiyas, and those known only for ʿadāla and ḍabṭ, whose hadith is only accepted out of necessity if it opposes qiyas. This lesson unpacks this classification and the underlying dispute with Imam Mālik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of narrators
The text divides narrators into two types: (1) those known for fiqh and ijtihad (maʿrūf bi’l-fiqh), e.g., the Rightly Guided Caliphs, the three ʿAbdallāhs, Zayd ibn Thābit, etc.; (2) those known for ʿadāla, ḥifẓ, and ḍabṭ but not fiqh, e.g., Abū Hurayra and Anas ibn Mālik.
The key distinction is juristic expertise, not just reliability.
2
Apply the ruling to each category
For category 1: the khabar wahid is a proof that abandons qiyas. For category 2: if the hadith agrees with qiyas, it is acted upon; if it contradicts, it is only accepted out of necessity (ḍarūra) and when the door of opinion is closed.
Example: the hadith of Abū Hurayra on musāraʿa (a sale of milk animals) was accepted out of necessity even though it opposed qiyas.
3
Understand the dispute with Imam Mālik
Imām Mālik holds that any khabar wahid opposing qiyas is abandoned, regardless of the narrator. He argues that khabar wahid has multiple doubts (error, lie, non-establishment) while qiyas has only one (mujtahid error). Thus qiyas is preferred.
Mālik's example: the hadith 'Whoever washes the deceased should perform ghusl' – it opposes qiyas but everyone acts on qiyas, not the hadith.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafī response: the doubt in khabar wahid is in transmission, not its origin; the origin is certain (it is from the Prophet). Qiyas, however, is doubtful in its origin because the effective cause (ʿilla) is conjectural. Therefore khabar wahid is stronger.
Thus, when the narrator is a faqīh, his khabar overrides qiyas; otherwise necessity limits its use.

خود بھی غسل کرے اور جس نے میت کو اٹھا یا وہ وضو کرے ۔ یہ حدیث قیاس کے خلاف ہے، کیونکہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ میت کو غسل دینے سے غسل واجب نہ ہو، اور نہ جنازہ اٹھانے سے وضو واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ اس میں حدث اکبر یا حدث اصغر نہیں پایا جارہا ہے جو غسل یا وضو کو واجب کرے۔اس جگہ سب کے نزدیک قیاس پر عمل ہے، امام مالک کہتے ہیں کہ دیکھو خبر واحد قیاس کے خلاف تھی، اس لئے مخبر واحد کو چھوڑ دیا۔ لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہاں مخبر واحد کو اس لئے چھوڑ دیا گیا کہ اس کے راوی ابو ہریرہ معروف بالفقہ والاجتہاد نہیں ہے ایسا نہیں ہے کہ مطلق خبر واحد کو جو مخالف للقیاس ہو، اس کو چھوڑ دیں گے، بلکہ اگر راوی معروف بالفقہ والا جتہاد ہو تو اس کی خبر واحد حجت گی ، اگر چہ قیاس کے خلاف ہو۔ امام مالک یہ دلیل پیش کرتے ہیں کہ خبر واحد میں کئی شبہات ہیں، یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ راوی کو سہو ہو گیا ہو، یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ راوی نے کذب بیانی کی ہو، یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ حدیث سرے سے ثابت ہی نہ ہو۔ اور قیاس میں صرف ایک ہی شبہ ہے کہ ہو سکتا ہے مجتہد نے خطا کی ہو، تو جس میں زیادہ شبہات ہوں اس کو مراد لینے کے بجائے جس میں ایک شبہ ہو اس کو مراد لینا اولی ہے، لہذا خبر واحد کے مقابلہ میں قیاس کو مراد لینا اولی ہوگا ، ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا کہ خبر واحد کی اصل میں کوئی شبہ نہیں ہے، کیونکہ یہ بات یقینی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی نیلم کی حدیث ہے، البتہ اس خبر کے طریق وصول میں یعنی اس خبر کے ہم تک پہنچنے میں شبہ ہے، اور قیاس کی تو اصل ہی شبہ و احتمال پر ہے، کیونکہ مجتہد نے جس وصف کو علت بنایا ہے، اس میں ہی شبہ و احتمال ہے کہ یہ وصف علت ہے یا اور کوئی وصف علت ہے، لہذا جس کی اصل ( بنیاد) محتمل ہو، اس کے مقابلہ میں جس کی اصل (بنیاد) یقینی ہو وہ زیادہ قوی ہے پس خبر واحد قیاس سے اولی ہوگا۔ وان كان الراوى - اور دوسری قسم یعنی اگر راوی عدالت ، حفظ اور ضبط میں معروف ہو، فقہ میں معروف نہ ہو جیسے حضرت ابو ہریرہ ، حضرت انس بن مالک تو ایسے راوی کی خبر واحد اگر قیاس کے موافق ہو تو اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا، ظاہر ہے کہ اس صورت میں قیاس پر بھی عمل ہوگا ، اور اگر خبر واحد قیاس کے خلاف ہو تو خبر کو ضرورت کی وجہ سے چھوڑ دیا جائے گا اور قیاس پر عمل کیا جائے گا، عبارت میں انسداد باب الرای ضرورۃ کا عطف تفسیری ہے،
And when it is established that khabar wahid is a proof, we say: if the narrator is known for fiqh and advancement in ijtihad, like the rightly guided caliphs, the three Abdallahs, Zayd ibn Thabit, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Aisha, and others who are famous for fiqh and consideration, then their hadith is a proof by which qiyas is abandoned. And if the narrator is known for uprightness, memory, and precision without fiqh, like Abu Huraira and Anas ibn Malik, then if his hadith agrees with qiyas it is acted upon, and if it contradicts it, it is not abandoned except out of necessity and the closure of the door of opinion. And that is like the hadith of Abu Huraira concerning al-musaraat. Translation: And when it is established that khabar wahid is a proof, we say: if the narrator is known for fiqh and advancement in ijtihad, like the rightly guided caliphs, the three Abdallahs, and Zayd ibn Thabit, and Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Aisha, and others who are famous for fiqh and consideration, then their hadith is a proof by which qiyas is abandoned. And if the narrator is known for uprightness, memory, and precision without fiqh, like Abu Huraira and Anas ibn Malik, then if his hadith agrees with qiyas it is acted upon, and if it contradicts, it is not abandoned except out of necessity and closure of the door of opinion. And that is like the hadith of Abu Huraira concerning al-musaraat. Commentary: The author, after finishing discussion on the narration, now speaks about the narrator. He says the narrator is either known or unknown. If known, there are two types: known for fiqh or known for uprightness. If unknown, there are five types, which the author will mention later. In any case, the first type: if the narrator (companion) is famous in fiqh and has superiority over other companions due to ijtihad, like the rightly guided caliphs, the three Abdallahs (Abdullah ibn Umar, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Abdullah ibn Abbas; some say Abdullah ibn Zubayr instead of Ibn Mas'ud, some say there are four: Abdullah ibn Umar, Abdullah ibn Zubayr, Abdullah ibn Abbas, Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As), similarly Zayd ibn Thabit, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and Aisha — all these companions are famous in fiqh and preeminent in ijtihad. Also others who became famous in consideration and fiqh like Ubayy ibn Ka'b, Abu Darda — they are also counted among the fuqaha of the companions. If these people narrate a khabar wahid and it contradicts qiyas, then qiyas is abandoned. Imam Malik says that any khabar wahid that contradicts qiyas should be abandoned and qiyas acted upon. For example, the marfu' hadith: 'Whoever washes the deceased should perform ghusl, and whoever carries him should perform wudu.' This hadith contradicts qiyas, because qiyas requires that washing a deceased does not make ghusl obligatory, nor does carrying a janazah make wudu obligatory, because no major or minor impurity is found that would necessitate ghusl or wudu. In this case, everyone acts upon qiyas. Imam Malik says: Look, the khabar wahid contradicted qiyas, so the khabar was abandoned. But we say that here the khabar was abandoned because its narrator, Abu Huraira, is not known for fiqh and ijtihad. It is not that every khabar wahid that opposes qiyas is abandoned; rather, if the narrator is known for fiqh and ijtihad, then his khabar wahid is a proof even if it opposes qiyas. Imam Malik presents the argument that khabar wahid has several doubts: it is possible the narrator made a mistake, or he lied, or the hadith is not established at all. Qiyas has only one doubt: that the mujtahid may have erred. So it is more appropriate to prefer that which has fewer doubts, so qiyas should be preferred over khabar wahid. Our response is that there is no doubt in the origin of khabar wahid, because it is certain that it is the hadith of the Messenger of Allah; rather, the doubt is in the manner of its transmission. As for qiyas, its very origin is based on doubt and probability, because the attribute that the mujtahid takes as the cause is itself subject to doubt. Therefore, what has a certain origin is stronger than what has a probable origin, so khabar wahid is preferable to qiyas. 'And if the narrator' — the second type: if the narrator is known for uprightness, memory, and precision, but not known for fiqh, like Abu Huraira and Anas ibn Malik, then if his khabar wahid agrees with qiyas, it is acted upon. Obviously, in that case qiyas is also acted upon. And if the khabar wahid contradicts qiyas, then the khabar is abandoned due to necessity and qiyas is acted upon. In the text, 'closure of the door of opinion' is an explanatory conjunction with 'necessity'.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from a sharh of al-Husami classifies narrators of khabar wahid when their report conflicts with qiyas. The author first states the rule: a khabar wahid from a narrator who is known for fiqh and ijtihad (like the Khulafa Rashideen, the three Abdallahs, Zayd ibn Thabit, etc.) is a proof that overrides qiyas. If the narrator is known only for uprightness, memory, and precision but not for fiqh (like Abu Huraira and Anas), then his hadith is accepted if it agrees with qiyas; if it contradicts, it is only accepted out of necessity (e.g., the hadith on musaraat). The commentary then expands: the narrator is either known or unknown. Known narrators are of two types: ma'ruf bil-fiqh (known for fiqh) and ma'ruf bil-'adala (known for uprightness). The author lists companion fuqaha. Then a dispute with Imam Malik arises: Malik holds that any khabar wahid opposing qiyas is abandoned, giving the example of the hadith 'man ghasala al-mayta...'. The Hanafis respond that this hadith was abandoned because its narrator Abu Huraira was not a faqih; if the narrator were a faqih, the hadith would prevail. Malik's argument: khabar wahid has multiple potential doubts (error, lie, non-establishment) while qiyas has only one (mujtahid error). Hanafi response: the doubt in khabar is in transmission, not origin; qiyas's origin itself is doubtful (the 'illa is conjectural). Thus khabar wahid is stronger. The second category is then reaffirmed.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith narrated by one or a few individuals not reaching tawatur; it is a proof (hujja) by consensus, but its preference over qiyas depends on the narrator's qualifications.
معروف بالفقہ (ma'ruf bi'l-fiqh): A narrator known for juristic understanding and ijtihad, such that his narrations override qiyas.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning applying an existing ruling to a new case due to shared effective cause ('illa). In this passage, qiyas is contrasted with khabar wahid as a source of law.
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity; in this context, an exceptional circumstance that allows accepting a khabar wahid from a non-faqih narrator that contradicts qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when is a khabar wahid that opposes qiyas accepted as a proof that abandons qiyas?
A) When the narrator is known for 'adala, hifz, and dhabt
B) When the narrator is known for fiqh and ijtihad
C) Only when the hadith is mutawatir
D) It is never accepted over qiyas

Key Takeaway
A narrator's juristic expertise (fiqh and ijtihad) determines whether his khabar wahid overrides qiyas; otherwise, it is only accepted in necessity.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Preference for Khabar al-Wahid from a Faqih Narrator over Qiyas
Explaining a usul rule with an inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that a khabar al-wahid from a faqih narrator is preferred over qiyas, and distinguish it from the case of a non-faqih narrator.

Core Idea
A narrator's fiqh makes his solitary report stronger than qiyas; without fiqh, qiyas prevails.

In Hanafi usul, not all solitary reports are equal. When a khabar al-wahid contradicts qiyas, the deciding factor is the narrator's level of fiqh. This passage from Al-Faiz-ul-Hijaz explains the rule and its rationale, contrasting it with Imam Malik's view, and applies it to the famous hadith of musarraah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of narrators
The passage divides narrators of khabar al-wahid into two types: those known for fiqh (like Ubayy ibn Ka'b) and those known only for reliability but not fiqh (like Abu Hurayra). Note the different ruling for each.
This categorization is critical: it determines whether the khabar or qiyas takes precedence.
2
State the Hanafi rule for each category
For a faqih narrator: his khabar is preferred over qiyas even if contrary. For a non-faqih narrator: if his khabar agrees with qiyas, both are followed; if contrary, qiyas is followed and the khabar is abandoned due to necessity.
The phrase 'due to necessity' refers to preserving qiyas as a valid source of law.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to Imam Malik's proof
Imam Malik argued that khabar al-wahid has multiple doubts (error, lying, non-establishment) while qiyas has only one (mujtahid's error). The Hanafi response: the doubts in khabar are only in transmission; its origin (the Prophet's statement) is certain. Qiyas's origin (the illa) is probabilistic. Certainty outweighs probability.
This is a key epistemological argument: thubut (certainty of origin) vs. wujub (certainty of transmission).
4
Apply the rule to the hadith of musarraah
The hadith narrated by Abu Hurayra (non-faqih) says that a buyer of an animal with tied udders has the option to return it and give one sa' of dates. This contradicts qiyas on two points: the option to return without a defect, and compensation by dates regardless of milk quantity. Since the narrator is non-faqih, Hanafis abandon the hadith and uphold the sale without option.
The practical impact: the sale is valid, and the buyer has no right to rescind; only the milk is compensated by its value, not a fixed sa'.
