ہیں، اور ان کے علاوہ جو نظر وفکر اور فقہ میں مشہور ہو گئے جیسے ابی بن کعب، ابودرداء ان کا بھی فقہائے صحابہ میں شمار ہے، یہ حضرات اگر خبر واحد روایت کریں، اور ان کی خبر واحد قیاس کے خلاف ہو تو قیاس کو ترک کر دیا جائے گا۔ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ مطلق خبر واحد جب قیاس کے خلاف ہو تو خبر واحد کو چھوڑ دیا جائے گا، اور قیاس پر عمل کیا جائے گا۔ جیسے مرفوع حدیث ہے من غَسَلَ الميت فليغتسل ومن حمله فليتوضا جس نے میت کو غسل دیا وہ خود بھی غسل کرے اور جس نے میت کو اٹھا یا وہ وضو کرے ۔ یہ حدیث قیاس کے خلاف ہے، کیونکہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ میت کو غسل دینے سے غسل واجب نہ ہو، اور نہ جنازہ اٹھانے سے وضو واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ اس میں حدث اکبر یا حدث اصغر نہیں پایا جارہا ہے جو غسل یا وضو کو واجب کرے۔اس جگہ سب کے نزدیک قیاس پر عمل ہے، امام مالک کہتے ہیں کہ دیکھو خبر واحد قیاس کے خلاف تھی، اس لئے مخبر واحد کو چھوڑ دیا۔ لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہاں مخبر واحد کو اس لئے چھوڑ دیا گیا کہ اس کے راوی ابو ہریرہ معروف بالفقہ والاجتہاد نہیں ہے ایسا نہیں ہے کہ مطلق خبر واحد کو جو مخالف للقیاس ہو، اس کو چھوڑ دیں گے، بلکہ اگر راوی معروف بالفقہ والا جتہاد ہو تو اس کی خبر واحد حجت گی ، اگر چہ قیاس کے خلاف ہو۔ امام مالک یہ دلیل پیش کرتے ہیں کہ خبر واحد میں کئی شبہات ہیں، یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ راوی کو سہو ہو گیا ہو، یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ راوی نے کذب بیانی کی ہو، یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ حدیث سرے سے ثابت ہی نہ ہو۔ اور قیاس میں صرف ایک ہی شبہ ہے کہ ہو سکتا ہے مجتہد نے خطا کی ہو، تو جس میں زیادہ شبہات ہوں اس کو مراد لینے کے بجائے جس میں ایک شبہ ہو اس کو مراد لینا اولی ہے، لہذا خبر واحد کے مقابلہ میں قیاس کو مراد لینا اولی ہوگا ، ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا کہ خبر واحد کی اصل میں کوئی شبہ نہیں ہے، کیونکہ یہ بات یقینی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی نیلم کی حدیث ہے، البتہ اس خبر کے طریق وصول میں یعنی اس خبر کے ہم تک پہنچنے میں شبہ ہے، اور قیاس کی تو اصل ہی شبہ و احتمال پر ہے، کیونکہ مجتہد نے جس وصف کو علت بنایا ہے، اس میں ہی شبہ و احتمال ہے کہ یہ وصف علت ہے یا اور کوئی وصف علت ہے، لہذا جس کی اصل ( بنیاد) محتمل ہو، اس کے مقابلہ میں جس کی اصل (بنیاد) یقینی ہو وہ زیادہ قوی ہے پس خبر واحد قیاس سے اولی ہوگا۔ وان كان الراوى - اور دوسری قسم یعنی اگر راوی عدالت ، حفظ اور ضبط میں معروف ہو، فقہ میں معروف نہ ہو جیسے حضرت ابو ہریرہ ، حضرت انس بن مالک تو ایسے راوی کی خبر واحد اگر قیاس کے موافق ہو تو اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا، ظاہر ہے کہ اس صورت میں قیاس پر بھی عمل ہوگا ، اور اگر خبر واحد قیاس کے خلاف ہو تو خبر کو ضرورت کی وجہ سے چھوڑ دیا جائے گا اور قیاس پر عمل کیا جائے گا، عبارت میں انسداد باب الرای ضرورۃ کا عطف تفسیری ہے، اور ضرورت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ غیر فقیہ راوی کی حدیث اگر قیاس کے مخالف ہو اور اس وقت بھی حدیث پر ہی عمل کیا گیا تو قیاس کا دروازہ بالکل بند ہو جائے گا، حالانکہ اللہ تعالی نے " فاعتبروا یا اولی الابصار " کے ذریعہ قیاس کا حکم فرمایا ہے۔ اور دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ چونکہ راوی غیر فقیہ ہے تو احتمال ہے کہ اس نے روایت بالمعنی کی ہو، کیونکہ صحابہ میں روایت بالمعنی کا طریقہ رائج تھا، قومی امکان ہے کہ راوی نے غیر فقیہ ہونے کی وجہ سے آپ سالی یا پیام کا مقصد نہ سمجھا ہو، غلطی کی ہو، روایت بالمعنی کر دی ہو، لہذا قیاس کے خلاف ہونے کی صورت میں غیر فقیہ راوی کی روایت ترک کردی جائے گی۔ وذلك مثل حدیث ابی هریرہ:- غیر فقیہ راوی کی روایت جو قیاس کے مخالف ہو اس کی مثال ابوہریرہ رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث مُصَرَّاۃ ہے، وہ حدیث ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لا تصر وا الابل والغنم فمن ابتاعها بعد ذلك فهو بخير النظرين بعد أن يجلبها أن رضيها أمسكها وان سخطهاردها و صاعا من تمر، (مسلم) رسول اللہ صلی ایتم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ تم اونٹوں اور بکریوں کے تھنوں میں دودھ جمع نہ کرو، پس جس نے اس جانور کو خریدا تصریہ کے بعد ، تو اس کو دوہنے کے بعد مشتری کو اختیار ہے، پسند ہو تو رکھ لے اور نا پسند کرے تو وہ جانور واپس لوٹا دے اور ایک صاع کھجور بھی دیدے۔ تصر یہ کہتے ہیں جانور کے تھنوں میں دودھ جمع کرنا ، تا کہ اس کے تھن بھرے ہوئے ہوں اور اس کی قیمت اچھی ملے، یہ مشتری کے ساتھ دھو کہ ہے، اس لئے مشتری کو اختیار ہے، چاہے تو رکھ لے چاہے تو واپس کرے اور جو دودھ دوہا ہے اس کے بدلہ ایک صاع کھجور دیدے۔ یہ حدیث ہر طرح سے قیاس کے مخالف ہے، کیونکہ کسی نقصان کی تلافی کے لئے قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ ذوات الامثال میں مثل سے ضمان ہو، اور ذوات القیم میں قیمت سے ضمان ہو، اور یہاں ہر حال میں ایک صاع کھجور واجب ہے، جو دودھ کا نہ مثل صوری ہے نہ معنوی یعنی قیمت ، ایک صاع کھجور کو قیمت بھی نہیں کہہ سکتے ، کیونکہ اگر قیمت ہے تو دودھ کے برابر ہونی چاہیے، اور یہاں چاہے جتنا بھی دودھ نکالا ہو، ایک صاع تمر واجب ہے، بہر حال یہ حدیث قیاس کے بالکل مخالف ہے، لہذا حدیث کو چھوڑ دینگے اور بیچ منعقد ہو جائے گی اور مشتری کو بیع فسخ کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ بیج کو واپس کرنے کا اختیار صرف اسی صورت میں ہوتا ہے جب صبیح میں عیب ہو اور یہاں مبیع صحیح سالم ہے،صرف اس کے ثمرہ (دودھ) میں کمی ہوئی ہے، اور ثمرہ کے معدوم ہونے سے مبیع معدوم نہیں ہوتی تو شمرہ میں کمی سے بدرجہ اولی بیچ معدوم نہ ہوگی لہذا طبیع کو واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا ، امام صاحب کا
And besides them, those who became famous in thought, reflection, and fiqh, such as Ubayy ibn Ka'b and Abu Darda', are also counted among the fuqaha of the Companions. If these noble persons narrate a khabar al-wahid, and their khabar al-wahid is contrary to qiyas, then qiyas will be abandoned. Imam Malik says: Absolutely any khabar al-wahid, when it is contrary to qiyas, the khabar al-wahid will be abandoned and qiyas will be acted upon. For example, the marfu' hadith: 'Whoever washes the deceased, let him perform ghusl, and whoever carries him, let him perform wudu.' This hadith is contrary to qiyas, because the requirement of qiyas is that washing the deceased does not make ghusl obligatory, nor does carrying the funeral make wudu obligatory, because there is no major or minor impurity occurring that would make ghusl or wudu obligatory. In this place, according to everyone, qiyas is acted upon. Imam Malik says: Look, the khabar al-wahid was contrary to qiyas, therefore the single narrator was abandoned. But we say: Here the single narrator was abandoned because its narrator, Abu Hurayra, is not known for fiqh and ijtihad. It is not that absolutely any khabar al-wahid that is contrary to qiyas will be abandoned. Rather, if the narrator is known for fiqh and ijtihad, then his khabar al-wahid is a proof, even if it is contrary to qiyas. Imam Malik presents this proof: In khabar al-wahid there are several doubts: there is a possibility that the narrator made an error, there is a possibility that the narrator lied, there is a possibility that the hadith is not established at all. But in qiyas there is only one doubt: that the mujtahid may have erred. So to prefer what has more doubts over what has one doubt is not appropriate; rather, preferring what has one doubt is more appropriate. Therefore, compared to khabar al-wahid, preferring qiyas is more appropriate. Our response to this is: In khabar al-wahid, its origin has no doubt because it is certain that it is the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, may peace be upon him. However, there is doubt in the method of its transmission, i.e., in its reaching us. As for qiyas, its very origin is based on doubt and probability, because the mujtahid, the attribute he made as the cause, there is doubt and probability in it as to whether this attribute is the cause or some other attribute is the cause. Therefore, that whose origin (basis) is probable, compared to that whose origin (basis) is certain, the latter is stronger. Thus, khabar al-wahid is more appropriate than qiyas. 'And if the narrator' — and the second type: if the narrator is known for 'adala, memory, and precision, but not known in fiqh, like Abu Hurayra and Anas ibn Malik, then the khabar al-wahid of such a narrator, if it agrees with qiyas, will be acted upon. Obviously, in this case qiyas will also be acted upon. And if the khabar al-wahid is contrary to qiyas, then due to necessity the khabar will be abandoned and qiyas will be acted upon. In the text, 'insidad bab al-ra'y daruratan' is explanatory apposition. And the meaning of necessity is that if the hadith of a non-faqih narrator is contrary to qiyas and even then the hadith is acted upon, then the door of qiyas would be completely closed, whereas Allah Almighty has commanded qiyas through 'So take heed, O people of insight.' And the second reason is that since the narrator is non-faqih, there is a possibility that he narrated by meaning (riwaya bil-ma'na), because among the Companions the method of narration by meaning was prevalent. There is a strong possibility that the narrator, due to being non-faqih, did not understand the purpose of the Prophet, may peace be upon him, made a mistake, and narrated by meaning. Therefore, when contrary to qiyas, the narration of a non-faqih narrator will be abandoned. 'And that is like the hadith of Abu Hurayra' — an example of a non-faqih narrator's narration that is contrary to qiyas is the hadith of Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him, about musarraah. That hadith is: 'The Prophet, may peace be upon him, said: Do not tie the udders of camels and sheep. Whoever buys such an animal after that has the choice after milking it: if he is pleased, he keeps it; if he is displeased, he returns it and (gives) a sa' of dates.' (Muslim) The Messenger of Allah, may peace be upon him, commanded: Do not accumulate milk in the udders of camels and goats. So whoever buys this animal after tasriyah, then after milking, the buyer has the choice: if he likes, he keeps it; if he dislikes, he returns the animal and gives one sa' of dates. Tasriyah means to accumulate milk in the animal's udders so that its udders are full and it fetches a good price. This is deception with the buyer, so the buyer has the choice: if he wishes, he keeps it; if he wishes, he returns it and gives one sa' of dates in exchange for the milk he milked. This hadith is completely contrary to qiyas, because for compensation of any loss, the requirement of qiyas is that for things with equivalents, compensation is with an equivalent; for things with value, compensation is with value. But here in all cases one sa' of dates is obligatory, which is neither a formal equivalent nor a meaningful one, i.e., value. One sa' of dates cannot even be called value, because if it is value, it should be equal to the milk. Yet here, no matter how much milk was taken, one sa' of dates is obligatory. In any case, this hadith is absolutely contrary to qiyas, so we will abandon the hadith, and the sale will be concluded, and the buyer will not have the option to rescind the sale, because the option to return the sale is only in case there is a defect in the sold item, and here the sold item is sound and intact; only its fruit (milk) has decreased, and the disappearance of the fruit does not make the sold item non-existent. So if the fruit decreased, a fortiori the sale does not become void. Therefore, the buyer will not have the option to return. Imam Sahib's...
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage from Al-Faiz-ul-Hijaz discusses the Hanafi rule regarding the acceptance of khabar al-wahid (a report from a single narrator) when it contradicts qiyas (analogical reasoning). The text distinguishes between two types of narrators: (1) those who are known for their fiqh and ijtihad (the fuqaha among the Companions, such as Ubayy ibn Ka'b and Abu Darda'), and (2) those who are known for their reliability and precision but not for fiqh (like Abu Hurayra and Anas ibn Malik). For the first type, the Hanafi position is that their khabar al-wahid takes precedence over qiyas, even if it contradicts it. For the second type, if their report agrees with qiyas, both are accepted; if it contradicts qiyas, the report is abandoned due to necessity, and qiyas is followed. The passage then refutes Imam Malik's view that all khabar al-wahid contradicting qiyas should be abandoned. Malik argued that khabar al-wahid has multiple doubts (possibility of error, lying, non-establishment), while qiyas has only one doubt (mujtahid's error), so qiyas is preferable. The Hanafi response is that the origin of khabar al-wahid is certain (it is from the Prophet), while the origin of qiyas is inherently probabilistic (the determination of the effective cause). Thus, the certain origin is stronger. The example of the hadith of musarraah (tying udders) is given: Abu Hurayra narrated it, but he is not from the fuqaha, and the hadith contradicts qiyas. According to Hanafis, this hadith is not acted upon; the sale is valid without the option of return, because the animal is sound and only the milk (a separable benefit) is diminished. The compensation of one sa' of dates for the milk is also contrary to qiyas, which would require compensation by equivalent or value. Hence, the hadith is rejected.

Key Terms
خبر واحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by a single narrator that does not reach the level of tawatur.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that applies a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause (illa).
فقیہ (faqih): A person who has deep understanding of fiqh and is capable of ijtihad.
تصریہ (tasriyah): The practice of tying the udders of an animal to accumulate milk, thereby deceiving the buyer about its milk yield.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is the hadith of musarraah (tying udders) not acted upon?
A) Because it contradicts the Quran.
B) Because its narrator, Abu Hurayra, is not known for fiqh and the hadith contradicts qiyas.
C) Because it is a weak hadith (da'if).
D) Because qiyas cannot be overridden by any solitary report.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the preference between a solitary report and analogical reasoning depends primarily on the narrator's fiqh: faqih narrators' reports take precedence, while non-faqih narrators' reports are abandoned when they contradict qiyas.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
Hadith of Musarra: Non-Faqih Narrator and Qiyas
Usul dispute: non-faqih narrator's hadith vs qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle of preferring qiyas over a hadith narrated by a non-faqih, using the musarra example.

Core Idea
A non-faqih narrator's hadith is abandoned when it contradicts qiyas.

In Hanafi usul, not every authentic hadith is automatically acted upon. The narrator's understanding of fiqh matters. When a narrator lacks juristic depth, his transmission may be unreliable if it contradicts established analogical reasoning. The hadith of musarra (tying udders) is a classic case: Abu Huraira, a non-faqih narrator, reported a ruling that conflicts with qiyas. This lesson unpacks why the Hanafi school sets aside this hadith and what principle governs such conflicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrator and his fiqh status
The hadith is narrated by Abu Huraira. According to Hanafi classification, he is not considered a faqih (deep jurist). Understand why this matters: his riwaya bil ma'na (transmission by meaning) may be inaccurate.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between faqih and non-faqih narrators.
2
State the ruling of the hadith
The hadith gives the buyer an option to return the animal with a sa' of dates after discovering tasriya. Write down the exact ruling: buyer may keep or return plus sa' dates.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim.
3
Contrast with qiyas
Qiyas requires compensation proportional to the loss: like for like (mithli) or value for value (qimi). A fixed sa' of dates for any amount of milk violates this principle. Recognize the incompatibility.
This contradiction is the crux of the dispute.
4
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
Because the narrator is non-faqih and the hadith contradicts qiyas, the Hanafi school abandons the hadith. The sale remains valid without an option to return.
This reflects the hierarchy: qiyas (derived from Quran) is given priority over an ahad hadith from a non-faqih.

وذلك مثل حديث أبي هريرة:- غير فقيه راوي كي روايت جو قياس کے مخالف ہو اس کی مثال ابوہریرہ کی حدیث مُصَرَّاۃ ہے، وہ حدیث ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لا تصروا الابل والغنم فمن ابتاعها بعد ذلك فهو بخير النظرين بعد أن يحلبها أن رضيها أمسكها وان سخطها ردها و صاعا من تمر، (مسلم) رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ تم اونٹوں اور بکریوں کے تھنوں میں دودھ جمع نہ کرو، پس جس نے اس جانور کو خریدا تصریہ کے بعد ، تو اس کو دوہنے کے بعد مشتری کو اختیار ہے، پسند ہو تو رکھ لے اور نا پسند کرے تو وہ جانور واپس لوٹا دے اور ایک صاع کھجور بھی دیدے۔ تصریہ کہتے ہیں جانور کے تھنوں میں دودھ جمع کرنا، تاکہ اس کے تھن بھرے ہوئے ہوں اور اس کی قیمت اچھی ملے، یہ مشتری کے ساتھ دھوکہ ہے، اس لئے مشتری کو اختیار ہے، چاہے تو رکھ لے چاہے تو واپس کرے اور جو دودھ دوہا ہے اس کے بدلہ ایک صاع کھجور دیدے۔ یہ حدیث ہر طرح سے قیاس کے مخالف ہے، کیونکہ کسی نقصان کی تلافی کے لئے قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ ذوات الامثال میں مثل سے ضمان ہو، اور ذوات القیم میں قیمت سے ضمان ہو، اور یہاں ہر حال میں ایک صاع کھجور واجب ہے، جو دودھ کا نہ مثل صوری ہے نہ معنوی یعنی قیمت، ایک صاع کھجور کو قیمت بھی نہیں کہہ سکتے، کیونکہ اگر قیمت ہے تو دودھ کے برابر ہونی چاہیے، اور یہاں چاہے جتنا بھی دودھ نکالا ہو، ایک صاع تمر واجب ہے، بہر حال یہ حدیث قیاس کے بالکل مخالف ہے، لہذا حدیث کو چھوڑ دینگے اور بیع منعقد ہو جائے گی اور مشتری کو بیع فسخ کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ بیع کو واپس کرنے کا اختیار صرف اسی صورت میں ہوتا ہے جب مبیع میں عیب ہو اور یہاں مبیع صحیح سالم ہے، صرف اس کے ثمرہ (دودھ) میں کمی ہوئی ہے، اور ثمرہ کے معدوم ہونے سے مبیع معدوم نہیں ہوتی تو ثمرہ میں کمی سے بدرجہ اولی بیع معدوم نہ ہوگی لہذا مبیع کو واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا، امام صاحب کا مسلک یہی ہے۔ امام شافعی اور امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ تصریہ عیب ہے لہذا حدیث پر عمل کرتے ہوئے مشتری کو خیار عیب حاصل ہوگا، چاہے تو رکھ لے چاہے تو وہ جانور واپس کر دے اور بیع فسخ کر دے اور ایک صاع تمر دیدے۔
And that is like the hadith of Abu Huraira: an example of a non-faqih narrator's narration that contradicts qiyas is the hadith of musarra. It is the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not tie the udders of camels and sheep. Whoever buys such an animal after that has the choice after milking it: if he is pleased, he may keep it; if he is displeased, he may return it along with a sa' of dates.' (Muslim) The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) commanded not to collect milk in the udders of camels and goats. So whoever buys this animal after tasriya, then after milking, the buyer has an option: if he likes, he may keep it; if he dislikes, he may return the animal and give one sa' of dates. Tasriya means collecting milk in the animal's udder so that its udder appears full and its price is good. This is deception of the buyer, therefore the buyer has an option: if he wishes, he may keep it; if he wishes, he may return it and give one sa' of dates in exchange for the milk he milked. This hadith contradicts qiyas in every way, because to compensate for a loss, qiyas requires that in things of similar measure, compensation be with a like, and in things of value, compensation be with value. But here in every case one sa' of dates is obligatory, which is neither a like of milk nor a value. One cannot even call a sa' of dates a value, because if it were value, it would have to be equivalent to the milk. Here, regardless of how much milk was drawn, one sa' of dates is obligatory. In any case, this hadith completely contradicts qiyas, therefore we will abandon the hadith. The sale will be concluded, and the buyer will have no option to rescind the sale, because the option to return the sale exists only when the sold item has a defect. Here the sold item is sound and intact; only its produce (milk) has decreased. The disappearance of the produce does not cause the sold item to disappear, so a decrease in produce does not, a fortiori, cause the sale to disappear. Therefore, the buyer will not have the option to return. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik say that tasriya is a defect, therefore, acting upon the hadith, the buyer has the option of defect: if he wishes, he may keep it; if he wishes, he may return the animal, rescind the sale, and give one sa' of dates.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This is an usul dispute illustrating a key Hanafi principle: when a hadith transmitted by a non-faqih narrator contradicts qiyas (analogical reasoning), the Hanafi school abandons the hadith and upholds qiyas. The passage opens with the example of the hadith of musarra (tying udders) narrated by Abu Huraira (RA). The hadith gives the buyer an option to return the animal with a sa' of dates after discovering the deception. However, this ruling contradicts qiyas because qiyas requires compensation to be proportional (like for like or value for value), whereas the hadith prescribes a fixed sa' of dates regardless of the quantity of milk. The Hanafi reasoning is explained: a non-faqih narrator might have transmitted the meaning (riwaya bil ma'na) incorrectly due to lack of juristic understanding. Therefore, the hadith is set aside. The sale remains valid without an option to return, since the animal itself has no defect; only the milk (produce) is diminished. The text then contrasts the positions of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik, who consider tasriya a defect and thus grant the buyer khiyar al-ayb (option of defect) in accordance with the hadith. This shows the practical impact of usul principles on fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
مُصَرَّاة (musarra): An animal whose udder is tied to accumulate milk, deceiving the buyer into thinking it is a good milker.
راوٍ غير فقيه (rawin ghayr faqih): A narrator who lacks deep understanding (fiqh) of the religion, especially of legal rulings and their underlying rationale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the buyer of a musarra animal not given the option to return it?
A) Because the hadith is weak.
B) Because the narrator Abu Huraira is not a faqih, and the hadith contradicts qiyas.
C) Because the animal has no defect; the milk is not part of the sale.
D) Because the buyer agreed to the sale.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a hadith from a non-faqih narrator that contradicts qiyas is set aside, as seen in the case of musarra.

Ruling on the Hadith of a Majhul Narrator
Stating the conditions for accepting hadith of a majhul narrator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a hadith from a majhul narrator is accepted in the Hanafi school and apply these conditions to classify a narrator.

Core Idea
A majhul narrator's hadith is accepted if the Salaf narrated from him and attested to authenticity; otherwise it may be permissible or rejected.

In Hanafi usul, not all unknown narrators are treated equally. This rule from al-Husami explains how the stance of the Salaf determines the legal weight of a majhul narrator's hadith. Understanding these categories is essential for evaluating ahad hadith in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Define majhul narrator
Identify a narrator known only by one or two hadith; not recognized for widespread transmission or justice.
Examples given: Wabisa ibn Ma'bad and Salama ibn al-Muhabbiq.
2
Identify three main scenarios
Based on the Salaf's reaction: (a) narrated and attested or remained silent, (b) only rejected, (c) no mention.
A sub-scenario of (a) includes disagreement among the Salaf despite thiqat narrating.
3
Apply the condition for acceptance
If the Salaf narrated and attested or remained silent, the hadith is accepted like that of a known narrator.
Even if some Salaf disagree, as long as thiqat narrated, Hanafis accept it.
4
Apply the condition for rejection
If the Salaf only rejected, the hadith is mustankar and not accepted.
5
Apply the intermediate scenario
If the Salaf did not mention the narrator at all, acting upon his hadith is permissible but not obligatory, due to default justice in that era.
In later times, due to prevalence of sin, such a hadith is not permissible to act upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَ الرَّاوِيُّ مَجْهُولًا لَا يَعْرَفُ إِلَّا بِحَدِيثِ رَوَاهُ أَوْ بِحَدِيْثَيْنِ مِثْلُ وَابِصَةَ بْنِ مَعْبَدٍ وَسَلْمَةَ بْنِ الْمُحَبّقِ فَإِنْ رَوَى عَنْهُ السَّلَفْ وَشَهِدُوْا بِصِحَتِهِ أَوْ سَكَتُوا الطَّعْن صَارَ حَدِيْثُهُ مِثْلُ حَدِيْثِ الْمَعْرُوْفِ وَإِنْ أُخْتُلِفَ فِيْهِ مَعْ نَقْلِ الثَّقَاتِ عَنْهُ فَكَذَلِكَ عِنْدَنَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَظْهَرُ مِنَ السَّلَفِ إِلَّا الرَّدُّ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ حَدِيثُهُ وَصَارَ مُسْتَنْكَرًا وَانْ كَانَ لَمْ يَظْهَرُ حَدِيثُهُ فِي السَّلَفِ وَلَمْ يُقَابِلُ بِرَدٍ وَلَا قَبُولٍ لَمْ يَجِبِ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ لَكِنَّ الْعَمَلَ بِهِ جَائِزَ لِاَنَ الْعَدَالَةَ أَصْلٌ فِي ذَلِكَ الزَّمَانِ حَتَّى أَنَّ رِوَايَةَ مِثْلِ هَذَا الْمَجْهُولِ فِي زَمَانِنَا لَا يَحِلُّ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ لِظُهُورِ الْفِسْقِ ترجمہ: اور اگر راوی مجہول ہے نہیں جانا جاتا ہے مگر ایک حدیث کے ساتھ جس کو اس نے روایت کیا ہے یا دو حدیثوں کے ساتھ جیسے وابصہ بن معبد اور سلمہ بن محیق، پس اگر اس سے سلف نے روایت کی ہو اور اس کی صحت کی شہادت دی ہو یا طعن سے سکوت کیا ہو، تو اس کی حدیث معروف کی حدیث کی طرح ہوگی، اور اگر اس میں اختلاف کیا گیا اس سے ثقات کے نقل کرنے کے ساتھ تو ایسا ہی ہے ہمارے نزدیک، اور اگر نہ ظاہر ہو سلف سے مگر رد تو اس کی حدیث قبول نہیں کی جائے گی اور وہ مستنکر ہوگی، اور اگر اس کی حدیث سلف میں ظاہر نہ ہوئی ہو اور نہ سامنا کیا ہو کسی نے نہ رد کے ساتھ، نہ قبول کے ساتھ تو اس پر عمل واجب نہیں ہے لیکن اس پر عمل جائز ہے، اس لئے کہ عدالت اصل ہے اس زمانے میں، یہاں تک کہ اس مجہول راوی کے مثل کی روایت ہمارے زمانے میں حلال نہیں ہے اس پر عمل کرنا فسق کے ظاہر ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح:- اگر کوئی راوی مجہول ہو، مجہول النسب نہیں بلکہ روایت حدیث اور عدالت میں مجہول ہو، اس طرح کہ ایک دو حدیث کے علاوہ اس کی کوئی حدیث نہیں ہے، بس انہی ایک دو روایتوں سے وہ معروف ہے جیسے وابصہ بن مَعْبُدُ اور سلمہ بن محبق، تو اس کی پانچ قسمیں ہیں۔ (1) پہلی قسم یہ ہے کہ اس مجهول راوی سے سلف یعنی ان حضرات صحابہ نے روایت کی ہو جو عدالت اور فقہ کے ساتھ معروف ہیں، اور اس کی حدیث کی صحت کی شہادت دی ہو۔
And if the narrator is majhul (unknown), not known except by a hadith he narrated or by two hadith, like Wabisa ibn Ma'bad and Salama ibn al-Muhabbiq: if the Salaf narrated from him and testified to its authenticity or remained silent regarding criticism, then his hadith becomes like the hadith of a known narrator. And if there is disagreement about him even though trustworthy narrators have narrated from him, then it is similarly (accepted) according to us. And if nothing appears from the Salaf except rejection, then his hadith is not accepted and it becomes mustankar (rejected). And if his hadith did not appear among the Salaf and was not met with either rejection or acceptance, then acting upon it is not obligatory, but acting upon it is permissible, because justice (adala) was the norm at that time, to the extent that narrating like this majhul in our time, acting upon it is not permissible due to the prevalence of sin. Translation: And if the narrator is majhul, not known except by one hadith he narrated or by two hadith, such as Wabisa ibn Ma'bad and Salama ibn al-Muhabbiq. Then if the Salaf narrated from him and testified to its authenticity or remained silent regarding criticism, then his hadith becomes like the hadith of a known narrator. And if there is disagreement about him even though trustworthy narrators have narrated from him, then similarly it is (accepted) according to us. And if nothing appears from the Salaf except rejection, then his hadith is not accepted and it becomes mustankar (rejected). And if his hadith did not appear among the Salaf and was not met with either rejection or acceptance, then acting upon it is not obligatory, but acting upon it is permissible, because justice was the norm at that time, to the extent that narrating like this majhul in our time, acting upon it is not permissible due to the prevalence of sin. Explanation: If a narrator is majhul, not unknown in lineage but unknown in hadith narration and justice, such that he is only known by one or two hadith, like Wabisa ibn Ma'bad and Salama ibn al-Muhabbiq, then there are five categories. (1) The first category is that the Salaf, meaning the Companions who are known for justice and fiqh, narrated from this majhul narrator and testified to the authenticity of his hadith.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This is an usul rule defining the treatment of a majhul (unknown) narrator. The text defines a majhul narrator as one who is not recognized except through one or two hadith that he narrated. It then outlines the conditions for accepting his narrations based on the stance of the Salaf (early Muslims, especially Companions). The key principle is that if the Salaf narrated from him and either attested to the authenticity of his hadith or remained silent regarding any criticism, then his hadith is treated like that of a known narrator. Even if there is disagreement among the Salaf about him, the Hanafi school still accepts it as long as trustworthy narrators have narrated from him. However, if the Salaf explicitly rejected his hadith, it is not accepted and is deemed mustankar (rejected). If the Salaf neither accepted nor rejected it (i.e., his hadith was not known among them), then acting upon it is not obligatory but permissible. The rationale is that in the early period, the default assumption was that narrators were just (adala). In later times, due to the prevalence of sin, such a narration is not permissible to act upon. The explanation (tashrih) adds that the narrator is not majhul an-nasab (unknown in lineage) but majhul in terms of narration and justice. It mentions five categories but only details the first: when the Salaf (notably Companions known for justice and fiqh) narrated from him and testified to the authenticity of his hadith.

Key Terms
مجهول (majhul): A narrator not known except through one or two hadith he narrated; unknown in terms of widespread recognition and justice.
السلف (al-Salaf): The early righteous predecessors, especially the Companions and early scholars known for justice and fiqh.
مستنكر (mustankar): A hadith that is rejected because the Salaf explicitly rejected its narrator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a hadith from a majhul narrator if the Salaf neither accepted nor rejected it?
A) It is rejected outright.
B) Acting upon it is obligatory.
C) Acting upon it is permissible but not obligatory.
D) It is considered mustankar.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a majhul narrator's hadith depends on the Salaf's engagement: narrated and attested → accepted; rejected → mustankar; not mentioned → permissible.

Categories of Majhul Narrator's Hadith in Hanafi Usul
Categories of majhul narrator's hadith and legal effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a hadith from a majhul narrator according to Hanafi usul categories and determine whether it is accepted or rejected based on the Salaf's treatment.

Core Idea
A majhul narrator's hadith is not automatically rejected: its fate depends on how the Salaf treated it.

In Hanafi usul, the reliability of a narrator is not always known. When a narrator is majhul (unknown) except for one or two hadiths, scholars differ on accepting their narrations. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, which classifies such hadith into five categories based on the Salaf's response. Understanding these categories helps you resolve apparent conflicts between hadith and qiyas, as illustrated by the famous case of Ma'qil ibn Sinan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrator's status
First, determine if the narrator is majhul: known only by one or two hadiths, and not well-known for reliability. Examples in the text: Wabisah ibn Ma'bad and Salamah ibn al-Muhabbiq.
2
Observe the Salaf's response
Examine how the early generation (Companions) interacted with this narrator's hadith: did they narrate from him, remain silent, disagree, reject, or have no reaction? Each response leads to a different ruling.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
Based on the Salaf's response, apply the rule: acceptance if the Salaf narrated or remained silent (categories 1-2); acceptance even if disagreement, as long as reliable imams transmitted (category 3); rejection if the Salaf unanimously rejected (category 4); permissibility without obligation if no reaction (category 5).
The rule is built on the principle that integrity was the norm in the early era.
4
Analyze the dispute example
Work through the case of Ma'qil ibn Sinan: a majhul narrator whose hadith on mahr was accepted by Ibn Mas'ud but rejected by Ali based on qiyas. The Hanafis accept the hadith over qiyas because reliable imams transmitted it and the Salaf (Ibn Mas'ud) accepted it.
This shows the practical thamarah al-khilaf (consequence of difference).
5
Evaluate the hierarchy
Note that in Hanafi usul, a hadith from a majhul narrator, if accepted through these categories, takes precedence over qiyas. This is a key feature of Hanafi methodology: privileging textual evidence (even from weak narrators) when supported by the Salaf's practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بِصِحَتِهِ أَوْ سَكَتُوا الطَّعْن صَارَ حَدِيْثُهُ مِثْلُ حَدِيْثِ الْمَعْرُوْفِ وَإِنْ أُخْتُلِفَ فِيْهِ مَعَ نَقْلِ الثَّقَاتِ عَنْهُ فَكَذَلِكَ عِنْدَنَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَظْهَرُ مِنَ السَّلَفِ إِلَّا الرَّدُّ لَمْ يُقْبَلْ حَدِيثُهُ وَصَارَ مُسْتَنْكَرًا وَانْ كَانَ لَمْ يَظْهَرُ حَدِيثُهُ فِي السَّلَفِ وَلَمْ يُقَابِلُ بِرَةٍ وَلَا قَبُولٍ لَمْ يَجِبِ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ لَكِنَّ الْعَمَلَ بِهِ جَائِزَ لِاَنَ الْعَدَ الَةَ أَصْلُّ فِي ذَلِكَ الزَّمَانِ حَتَّى أَنَّ رِوَايَةَ مِثْلِ هَذَا الْمَجْهُولِ فِي زَمَانِنَا لَا يَحِلُّ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ لِظُهُورِ الْفِسْقِ ترجمہ: اور اگر راوی مجہول ہے نہیں جانا جاتا ہے مگر ایک حدیث کے ساتھ جس کو اس نے روایت کیا ہے یا دو حدیثوں کے ساتھ جیسے وابصہ بن معبد اور سلمہ بن محیق ، پس اگر اس سے سلف نے روایت کی ہو اور اس کی صحت کی شہادت دی ہو یا طعن سے سکوت کیا ہو ، تو اس کی حدیث معروف کی حدیث کی طرح ہوگی ، اور اگر اس میں اختلاف کیا گیا اس سے ثقات کے نقل کرنے کے ساتھ تو ایسا ہی ہے ہمارے نزدیک ، اور اگر نہ ظاہر ہوسلف سے مگر رد تو اس کی حدیث قبول نہیں کی جائے گی اور وہ مستنکر ہوگی ، اور اگر اس کی حدیث سلف میں ظاہر نہ ہوئی ہو اور نہ سامنا کیا ہوکسی نے نہ رد کے ساتھ ، نہ قبول کے ساتھ تو اس پر عمل واجب نہیں ہے لیکن اس پر عمل جائز ہے، اس لئے کہ عدالت اصل ہے اس زمانے میں ، یہاں تک کہ اُس مجہول راوی کے مثل کی روایت ہمارے زمانے میں حلال نہیں ہے اس پر عمل کرنا فسق کے ظاہر ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح:- اگر کوئی راوی مجہول ہو، مجہول النسب نہیں بلکہ روایت حدیث اور عدالت میں مجہول ہو، اس طرح کہ ایک دو حدیث کے علاوہ اس کی کوئی حدیث نہیں ہے، بس انہی ایک دو روایتوں سے وہ معروف ہے جیسے وابصہ بن مَعْبُدُ اور سلمہ بن محبق ، تو اس کی پانچ قسمیں ہیں۔ (1) پہلی قسم یہ ہے کہ اس مجہول راوی سے سلف یعنی ان حضرات صحابہ نے روایت کی ہو جو عدالت اور فقہ کے ساتھ معروف ہیں، اور اس کی حدیث کی صحت کی شہادت دی ہو۔ (۲) دوسری قسم یہ ہے کہ اس مجہول راوی کی روایت جب سلف کو پہنچی تو انہوں نے اس پر طعن نہ کیا ہو بلکہ سکوت کیا ہو، ان دونوں قسموں میں مجہول راوی کی روایت اس راوی کی روایت کی طرح قبول کی جائے گی جو عدالت، ضبط اور فقہ میں معروف ہے، اور اس کو قیاس پر مقدم کیا جائے گا۔ (۳) تیسری قسم یہ ہے کہ اس مجہول راوی کی حدیث میں سلف (صحابہ ) نے اختلاف کیا ہو، ، بعض صحابہ نے قبول کیا ہو اور بعض نے اس کی حدیث کو رد کر دیا ہو، اس کے باوجود ائمہ ثقات نے اس کی حدیث کو نقل کیا ہو تو ہمارے نزدیک یہ حدیث معروف راوی کی حدیث کی طرح قابل قبول ہوگی ، اور قیاس پر مقدم ہوگی۔اس کی مثال عبد اللہ بن مسعود سے پوچھا گیا کہ ایک آدمی نے ایک عورت سے نکاح کیا اور اس کا مہر ذکر نہیں کیا اور نہ دخول کیا کہ اس سے پہلے ہی اس کا انتقال ہو گیا، تو اس عورت کے بارے میں کیا حکم ہے؟ تو ابن مسعود اس مسئلہ میں ایک مہینہ تک غور و فکر کرتے رہے، اور سائل مسلسل چکر لگا تارہا، بالاخر ابن مسعود نے فرمایا کہ میں نے حضور سلائی کی تم سے اس سلسلہ میں کچھ نہیں سنا ہے، اپنی رائے سے اجتہاد کرتا ہوں اگر درست ہو تو اللہ اور اس کے رسول کی طرف سے ہے اور اگر خطا ہو تو میری اور شیطان کی طرف سے ہے، میں اس عورت کے لئے مہر مثل سمجھتا ہوں ، نہ اس سے کم نہ زیادہ ، اور عدت بھی واجب ہے اور اس کے لئے میراث بھی ہوگی ، یہ جواب سن کر معقل بن سنان کھڑے ہوئے اور کہا کہ ہمارے اندر ایک عورت ہے ، ہلال بن مرہ کی بیوی بردع بنت واشق ، حضور صل للہ یہ تم نے اس کے لئے یہی فیصلہ کیا تھا، تو ابن مسعود اس موافقت سے اتنے خوش ہوئے کہ اس سے پہلے کبھی خوش نہیں ہوئے تھے۔ معقل بن سنان ( جو مجہول مسعوداس راوی ہے ) کی روایت کو ابن مسعود نے قبول کیا اور حضرت علی نے اس کو رد کر دیا اور قیاس پر عمل کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ اس عورت کے لئے میراث ہے، عدت بھی واجب ہے مگر مہر نہیں ہے، قیاس کی علت یہ ہے کہ معقود علیہ یعنی عورت کی ملک بضع دخول نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے صحیح سالم عورت کی طرف لوٹ آئی ، اور مہر ملک بضع کے مقابلہ میں ہوتا ہے، لہذا یہ عورت مہر کی مستحق نہ ہوگی۔ یہ مسئلہ ایسا ہی ہے جیسے کوئی آدمی بیوی کو قبل الدخول طلاق دیدے اور مہر طے نہ کیا ہو، تو وہ عورت مہر کی مستحق نہیں ہوتی ، حضرت امام شافعی نے حضرت علی کے قیاس پر عمل کیا اور ہم نے اس حدیث پر عمل کیا، کیونکہ اس حدیث کو ثقہ راویوں نے روایت کیا ہے، قرن اول میں ابن مسعود، اور ان کے بعد علقمہ،مسروق اور حسن وغیرہ نیز یہ حدیث قیاس کے مطابق بھی ہے کیونکہ موت جس طرح مہر مسٹی کو مو کر کر دیتی ہے، ایسے ہی مہر مثل کو بھی مؤکد کر دیتی ہے، لہذا مہر مثل کی مستحق ہوگی۔ (۴) چوتھی قسم یہ ہے کہ اس مجہول راوی کی حدیث کو سلف نے رد کر دیا ہو، تو وہ حدیث قابل قبول نہ ہوگی ، اس حدیث کو مستنکر کہا جائے گا ، ایسی حدیث اگر قیاس کے مخالف ہو تو قابل عمل نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ جب صحابہ نے اس حدیث
And if the narrator is unknown, not known except by a hadith he narrated or two hadiths, like Wabisah ibn Ma'bad and Salamah ibn al-Muhabbiq. Then if the Salaf narrated from him and testified to its authenticity, or remained silent about criticism, his hadith becomes like the hadith of a known narrator. And if there is disagreement about him, along with reliable narrators transmitting from him, then likewise according to us. And if nothing appears from the Salaf except rejection, his hadith is not accepted and becomes rejected (mustankar). And if his hadith did not appear among the Salaf and was not met with rejection nor acceptance, acting upon it is not obligatory but acting upon it is permissible, because integrity (adalah) was the norm in that time, to the extent that the narration of someone like this unknown narrator in our time, acting upon it is not permissible due to the prevalence of transgression. Translation: And if the narrator is unknown, not known except by one hadith that he narrated or two hadiths, like Wabisah ibn Ma'bad and Salamah ibn al-Muhabbiq. Then if the Salaf narrated from him and testified to its authenticity, or remained silent about criticism, his hadith will be like the hadith of a known narrator. And if there is disagreement about him along with reliable narrators transmitting from him, then likewise according to us. And if nothing appears from the Salaf except rejection, his hadith will not be accepted and it will be considered rejected (mustankar). And if his hadith did not appear among the Salaf and was not met with rejection nor acceptance, acting upon it is not obligatory but acting upon it is permissible, because integrity was the norm in that time, to the extent that the narration of someone like this unknown narrator in our time, acting upon it is not permissible due to the prevalence of transgression. Commentary: If a narrator is unknown, not unknown in lineage but unknown in hadith narration and integrity, such that he has no hadith except one or two, and he is known only by those one or two narrations, like Wabisah ibn Ma'bad and Salamah ibn al-Muhabbiq, then he has five categories. (1) The first category is that the Salaf, i.e., the Companions who are known for integrity and jurisprudence, narrated from this unknown narrator and testified to the authenticity of his hadith. (2) The second category is that when the narration of this unknown narrator reached the Salaf, they did not criticize it but remained silent. In both these categories, the narration of the unknown narrator will be accepted like the narration of a narrator known for integrity, precision, and jurisprudence, and it will be given precedence over qiyas. (3) The third category is that the Salaf (Companions) disagreed about the hadith of this unknown narrator, some Companions accepted it and some rejected it, yet the reliable imams transmitted his hadith. According to us, this hadith will be acceptable like the hadith of a known narrator and will be given precedence over qiyas. An example: Abdullah ibn Mas'ud was asked about a man who married a woman without mentioning her mahr and died before consummation. What is the ruling regarding the woman? Ibn Mas'ud reflected on the issue for a month, the questioner kept coming around. Finally, Ibn Mas'ud said: I have not heard anything from the Prophet ﷺ regarding this. I will make ijtihad based on my opinion; if it is correct, it is from Allah and His Messenger, and if it is wrong, it is from me and Satan. I hold that she is entitled to mahr al-mithl, not less nor more, and she must observe 'iddah and is entitled to inheritance. Hearing this, Ma'qil ibn Sinan stood up and said: Among us there is a woman, the wife of Hilal ibn Murrah, Bard'a bint Washiq, for whom the Prophet ﷺ made the same ruling. Ibn Mas'ud was so pleased with this agreement that he had never been so pleased before. The narration of Ma'qil ibn Sinan (who is the unknown narrator) was accepted by Ibn Mas'ud, but Ali rejected it and acted on qiyas, saying: This woman is entitled to inheritance and 'iddah, but no mahr, because the object of contract (the woman's right to sexual relations) returned intact to the woman due to non-consummation, and mahr is given in exchange for the right to sexual relations, so this woman is not entitled to mahr. This case is like a man who divorces his wife before consummation without fixing a mahr; she is not entitled to mahr. Imam al-Shafi'i acted on Ali's qiyas, while we acted on this hadith, because this hadith was narrated by trustworthy narrators: in the first generation, Ibn Mas'ud, and after him, 'Alqamah, Masruq, Hasan, etc. Also, this hadith is consistent with qiyas because just as death confirms the named mahr, similarly it confirms mahr al-mithl, so she is entitled to mahr al-mithl. (4) The fourth category is that the hadith of this unknown narrator was rejected by the Salaf; then that hadith will not be acceptable, it will be called mustankar (rejected). Such a hadith, if it opposes qiyas, will not be acted upon, because when the Companions rejected this hadith...
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a usul rule regarding the acceptance of hadith from a majhul (unknown) narrator. The author explains the categories based on the treatment of the narrator's hadith by the Salaf (early generations, particularly the Companions). The rule is that a majhul narrator is one known only by one or two hadiths he narrated. Five categories are listed, but only four are detailed in the visible text:

(1) If the Salaf narrated from him and testified to the authenticity of his hadith, it is accepted like that of a known narrator. (2) If the Salaf remained silent (did not criticize) after hearing his narration, it is also accepted. (3) If the Salaf disagreed (some accepted, some rejected) but reliable imams transmitted his hadith, the Hanafi position is that it is still accepted and takes precedence over qiyas. The example given is the case of a marriage without specified mahr where the husband died before consummation. Ibn Mas'ud initially gave an opinion based on his own ijtihad (mahr al-mithl, 'iddah, inheritance). Then Ma'qil bin Sinan (a majhul narrator) reported that the Prophet had ruled similarly. Ibn Mas'ud accepted this hadith, while Ali rejected it based on qiyas (no mahr because the right to sexual relations returned to the woman). The Hanafis follow Ibn Mas'ud's acceptance because the hadith was transmitted by trustworthy narrators (Ibn Mas'ud, 'Alqamah, etc.) and also because they find it consistent with qiyas: just as death confirms the named mahr, it confirms mahr al-mithl. Imam al-Shafi'i followed Ali's qiyas. (4) If the Salaf unanimously rejected the hadith, it is not accepted and is called mustankar; if it opposes qiyas, it is not acted upon. The passage cuts off while explaining the reasoning.

The passage also discusses a fifth category (not fully given): if the hadith was neither accepted nor rejected by the Salaf, acting upon it is not obligatory but permissible, because in that early time people were generally upright. However, in later times due to prevalence of transgression, acting upon such a narration is not permissible.

The lesson underscores the Hanafi methodology: hadith from a majhul narrator can be elevated to the level of a known narrator if the Salaf transmitted it or remained silent, or even if there is dispute among them but reliable transmitters exist. The authority weight here is from the later Hanafi usul tradition as this is a commentary on Al-Husami.

Key Terms
مجہول (majhul): A narrator who is unknown in terms of his reliability and hadith transmission, known only by one or two hadiths.
سلف (salaf): The early generations, primarily the Companions and those who followed them, known for their integrity and fiqh.
مستنکر (mustankar): A hadith that is rejected and not acted upon, specifically when the Salaf rejected it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul rule in this lesson, what is the ruling on a hadith from a majhul narrator if the Salaf remained silent (did not criticize) when it reached them?
A) The hadith is rejected.
B) The hadith is accepted like a known narrator's hadith and given precedence over qiyas.
C) The hadith is accepted only if it does not contradict qiyas.
D) The hadith is permissible to act upon but not obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a majhul narrator's hadith in Hanafi usul hinges on the treatment of the Salaf: if they narrated, remained silent, or even disagreed but reliable imams transmitted it, the hadith is accepted and takes precedence over qiyas.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
Accepting Unknown Narrator's Hadith: Silent or Divided Salaf
Explains acceptance of unknown narrator's hadith when Salaf are silent or divided

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two categories of unknown narrator acceptance in Hanafi usul and apply the rule to the mahr mithl case, distinguishing between Hanafi and Shafi'i positions.

Core Idea
An unknown narrator's hadith is accepted when the Salaf do not reject it, and it precedes qiyas.

This passage from Al-Husami presents two scenarios where the Hadith of a majhool (unknown) narrator is accepted in Hanafi usul: when the Salaf (early authorities) remain silent about it, or when they differ but some accept it. The famous example of the mahr mithl dispute illustrates how a solitary hadith was upheld over qiyas, and how this led to a difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. Understanding these categories refines your ability to evaluate hadith-based rulings in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two divisions
Extract the conditions under which a majhool narrator's hadith is accepted: (a) the Salaf remained silent, neither accepting nor criticizing; (b) the Salaf differed, some accepting and some rejecting, but reliable imams transmitted it. In both, the hadith is treated like that of a known trustworthy narrator.
These are the second and third of five categories in Hanafi usul.
2
Note the authority of the hadith
Once accepted, the hadith is given precedence over qiyas (analogical reasoning). This is a key Hanafi principle: a transmitted text, even from a majhool narrator under these conditions, outweighs human reasoning.
This preference is not absolute; it applies only when the narrator's identity is unknown but the chain and content are otherwise sound.
3
Examine the illustrative case
Work through the mahr mithl example: a man dies after marriage without consummation and without specifying mahr. Ibn Mas'ud first used ijtihad, then accepted Ma'qil ibn Sinan's hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him). Ali rejected the hadith and used qiyas. The Hanafi school follows the hadith.
Ma'qil ibn Sinan is considered majhool, but the hadith was transmitted by trustworthy successors.
4
Analyze the qiyas dispute
Compare the two analogies: Hanafi qiyas says death confirms mahr mithl just as it confirms specified mahr; Shafi'i qiyas analogizes to divorce before consummation, where no mahr is due. The Hanafi response: death strengthens the contract, unlike divorce.
The dispute shows how different analogical bases lead to different rulings, but here the hadith resolved it for the Hanafis.

کہا کہ ہمارے اندر ایک عورت ہے، ہلال بن مرہ کی بیوی بردع بنت واشق، حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس کے لئے یہی فیصلہ کیا تھا، تو ابن مسعود اس موافقت سے اتنے خوش ہوئے کہ اس سے پہلے کبھی خوش نہیں ہوئے تھے۔ معقل بن سنان (جو مجہول راوی ہے) کی روایت کو ابن مسعود نے قبول کیا اور حضرت علی نے اس کو رد کر دیا اور قیاس پر عمل کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ اس عورت کے لئے میراث ہے، عدت بھی واجب ہے مگر مہر نہیں ہے، قیاس کی علت یہ ہے کہ معقود علیہ یعنی عورت کی ملک بضع دخول نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے صحیح سالم عورت کی طرف لوٹ آئی، اور مہر ملک بضع کے مقابلہ میں ہوتا ہے، لہذا یہ عورت مہر کی مستحق نہ ہوگی۔ یہ مسئلہ ایسا ہی ہے جیسے کوئی آدمی بیوی کو قبل الدخول طلاق دیدے اور مہر طے نہ کیا ہو، تو وہ عورت مہر کی مستحق نہیں ہوتی، حضرت امام شافعی نے حضرت علی کے قیاس پر عمل کیا اور ہم نے اس حدیث پر عمل کیا، کیونکہ اس حدیث کو ثقہ راویوں نے روایت کیا ہے، قرن اول میں ابن مسعود، اور ان کے بعد علقمہ، مسروق اور حسن وغیرہ نیز یہ حدیث قیاس کے مطابق بھی ہے کیونکہ موت جس طرح مہر مسما کو مؤکد کر دیتی ہے، ایسے ہی مہر مثل کو بھی مؤکد کر دیتی ہے، لہذا مہر مثل کی مستحق ہوگی۔
(2) The second division is that when the narration of this unknown narrator reached the Salaf, they did not criticize it but remained silent. In both these divisions, the narration of an unknown narrator will be accepted like the narration of a narrator who is known for justice, precision and jurisprudence, and it will be given precedence over qiyas. (3) The third division is that the Salaf (Companions) differed about the hadith of this unknown narrator: some Companions accepted it and some rejected his hadith, yet reliable imams transmitted his hadith, then in our view this hadith will be acceptable like the hadith of a known narrator and will be given precedence over qiyas. An example: Abdullah ibn Mas'ud was asked about a man who married a woman without mentioning her mahr and died before consummation. What is the ruling? Ibn Mas'ud pondered for a month, then said: I have not heard anything from the Prophet (peace be upon him) about this; I will give my own opinion. If correct, it is from Allah and His Messenger; if wrong, it is from me and Satan. I think she deserves the mahr mithl, neither less nor more, and she must observe 'iddah and will inherit. Hearing this, Ma'qil ibn Sinan stood up and said: Among us is a woman, the wife of Hilal ibn Murra, Barid bint Washiq, for whom the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave this same verdict. Ibn Mas'ud was so pleased that he had never been so pleased. The narration of Ma'qil ibn Sinan (an unknown narrator) was accepted by Ibn Mas'ud, but Ali rejected it, acting on qiyas: she inherits and observes 'iddah, but no mahr. The cause of qiyas is that the object of contract, i.e., the woman's right to sexual enjoyment returns intact because of no consummation, and mahr is in exchange for that right, so she does not deserve mahr. This case is like a man divorcing his wife before consummation without fixing mahr: she is not entitled to mahr. Imam al-Shafi'i followed Ali's qiyas, but we follow this hadith, because it was transmitted by trustworthy narrators in the first generation (Ibn Mas'ud, then 'Alqamah, Masruq, Hasan, etc.) and also because this hadith is in accordance with qiyas: just as death confirms the specified mahr, so too it confirms the mahr mithl. Therefore she deserves the mahr mithl.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the acceptance of hadith from an unknown narrator (majhool rawi). The author outlines the second and third of five categories. In the second category, if the Salaf (Companions and early scholars) neither criticized nor accepted a hadith but remained silent, the unknown narrator's hadith is fully accepted and given precedence over qiyas. In the third category, if the Salaf differed—some accepting and some rejecting—the hadith is still accepted according to the Hanafi school, provided reliable imams transmitted it. The key point is that the hadith is treated like that of a known trustworthy narrator and preferred over qiyas. The author then provides the famous example of the 'mahr mithl' case: Abdullah ibn Mas'ud initially relied on his own reasoning (ijtihad) but later accepted Ma'qil ibn Sinan's hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him). The hadith was opposed by Ali, who used qiyas (analogy) to argue for no mahr, similar to the case of pre-consummation divorce. Imam al-Shafi'i followed Ali's qiyas. However, the Hanafi school follows the hadith, arguing that it is both reliably transmitted and in harmony with a proper analogy: just as death confirms the mahr musamma (specified mahr), it confirms mahr mithl (the mahr of her peers) because death makes the marriage final. Thus, the woman is entitled to mahr mithl, 'iddah, and inheritance.

Key Terms
مجہول راوی (majhool rawi): An unknown narrator whose identity or reliability is not established.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that extends a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause (illah).
مہر مثل (mahr mithl): The mahr that is customary for a woman of her status, used when no mahr was specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, what is the status of a hadith from a majhool narrator if the Salaf were divided about it (some accepted, some rejected) but reliable imams transmitted it?
A) It is rejected because of the narrator's unknown status.
B) It is accepted and given precedence over qiyas.
C) It is accepted only if it agrees with qiyas.
D) It is accepted only if the majority of Salaf accepted it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a hadith from a majhool narrator is accepted when the Salaf are silent or divided (with reliable transmission), and it takes precedence over qiyas, as illustrated by the mahr mithl case.

Mustankir Hadith: When the Salaf Reject Unanimously
Explains hadith of unknown narrator when Salaf unanimously reject it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a hadith is classified as mustankir and apply the Hanafi rule that such a hadith is not acted upon if it contradicts qiyas.

Core Idea
A hadith rejected by the entire Salaf (mustankir) has no independent legal weight; it may only support qiyas, never override it.

In Hanafi usul, not every hadith from an unknown narrator is automatically rejected. The fourth category is when the Salaf (Companions) have unanimously rejected it. This creates a strong presumption against the hadith, known as mustankir. The famous case of Fatima bint Qais shows how Umar's rejection, met with silent consensus, formed ijma that the hadith contradicts the Quran. This lesson unpacks the rule and its practical implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for mustankir
The hadith must be narrated by an unknown narrator (majhul) and the Salaf (Companions) must have unanimously rejected it. This is distinct from a hadith rejected by only some Companions.
Unanimity is key; individual rejection does not constitute mustankir.
2
Understand the primary consequence
If the mustankir hadith contradicts qiyas, it is not acted upon. The rejection by Salaf indicates that the narrator is suspected of lying, so the hadith is not established from the Prophet.
Qiyas here means reasoning based on the Quran and Sunnah, not mere opinion.
3
Analyze the example of Fatima bint Qais
Fatima reported that the Prophet said a triple divorcée gets no housing or maintenance. Umar rejected this in a gathering of Companions, citing the Quranic verse 'Do not turn them out of their houses' (65:1). No Companion objected, forming ijma.
The Quranic verse is qati' al-thubut and qati' al-dalalah, so it overrides a zanni hadith.
4
Recognize the role of ijma
The Companions' silent approval of Umar's rejection constitutes ijma, which is an independent proof that the hadith is mustankir. This ijma is itself a dalil for the ruling.
Hanafis accept ijma al-sahabi as a source of law.
5
Apply the exception: when mustankir can be used
If the mustankir hadith agrees with qiyas, it may be acted upon, but the legal authority comes from the qiyas, not the hadith. The hadith only serves as a supporting evidence (mu'ayyid).
This prevents the mustankir from being used as an independent source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴) چوتھی قسم یہ ہے کہ اس مجہول راوی کی حدیث کو سلف نے رد کر دیا ہو، تو وہ حدیث قابل قبول نہ ہوگی، اس حدیث کو مستنکر کہا جائے گا، ایسی حدیث اگر قیاس کے مخالف ہو تو قابل عمل نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ جب صحابہ نے اس حدیث کو رد کر دیا اور اس پر عمل نہیں کیا ہے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ راوی متہم بالکذب ہے، اور یہ حدیث حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے ثابت نہیں ہے، ورنہ صحابہ اس کو قبول کرتے، اس چوتھی قسم میں موضوع کی بہ نسبت کذب کا احتمال کم ہوتا ہے۔ اس کی مثال حضرت فاطمہ بنت قیس (جو مجہول راویہ ہے) کی حدیث، انہوں نے کہا کہ مجھے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانہ میں میرے شوہر نے تین طلاق دی تو رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا "لا سكنى لك ولا نفقة"، مگر جب حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ کے پاس یہ حدیث پہنچی، تو آپ نے صحابہ کے مجمع میں فرمایا کہ ہم ایک عورت کی بات پر کتاب وسنت کو نہیں چھوڑیں گے، کیونکہ کتاب اللہ میں ہے، "لا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن" یعنی عدت ونفقہ ہوگا، صحابہ میں سے کسی نے نکیر نہیں کی، تو یہ اجماع دلیل بنا کہ حدیث فاطمہ مستنکر ہے، قیاس کے خلاف ہے، ہاں اگر چوتھی قسم میں حدیث قیاس کے موافق ہو تو اس پر عمل جائز ہوگا مگر یہ جواز قیاس کی وجہ سے ہوگا نہ کہ حدیث کی وجہ سے، حدیث تو قیاس کے لئے صرف مؤید ہوگی۔
(4) The fourth division is that the Salaf rejected the hadith of this unknown narrator, so that hadith will not be acceptable; it will be called mustankir (rejected). Such a hadith, if it is contrary to qiyas, will not be acted upon. Because when the Companions rejected it and did not act on it, this means that the narrator is accused of lying and this hadith is not established from the Prophet (peace be upon him), otherwise the Companions would have accepted it. In this fourth division, the probability of lying is less than that of a fabricated hadith. Its example is the hadith of Fatima bint Qais (an unknown female narrator). She said that her husband divorced her with three divorces during the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'No housing and no maintenance.' But when Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) received this hadith, he said in a gathering of Companions: 'We will not abandon the Book and Sunnah because of the statement of a woman.' Because in the Book of Allah it says: 'Do not turn them out of their houses' meaning maintenance and housing are compulsory. None of the Companions objected, so this consensus became evidence that the hadith of Fatima is mustankir and contrary to qiyas. Yes, if in the fourth division a hadith agrees with qiyas, then acting upon it is permissible, but this permissibility is due to qiyas, not due to the hadith. The hadith only serves as a support for qiyas.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage explains the fourth of the five categories of hadith from an unknown narrator. If the Salaf (specifically the Companions) have rejected a hadith, it is called mustankir (rejected). Such a hadith is not acceptable as standalone evidence, especially if it contradicts qiyas. The author provides the famous example of Fatima bint Qais, who reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said an irrevocably divorced woman is entitled to no housing or maintenance. Caliph Umar rejected this hadith before the Companions, citing the Quranic verse 'Do not turn them out of their houses' (Surah at-Talaq, 65:1), and no Companion objected, forming an implicit consensus (ijma) that the hadith is mustankir. However, if a hadith in this category agrees with qiyas, it may be acted upon, but the effective legal authority is the qiyas, not the hadith itself. This category is distinct from a fabricated hadith (mawdu'), where the probability of lying is higher.

Key Terms
مستنکر (mustankir): A hadith that is rejected because it goes against established principles, especially if narrated by an unknown narrator and rejected by the Salaf.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the Companions (specifically, their silent approval of Umar's rejection).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Umar reject the hadith of Fatima bint Qais?
A) Because the narrator was a woman
B) Because it contradicted the Quran
C) Because it was narrated by an unknown narrator
D) Because the narrator was known to be a liar

Key Takeaway
A hadith rejected by the entire Salaf (mustankir) cannot override the Quran or qiyas; it may only support qiyas if consistent.

The Mustatar Hadith: Permissibility of Acting on an Unknown Narrator's Hadith Not Known to the Salaf
Explains the ruling on a mustatar hadith not attested among Salaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi ruling on a mustatar hadith and apply the conditions for acting upon it.

Core Idea
A mustatar hadith not known to the Salaf is permissible to act upon if it agrees with qiyas, but not obligatory.

In Hanafi usul, hadiths from unknown narrators are classified into several categories. The fifth category involves a hadith that was never presented to the Salaf—neither accepted nor rejected. The key question is: can we act upon such a hadith? The Hanafi answer distinguishes based on the era of the narrator and conformity with qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that the hadith is from an unknown narrator (majhul) and was not known to have been presented to the Salaf (Companions). It was neither accepted nor rejected by them.
This is distinct from categories where the Salaf accepted or rejected the hadith.
2
State the general ruling
The Hanafi position is that acting upon such a hadith is not obligatory (wajib), but it is permissible (ja'iz).
The default is not obligation because the narrator's reliability is uncertain.
3
Apply the condition of qiyas
Permissibility is conditional: the hadith must not contradict qiyas (analogical reasoning). If it contradicts qiyas, it cannot be acted upon.
This condition preserves the consistency of legal reasoning.
4
Distinguish by era
If the narrator belongs to the era of the Salaf (the first generations), acting upon it is permissible. If the narrator is from later generations (after the best of generations), it is not permissible.
The rationale is that justice ('adalah) was the norm in the early period, while corruption became prevalent later.
5
Understand the underlying principle
The permissibility is based on the principle of original justice: in the time of the Companions, narrators were presumed just unless proven otherwise. This presumption does not hold for later narrators.
This is a methodological assumption specific to Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵) پانچویں قسم یہ ہے کہ مجہول راوی کی حدیث سلف میں ظاہر نہ ہوئی ہو، اور نہ کسی نے اس کو قبول کیا ہو اور نہ رد کیا ہو، تو اس حدیث پر عمل واجب تو نہیں ہے البتہ اگر یہ حدیث قیاس کے مخالف نہ ہو تو عمل جائز ہے کیونکہ دور صحابہ میں عدالت اصل ہے، لہذا راوی کو عادل سمجھتے ہوئے اس پر عمل جائز ہوگا، اگر خیر القرون کے بعد کا راوی ایسا ہو تو حدیث پر عمل جائز بھی نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ بعد کے دور میں فسق و فجور غالب ہے۔
(5) The fifth division is that the hadith of the unknown narrator did not appear among the Salaf, nor did anyone accept or reject it. Then acting upon this hadith is not obligatory; however, if this hadith does not contradict qiyas, then acting upon it is permissible, because in the era of the Companions justice was the norm. Therefore, considering the narrator to be just, acting upon it is permissible. If the narrator is from after the best of generations, then acting upon the hadith is not permissible, because in later times corruption and immorality predominate.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage covers the fifth and final category of hadith from an unknown narrator. Here, the hadith was not known to have been presented to the Salaf (the Companions); neither was it accepted nor rejected by them. The key nuance is that acting upon such a hadith is not obligatory but permissible, provided it does not contradict qiyas. The reason for permissibility is the principle that justice ('adalah) was the default attribute of Companions and their contemporaries. However, if the narrator belongs to later generations (after the best of generations, i.e., after the early Muslims), the hadith is not even permissible to act upon because of the prevalence of corruption. This category is later referred to as mustatar (concealed) in the Arabic text.

Key Terms
مستتر (mustatar): A hadith from an unknown narrator that was not known to the Salaf; acting upon it is permissible but not obligatory, provided it agrees with qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true about a mustatar hadith not attested among the Salaf, according to Hanafi usul?
A) It is obligatory to act upon it.
B) It is permissible if it does not contradict qiyas and the narrator is from the early generations.
C) It is absolutely rejected regardless of conditions.
D) It is permissible only if the narrator is from a later generation.

Key Takeaway
A mustatar hadith from an early narrator, if not contradicted by qiyas, is permissible but not obligatory to act upon.

Mustanqar and Mustakir in Khabar Wahid
Defining mustanqar and mustakir types of khabar wahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mustanqar and mustakir khabar wahid and state the Hanafi ruling for each based on probability preponderance.

Core Idea
Mustanqar gives only illusion (wahm) and is not actionable; mustakir gives equal probability and is permissible but not obligatory.

This passage continues from the previous page, introducing two key subcategories of khabar wahid in Hanafi usul: mustanqar (rejected) and mustakir (neutral). Understanding these categories is essential for evaluating the legal weight of solitary reports, as the Hanafi school classifies them by the strength of probability they convey.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types and their Arabic terms
Locate the terms 'mustanqar' (مستنکر) and 'mustakir' (مستتر) in the text. Note that mustanqar is also called munkar.
The terms are defined in relation to probability of existence vs. non-existence.
2
Understand the probability framework
Distinguish between three levels: knowledge of tranquility (al-ilm al-tuma'nini) where non-existence is very weak; speculation (zann) where existence is preponderant; and illusion (wahm) where non-existence is preponderant. Mustanqar gives wahm; mustakir gives equal probability.
The passage compares these levels explicitly.
3
Determine the ruling for each type
For mustanqar: since it gives only wahm, it cannot be used as proof. For mustakir: since existence and non-existence are equal, acting upon it is permissible (mubah) but not obligatory (wajib).
This is the core practical outcome.
4
Note the practical consequence
A mustanqar hadith is rejected and cannot establish a ruling. A mustakir hadith leaves the matter optional—the mukallaf may follow it or not.
This contrasts with mustafid (widely transmitted) which gives certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستنکر ہوتی ہے، اور خبر واحد غلبہ ظن کا فائدہ دیتی ہے، ظن کہتے ہیں جس میں ثبوت کی جہت راحج اور عدم ثبوت کی جہت مرجوح ہو۔۔ طمانیت اور فن میں فرق یہ ہے کہ علم طمانیت میں عدم کی جہت بہت مرجوح ہوتی ہے، اور ظن میں عدم کی جہت طمانیت کے مقابلہ میں کم درجہ مرجوح ہوتی ہے، تو علم طمانیت ظن سے اقومی ہے، اور خبر واحد میں حدیث مستنکرظن یعنی وہم کا فائدہ دیتی ہے، اور وہم حق میں کسی بھی چیز کا فائدہ نہیں دیتا، لہذا مستنکر پر عمل جائز نہیں ہے وہم اس کو کہتے ہیں جس میں عدم ثبوت راج ہو، اور خبر واحد میں مستتر جس کو سلف نے نہ قبول کیا ہو نہ رد کیا ہو، اس پر عمل جائز تو ہے واجب نہیں کیونکہ خبر مستر ایسے علم کا فائدہ دیتی ہے جس میں ثبوت اور عدم ثبوت کی دونوں جہتیں برابر ہوتی ہیں، لہذا یہ جائز ہوگا واجب نہ ہوگا ، یعنی اس پر عمل کرنا نہ کرنا دونوں جہتیں برابر ہیں،
It becomes munkar, and khabar wahid gives the benefit of preponderance of speculation. Speculation is defined as that in which the direction of existence is preponderant and the direction of non-existence is weak. The difference between tranquility and speculation is that in the knowledge of tranquility, the direction of non-existence is very weak, and in speculation the direction of non-existence is weaker in degree compared to tranquility. So knowledge of tranquility is stronger than speculation. In khabar wahid, the hadith of mustanqar gives the benefit of speculation, i.e., illusion (wahm), and illusion does not benefit any matter of right. Therefore, acting on mustanqar is not permissible. Wahm is called that in which non-existence is preponderant. And in khabar wahid, mustakir, which the predecessors neither accepted nor rejected, acting on it is permissible but not obligatory, because mustakir gives benefit of knowledge in which both the direction of existence and non-existence are equal. Therefore, it will be permissible, not obligatory, meaning acting or not acting upon it are equal.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage defines two types of khabar wahid in Hanafi usul: mustanqar (also called munkar) and mustakir. It distinguishes between levels of certainty: knowledge of tranquility (al-ilm al-tuma'nini) where non-existence is very improbable, and speculation (al-zann) where existence is probable but non-existence is still possible. For mustanqar, the probability of non-existence outweighs existence, so it gives wahm (illusion), which carries no legal weight; thus it cannot be acted upon. For mustakir, the probabilities are equal; it gives no preponderance, so acting upon it is permissible (mubah) but not obligatory (wajib). The Hanafi distinction is crucial: unlike the Shafi'i school which often grades ahad, the Hanafis categorize based on probability strength.

Key Terms
مستنکر (mustanqar): A khabar wahid that gives the benefit of speculation (zann) but actually only gives wahm (illusion) because the probability of non-existence is preponderant.
مستتر (mustakir): A khabar wahid that was neither accepted nor rejected by the early authorities; it gives equal probability of existence and non-existence.
وہم (wahm): A level of probability where non-existence is preponderant over existence; gives no legal benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal ruling for acting upon a mustanqar hadith?
A) It is obligatory (wajib)
B) It is permissible (mubah) but not obligatory
C) It is not permissible (jayyiz nahin)
D) It is recommended (mustahabb)

Key Takeaway
Mustanqar khabar wahid is rejected because it gives only wahm; mustakir is optional because it gives equal probability of existence and non-existence.

Al-Sunnah as Source

Conditions for Rejecting a Hadith: Narrator's Opposition and Teacher's Denial
Stating the rule for suqut al-'amal with an ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a hadith is dropped due to narrator or Companion opposition, and apply the Hanafi rule for the teacher's denial.

Core Idea
A hadith is abandoned when the narrator contradicts it after narration, or when Companions oppose it despite its clarity, indicating abrogation.

This passage from Al-Husami states a key Hanafi usul principle: a hadith loses its legal force when the narrator himself contradicts it after narrating, or when leading Companions oppose it while it was widespread. However, if the hadith could have been unknown to the opponent, it remains valid. The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the case where the teacher (mawwi 'anhu) denies narrating the hadith. Understanding this rule is essential for evaluating hadith evidence in Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule's trigger
Note the condition: opposition (mukhalafah) must appear from the narrator after narration, or from other leading scholars (Companions).
Opposition before narration does not cause suqut.
2
Assess the hadith's clarity
The hadith must be apparent (zahir) and not likely hidden from the opponent. If it could have been unknown, the opposition does not invalidate.
Example: laughter during prayer hadith opposed by some Companions, but it remained valid because it was a rare occurrence.
3
Interpret the consequence
When suqut occurs, the hadith is interpreted as abrogated (naskh), not as necessarily fabricated.
This preserves the integrity of the narrator while acknowledging the opposition.
4
Analyze the teacher's denial
If the teacher (mawwi 'anhu) denies narrating the hadith, there is an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf. Abu Yusuf drops the hadith; Muhammad accepts it.
The passage indicates that dropping it is 'al-ashbah' (more appropriate), favoring Abu Yusuf.
5
Examine the qiyas foundation
The ikhtilaf is analogized from the case of two witnesses testifying before a qadi who does not recall the case. Abu Yusuf rejects the testimony; Muhammad accepts it.
The analogy: the teacher's denial is like the qadi's lack of memory.

الْخِفَاءَ عَلَيْهِمْ وَيُحْمَلُ عَلَى النَّسْخِ وَاخْتُلِفَ فِيمَا إِذَا أَنْكَرَهُ الْمَرْوِيُّ عَنْهُ قَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ يَسْقُطُ الْعَمَلُ بِهِ وَهُوَ الْأَشْبَهُ وَقَدْ قِيلَ إِنَّ هَذَا قَوْلُ ترجمہ : اور ساقط ہو جائے گا حدیث پر عمل کرنا جب کہ راوی کی مخالفت ظاہر ہو قولاً یا عملاً روایت کے بعد، یا راوی کے غیر کی طرف سے ائمہ حدیث میں سے، جب کہ حدیث ایسی ظاہر ہو جو ان پر مخفی ہونے کا احتمال نہ رکھتی ہو، اور محمول کیا جائے گا حدیث کو منسوخ ہونے پر ۔ اور اختلاف کیا گیا ہے اس صورت میں جب کہ مروی عنہ (استاذ) حدیث کا انکار کر دے، بعض نے کہا ہے کہ اس پر عمل ساقط ہو جائے گا اور یہی حق کے زیادہ مشابہ ہے، اور کہا گیا ہے، کہ یہ امام ابو یوسف کا قول ہے، امام محمد کے خلاف ، اور یہ اختلاف فرع ہے ان دونوں کے اختلاف کی ان دو گواہوں کے بارے میں جنہوں نے قاضی کے خلاف گواہی دی کسی فیصلہ میں ، اور حال
