احتمال ہے اور راوی نے ایک معنی اختیار کر لیا، تو اس مخالفت سے حدیث متروک نہ ہوگی ، اسی طرح اگر راوی کی مخالفت روایت کرنے سے پہلے ہو یا مخالفت کی تاریخ کا علم نہ ہو تو بھی حدیث متروک نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ روایت سے پہلے مخالفت ہے تو یوں کہیں گے کہ راوی نے روایت کے بعد اپنا مذہب بدل دیا، اور مخالفت کی تاریخ معلوم نہ ہونے کی صورت میں یوں کہیں گے کہ حدیث اصل میں یقین کے ساتھ حجت ہے، اور تاریخ معلوم نہ ہونے سے اس کے ساقط الاعتبار ہونے میں شک ہو گیا، اور یقین شک سے زائل نہیں ہوتا ، لہذا حدیث حجت رہے گی۔ اسی طرح اگر راوی کے علاوہ ائمہ حدیث یعنی صحابہ میں سے کسی نے اس حدیث کی مخالفت کی ہو، اور حدیث ایسی ہو جس کے ان حضرات پر مخفی ہونے کا احتمال نہ ہو، تو بھی حدیث متروک ہو جائے گی ، جیسے راوی کی مخالفت سے متروک ہوتی ہے، اور اگر حدیث ایسی ہے جس کے مخفی ہونے کا احتمال ہے تو ان کی مخالفت سے حدیث متروک نہ ہوگی جیسے نماز میں قہقہہ سے وضو ٹوٹنے کی حدیث، بعض صحابہ نے اس کی مخالفت کی ہے، وہ اس کے قائل نہیں ہیں تو ان کی مخالفت کے باوجود حدیث متروک نہ ہوگی کیونکہ نماز میں قہقہہ ایک نادر چیز ہے، ممکن ہے مخالفت کرنے والے صحابہ پر یہ امرمخفی رہا ہو، پتہ نہ چلا ہو۔ بہر حال راوی کی مخالفت یا راوی کے علاوہ ائمہ صحابہ کی مخالفت سے بھی حدیث متروک ہو جائے گی اور اس حدیث کو منسوخ ہونے پر محمول کیا جائے گا جیسے حدیث ہے البكر بالبكر جلد مأة وتغريب عام في محصن زانی اور زانیہ کی سزا سو کوڑے اور ایک سال جلد وطنی ہے، امام شافعی نے اسی حدیث سے استدلال کر کے جلا وطن کرنے کو حد زنا کا جزء قرار دیا مگر احناف کہتے ہیں کہ ائمہ صحابہ نے اس حدیث کی مخالفت کی ہے، حالانکہ حدیث تمام صحابہ پر عیاں تھی ، معلوم ہوا کہ حدیث منسوخ ہے، اس پر عمل نہ ہوگا ، اگر حدیث ثابت ہوتی تو صحابہ سے یہ بعید ہے کہ وہ حدیث کی مخالفت کریں۔ واختلف فيما اذا نكرة : - اگر کسی راوی نے کوئی حدیث روایت کی اور مروی عنہ یعنی اس کے شیخ نے انکار کر دیا، یہ انکار دوطرح کا ہے، (۱) ایک تو یہ کہ انکار جاحد ہو جیسے شیخ کہے میں نے تیرے سامنے یہ حدیث کبھی بیان نہیں کی ، یا تو نے مجھ پر جھوٹ بولا ، تو اس صورت میں تو بالا تفاق حدیث ترک کر دی جائے گی کیونکہ راوی اور شیخ دونوں میں سے ایک لا علی التعیین جھوٹا ہے، اور اس کی وجہ سے حدیث میں عیب پیدا ہو گیا لیکن اس حدیث کی وجہ
And action upon the hadith is dropped when its opposition appears, in statement or action, from the narrator after narration, or from others among the leading Companions, while the hadith is apparent, not likely to be hidden from them, and it is interpreted as abrogated. And there is disagreement regarding when the one from whom it is narrated (the teacher) denies it. Some said that action upon it is dropped, and that is more appropriate. And it has been said that this is the statement of Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. And this is a branch of their disagreement concerning two witnesses who testified before the qadi about a case, while he does not recall it. Abu Yusuf said: Their testimony is not accepted. Muhammad said: It is accepted. Translation: Action upon the hadith will be dropped when the narrator's opposition appears, in statement or action, after narration, or from others among the hadith scholars, when the hadith is apparent, not likely to be hidden from them, and the hadith will be interpreted as abrogated. There is disagreement in the case where the one from whom it is narrated (the teacher) denies the hadith. Some said that action upon it is dropped, and that is more appropriate. It has been said that this is the statement of Imam Abu Yusuf, contrary to Imam Muhammad. And this disagreement is a branch of their disagreement concerning two witnesses who testified before the qadi about a case, and the qadi does not recall it. Imam Abu Yusuf said: Their testimony is not accepted. Imam Muhammad said: It will be accepted. Commentary: If a narrator after narrating a hadith opposes it, meaning his statement, action, or fatwa is contrary to the narration, then this hadith will not be actionable. This is because the narrator's opposition to his own narration could be because the hadith is fabricated or abrogated, or the narrator is careless, or he is dominated by negligence and forgetfulness, or he considers the narration insignificant. In all these cases, the hadith loses credibility, because the conditions for trustworthiness in the narrator are missing. However, if the narrator's opposition is regarding a hadith that can bear multiple meanings and the narrator has selected one meaning, then the hadith is not abandoned due to this opposition. Similarly, if the narrator's opposition occurred before the narration, or the date of the opposition is not known, then the hadith is also not abandoned. If opposition occurred before narration, we will assume the narrator changed his view after narrating. If the date is unknown, we will say that the hadith originally is a proof with certainty, and because of unknown date doubt arises about its abandonment, but certainty is not removed by doubt, so the hadith remains a proof. Similarly, if other hadith scholars among the Companions oppose this hadith, and the hadith is such that it could not be hidden from them, then the hadith is abandoned, just as it is abandoned due to the narrator's opposition. But if the hadith could have been hidden from them, then the hadith is not abandoned because of their opposition, like the hadith about laughter in prayer breaking wudu. Some Companions opposed this hadith and did not hold it, yet the hadith is not abandoned because laughter in prayer is a rare occurrence; it is possible that the opposing Companions were unaware of it. In any case, opposition from the narrator or from other leading Companions causes the hadith to be abandoned, and such a hadith will be interpreted as abrogated, like the hadith: 'For the unmarried, flogging of one hundred and exile for one year.' Imam al-Shafi'i used this hadith to consider exile as part of the hadd punishment. The Hanafis say that the leading Companions opposed this hadith, even though it was manifest to all of them; this shows that the hadith is abrogated and will not be acted upon. If the hadith had been valid, it would be unlikely for the Companions to oppose it. And there is disagreement regarding the case when the source denies: If a narrator narrates a hadith and the one from whom it is narrated (his teacher) denies it, this denial is of two types: (1) that the denial is rejective, e.g., the teacher says: 'I never narrated this hadith before you,' or 'You have lied about me.' In this case, by agreement, the hadith will be abandoned because one of the two is lying, and a defect appears in the hadith. But this hadith because... [cut off]
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a rule from Hanafi usul: the validity of a hadith can be undermined by the narrator's own contrary practice or by opposition from the Companions, but only if the hadith is well-known and could not be unknown to them. If opposition occurs, the hadith is considered abrogated or weakened. The rule also distinguishes cases where the hadith allows multiple interpretations, where opposition before narration does not harm, and where the date of opposition is unknown (principle of continuity: certainty is not removed by doubt). The Hanafi position on the hadith of flogging and exile for the unmarried is cited: because leading Companions opposed it even though it was widespread, the Hanafis deem it abrogated, rejecting the Shafi'i use of it. The passage ends with the ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the case where the teacher (rawi 'anhu) denies the narration. Abu Yusuf drops the hadith; Muhammad accepts it, analogized from the case of witnesses. The commentary explains two types of denial: outright rejection (takdhib) leading to definite abandonment, and other types (likely the text cuts off).

Key Terms
سقوط العمل (suqut al-'amal): The dropping of legal effect of a hadith; it is no longer considered a valid proof.
مخالفة (mukhalafah): Opposition to a hadith by the narrator or other scholars in word or deed, indicating that the hadith is no longer reliable.
مروي عنه (mawwi 'anhu): The teacher from whom a hadith is narrated; if he denies narrating it, a dispute arises.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a hadith when the narrator opposes it after narration, and the opposition is in a hadith that has only one possible meaning?
A) The hadith is still a proof and must be acted upon
B) The hadith is abandoned and interpreted as abrogated
C) The hadith is considered weak but still acceptable
D) The narrator's opposition is ignored if he is reliable

Key Takeaway
A hadith is abandoned if the narrator or Companions oppose it after it was clearly known, and it is then treated as abrogated.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
10 min
Narrator and Companion Opposition in Hadith Evaluation
Conditions affecting hadith reliability due to opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criteria for when narrator or Companion opposition causes a hadith to be abandoned, and distinguish between types of opposition that do and do not affect a hadith's authority.

Core Idea
Opposition only abandons a hadith when it shows rejection of the hadith itself, not when based on interpretation or timing ambiguity.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi usul principle: when does opposition (mukhalafa) to a hadith by its narrator or by the Companions render the hadith unreliable? You might think any opposition invalidates a hadith, but the Hanafis draw careful distinctions based on the nature of the opposition, its timing, and whether the hadith was widely known. Understanding this rule is crucial for evaluating hadith evidence and resolving conflicts between transmitted reports and scholarly practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of opposition
Determine whether the opposition comes from the narrator of the hadith or from a Companion (or other scholar). This affects which set of conditions apply.
2
If narrator opposition: check interpretation vs rejection
If the narrator adopted one of multiple possible meanings, the hadith remains valid. If he rejected the hadith outright (e.g., calls it trivial), the hadith becomes invalid.
Opposition due to interpretation does not harm the hadith.
3
If narrator opposition: check timing and date
If opposition occurred before narration, we assume the narrator later changed his view, so hadith stands. If date is unknown, certainty of the hadith's authority prevails over doubt.
Uncertainty does not overturn certainty.
4
If Companion opposition: check fame of the hadith
If the hadith was widely known and could not have been hidden from the Companions, their opposition indicates abrogation and the hadith is abandoned. If it was obscure, their opposition is ignored.
Example: hadith on lashing and exile was famous, so Companion opposition shows naskh.
5
Conclude on the hadith's status
Apply the above criteria to decide whether the hadith remains a valid proof (hujja) or is deemed abrogated/invalid.
If invalid, the hadith is said to be saqit al-i'tibar.

حدیث موضوع ہے یا منسوخ ہے، یا راوی لا پرواہ ہے یا راوی پر غفلت و نسیان کا غلبہ ہے یا وہ روایت کو حقیر سمجھتا ہے، تو ان تمام صورتوں میں حدیث ساقط الاعتبار ہوگی، کیونکہ راوی میں روایت کی شرطیں مفقود ہیں، البتہ اگر راوی کی مخالفت ایسی حدیث میں ہے جس میں چند معانی کا احتمال ہے اور راوی نے ایک معنی اختیار کر لیا، تو اس مخالفت سے حدیث متروک نہ ہوگی ، اسی طرح اگر راوی کی مخالفت روایت کرنے سے پہلے ہو یا مخالفت کی تاریخ کا علم نہ ہو تو بھی حدیث متروک نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ روایت سے پہلے مخالفت ہے تو یوں کہیں گے کہ راوی نے روایت کے بعد اپنا مذہب بدل دیا، اور مخالفت کی تاریخ معلوم نہ ہونے کی صورت میں یوں کہیں گے کہ حدیث اصل میں یقین کے ساتھ حجت ہے، اور تاریخ معلوم نہ ہونے سے اس کے ساقط الاعتبار ہونے میں شک ہو گیا، اور یقین شک سے زائل نہیں ہوتا ، لہذا حدیث حجت رہے گی۔ اسی طرح اگر راوی کے علاوہ ائمہ حدیث یعنی صحابہ میں سے کسی نے اس حدیث کی مخالفت کی ہو، اور حدیث ایسی ہو جس کے ان حضرات پر مخفی ہونے کا احتمال نہ ہو، تو بھی حدیث متروک ہو جائے گی ، جیسے راوی کی مخالفت سے متروک ہوتی ہے، اور اگر حدیث ایسی ہے جس کے مخفی ہونے کا احتمال ہے تو ان کی مخالفت سے حدیث متروک نہ ہوگی جیسے نماز میں قہقہہ سے وضو ٹوٹنے کی حدیث، بعض صحابہ نے اس کی مخالفت کی ہے، وہ اس کے قائل نہیں ہیں تو ان کی مخالفت کے باوجود حدیث متروک نہ ہوگی کیونکہ نماز میں قہقہہ ایک نادر چیز ہے، ممکن ہے مخالفت کرنے والے صحابہ پر یہ امرمخفی رہا ہو، پتہ نہ چلا ہو۔ بہر حال راوی کی مخالفت یا راوی کے علاوہ ائمہ صحابہ کی مخالفت سے بھی حدیث متروک ہو جائے گی اور اس حدیث کو منسوخ ہونے پر محمول کیا جائے گا جیسے حدیث ہے البكر بالبكر جلد مأة وتغريب عام في محصن زانی اور زانیہ کی سزا سو کوڑے اور ایک سال جلد وطنی ہے، امام شافعی نے اسی حدیث سے استدلال کر کے جلا وطن کرنے کو حد زنا کا جزء قرار دیا مگر احناف کہتے ہیں کہ ائمہ صحابہ نے اس حدیث کی مخالفت کی ہے، حالانکہ حدیث تمام صحابہ پر عیاں تھی ، معلوم ہوا کہ حدیث منسوخ ہے، اس پر عمل نہ ہوگا ، اگر حدیث ثابت ہوتی تو صحابہ سے یہ بعید ہے کہ وہ حدیث کی مخالفت کریں۔
A hadith is fabricated or abrogated, or the narrator is careless or dominated by heedlessness and forgetfulness, or he considers the narration trivial—in all these cases the hadith becomes invalid, because the conditions for narration are missing in the narrator. However, if the narrator's opposition is in a hadith that has probability of multiple meanings and the narrator adopted one meaning, then the hadith is not abandoned due to such opposition. Likewise, if the opposition occurred before narrating, or the date of opposition is unknown, the hadith is not abandoned. Because if the opposition is before narration, we say the narrator changed his madhhab after narrating; and if the date of opposition is unknown, we say the hadith is originally established as proof with certainty, and due to the unknown date, doubt arose about its invalidation, and certainty is not removed by doubt. Hence the hadith remains proof. Similarly, if someone other than the narrator from the scholars of hadith, i.e., among the Companions, opposed this hadith, and the hadith is such that it could not have been hidden from them, then the hadith is abandoned, just as it is abandoned due to the narrator's opposition. But if the hadith could have been hidden from them, their opposition does not abandon the hadith—as in the hadith about laughter in prayer breaking wudu: some Companions opposed it and did not accept it, yet the hadith is not abandoned because laughter in prayer is rare and it is possible that the opposing Companions were unaware of it. In any case, opposition by the narrator or by the Companions can cause the hadith to be abandoned, and such a hadith is deemed to be abrogated. For example, the hadith: 'The unmarried male and female: one hundred lashes and exile for one year'—Imam al-Shafi'i used this hadith to make exile part of the punishment for fornication. But the Hanafis say that the Companions opposed this hadith, even though it was known to all of them. Hence it is abrogated and not acted upon. If the hadith were authentic, it would be remote for the Companions to oppose it.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul rule on when a hadith is rendered unreliable due to opposition (mukhalafa) by the narrator or by the Companions. The author explains that a hadith becomes invalid if the narrator lacks the required conditions (trustworthiness, precision, etc.). However, opposition only harms the hadith if it stems from rejection of the hadith itself—not from choosing one of multiple legitimate interpretations. If the narrator opposed the hadith before narrating it, we consider that he later changed his view, so the hadith remains valid. If the date of opposition is unknown, certainty of the hadith's authority prevails over doubt. As for opposition by Companions: if the hadith was widely known and could not have been hidden, their opposition indicates it is abrogated; if it was obscure, their opposition does not affect it. The example given is the hadith prescribing lashing and exile for unmarried fornicators. The Hanafis argue that the Companions' rejection of this hadith, despite its fame, shows it was abrogated. This is a key usul principle: a famous hadith opposed by all Companions is taken as abrogated. The passage does not provide the full fiqh details but uses the example to illustrate the usul ruling.

Key Terms
مخالفة (mukhalafa): Opposition by the narrator or a Companion to the content of a hadith, which may affect its reliability.
ساقط الاعتبار (saqit al-i'tibar): A hadith that loses its status as a valid proof due to defects in the narrator or chain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does opposition by a Companion cause a hadith to be abandoned according to the Hanafi usul?
A) Whenever any Companion opposes the hadith, regardless of the circumstances.
B) Only if the hadith is unknown and could have been hidden from the Companions.
C) Only if the hadith is famous and could not have been hidden from the Companions.
D) Only if the Companion is a narrator of the hadith.

Key Takeaway
When a narrator or Companion opposes a hadith, its status depends on the nature and timing of the opposition: interpretation does not invalidate, but outright rejection or fame-based Companion opposition indicates abrogation.

Shaykh's Hesitant Denial: Hanafi Internal Dispute on Hadith Continuity
Hanafi internal dispute on the effect of a shaykh's hesitant denial on hadith reliability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between categorical and hesitant denial by the shaykh, and evaluate the Hanafi internal dispute on whether such denial renders a hadith unreliable.

Core Idea
A shaykh's hesitant denial breaks the chain's continuity, making the hadith munqati' and non-actionable for Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

In the transmission of hadith, what happens when a narrator's teacher denies having ever taught that hadith? The Hanafi school distinguishes between a flat denial and a hesitant one. This lesson explores the internal Hanafi dispute on hesitant denial, its basis in the principle of chain continuity (ittiṣāl), and its practical consequences for legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of denial
Categorical denial (jāḥid) leads to unanimous rejection because one party lies. Hesitant denial (mutaqif) is the disputed case.
2
Identify the two positions on hesitant denial
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf reject the hadith due to discontinuity; Imam Muhammad accepts it because hesitation is not a defect.
3
Trace the evidence for each position
The rejectionists argue that a hadith is only authoritative when it reaches us connected (muttasil); denial breaks that. The acceptance side argues that forgetfulness is possible and does not amount to a defect (jarh).
4
Analyze the analogy with the judge's memory
The parallel disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on accepting testimony when a judge denies his verdict clarifies the principle behind the hadith dispute.
This analogy shows the underlying principle: denial creates uncertainty about the chain.
5
Apply the dispute to real hadith examples
Examine the hadith of 'one witness and an oath' and the hadith of 'marriage without guardian' to see the practical outcome.

واختلف فيما اذا نكرة : - اگر کسی راوی نے کوئی حدیث روایت کی اور مروی عنہ یعنی اس کے شیخ نے انکار کر دیا، یہ انکار دوطرح کا ہے، (۱) ایک تو یہ کہ انکار جاحد ہو جیسے شیخ کہے میں نے تیرے سامنے یہ حدیث کبھی بیان نہیں کی ، یا تو نے مجھ پر جھوٹ بولا ، تو اس صورت میں تو بالا تفاق حدیث ترک کر دی جائے گی کیونکہ راوی اور شیخ دونوں میں سے ایک لاعلی التعیین جھوٹا ہے، اور اس کی وجہ سے حدیث میں عیب پیدا ہو گیا لیکن اس حدیث کی وجہ سے دوسری احادیث میں عیب پیدا نہ ہوگا ، پس اس راوی اور شیخ کی دوسری روایات قابل قبول ہیں۔ (۲) دوسرے یہ کہ انکار متوقف ہو جیسے شیخ کہے میں تو حدیث کو نہیں جانتا، یا مجھے یاد نہیں کہ میں نے تیرے سامنے یہ حدیث بیان کی ہو، انکار کی اس صورت میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے، ابوالحسن کرخی اور حنفیہ کی ایک جماعت کہتی ہے کہ اس پر عمل کرنا ساقط ہو جائے گا، اور امام جی اور متکلمین کی ایک جماعت کہتی ہے کہ اس حدیث پر عمل کیا جائے گا، مصنف نے پہلے قول کو اشبه بالحق فرما یا یعنی حق کے زیادہ مشابہ اور قریب ہے، کیونکہ حدیث اسی وقت حجت بنتی ہے جب وہ رسول اللہ لا یا یہ ہم تک متصل ہو اور انکار کے سبب انقطاع پیدا ہو گیا۔ بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ حدیث پر عمل کا ساقط ہونا امام ابو یوسف کا قول ہے، اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس حدیث پر عمل جائز ہوگا کیونکہ مروی عنہ یعنی شیخ کے توقف سے حدیث میں کوئی جرح نہیں پیدا ہوا لہذا حدیث قابل عمل ہے، یہی امام شافعی اور امام مالک کا مذہب ہے۔ وهو فرع اختلافهما : - صاحبین کے درمیان یہ اختلاف ایک دوسرے مسئلہ میں ان کا جو اختلاف ہوا ہے اس کی فرع ہے، وہ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے قاضی کے سامنے دعوی کیا کہ آپ نے میرے لئے میرے فریق مخالف پر دو ہزار روپے کی مالیت کا فیصلہ کیا ہے، قاضی کہتا ہے مجھے تو یہ فیصلہ یاد نہیں، تو مدعی نے دو گواہ پیش کر دئے جو گواہی دے رہے ہیں کہ قاضی نے دو ہزار کی مالیت کا فیصلہ کیا ہے، تو اس مسئلہ میں صاحبین میں اختلاف ہے، امام ابو یوسف کہتے ہیں کہ قاضی کے انکار کی وجہ سے دو گواہوں کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی ، اور امام محمد کہتے ہیں کہ شہادت قبول ہوگی کیونکہ امکان ہے کہ قاضی اپنا فیصلہ بھول رہا ہو یہی اختلاف صاحبین کا حدیث کے باب میں ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک شیخ کے انکار کی صورت میں حدیث پر عمل جائز نہیں اور امام محمد کے نزدیک عمل جائز ہے،اس کی مثال ربيعه عن سهل عن أبي صالح عن ابي هريرة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى بشاهد ويمين - حضور صلی شما اینم نے ایک گواہ اور ایک قسم پر فیصلہ کیا، یہ حدیث ربیعہ روایت کرتے ہیں سہل سے لیکن جب سہل سے پوچھا گیا تو سہل نے کہا مجھے تو یاد نہیں تو یہ حدیث امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام یوسف کے نزدیک مروی عنہ یعنی شیخ کے انکار کی وجہ سے قابل عمل نہیں، لیکن امام شافعی نے اس حدیث پر عمل کیا ۔۔ اسی طرح ایک حدیث ہے سليمان بن موسى عن الزهري عن عروة عن عائشه ان النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ايما امرأة نكحت بغير اذن وليها فنكاحها باطل باطل باطل - ابن جریج نے زہری سے سوال کیا تو زہری اس حدیث کو پہچان نہ سکے۔ تو یہ حدیث امام ابو یوسف اور امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک شیخ کے انکار کی وجہ سے قابل عمل نہیں ، اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ حدیث قابل عمل ہے۔
They differ regarding when there is denial: If a narrator narrates a hadith and the one narrated from, i.e., his shaykh, denies it. This denial is of two types: (1) categorical denial, like the shaykh says, 'I never narrated this hadith to you,' or 'You lied about me,' then in this case the hadith is abandoned by agreement, because one of the two—the narrator or the shaykh—is definitely lying, and due to that a defect appears in the hadith. However, this hadith does not cause a defect in other hadiths; so other narrations from this narrator and shaykh are acceptable. (2) The denial is hesitant, like the shaykh says, 'I do not know this hadith,' or 'I do not remember having narrated it to you.' In this form of denial there is disagreement among scholars. Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and a group of Hanafis say that acting upon it becomes invalid. Imam al-Ji (?) and a group of mutakallimun say that acting upon this hadith is permissible. The author (al-Husami) deemed the first opinion closer to truth (ashbah bi al-haqq), because a hadith is only authoritative when it reaches us connected to the Prophet, and due to the denial, disconnection (inqita') occurs. Some say that the invalidity of acting on the hadith is the view of Imam Abu Yusuf, while Imam Muhammad considers acting on it permissible because the shaykh's hesitation does not introduce any defect (jarh) in the hadith; hence it is actionable. This is also the view of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik. And this disagreement is a branch (far') of their disagreement in another issue: that a man claimed before a judge, 'You have ruled in my favor against my opponent for two thousand rupees,' and the judge says, 'I do not remember this ruling.' Then the claimant brings two witnesses who testify that the judge ruled for two thousand. In this issue there is disagreement between the two Shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf says that the testimony of the two witnesses is not accepted due to the judge's denial. Muhammad says the testimony is accepted because it is possible that the judge forgot his ruling. This same disagreement occurs in the chapter of hadith: Abu Yusuf holds that when the shaykh denies, acting on the hadith is not permissible; Muhammad holds it is permissible. An example is the hadith: 'Rabi'a from Sahl from Abu Salih from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet (SAW) judged on the basis of one witness and an oath'—this hadith was narrated by Rabi'a from Sahl, but when Sahl was asked, he said, 'I do not remember.' So this hadith, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, is not actionable due to the shaykh's denial, but Imam al-Shafi'i acted on it. Similarly, there is a hadith: 'Sulayman ibn Musa from al-Zuhri from Urwa from Aisha that the Prophet (SAW) said: Any woman who marries without the permission of her guardian, her marriage is invalid, invalid, invalid'—Ibn Jurayj asked al-Zuhri about it, and al-Zuhri did not recognize it. So this hadith, according to Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa, is not actionable due to the shaykh's denial; but according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, it is actionable.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi internal dispute on whether a hadith can be acted upon when the shaykh (teacher) denies having narrated it. The denial can be categorical (jāḥid) — where the shaykh flatly rejects — leading to unanimous abandonment because one of the two must be lying. However, other narrations from the same narrator or shaykh remain valid. The disputed case is hesitant denial (mutaqif): the shaykh claims ignorance or forgetfulness. Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and a group of Hanafis say such a hadith is invalid (saqit al-i'tibar) because it creates discontinuity (inqita') in the chain; the author of the matn (likely al-Husami) prefers this view as closer to truth. Others, including Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, Imam al-Shafi'i, and Imam Malik, argue that hesitation does not amount to a defect (jarh), so the hadith remains actionable. The passage further explains that this disagreement is a branch (far') of a broader difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding a judge's memory: if a judge denies having issued a verdict but two witnesses testify otherwise, Abu Yusuf rejects the testimony (analogous to rejecting the hadith), while Muhammad accepts it (since the judge may have forgotten). Two examples illustrate the hadith dispute: (1) the hadith of judging by one witness and an oath (Rabi'a from Sahl — Sahl forgot); (2) the hadith of marriage without guardian (Sulayman ibn Musa from al-Zuhri — al-Zuhri did not recognize it). In both, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf reject the hadith, while Muhammad and al-Shafi'i accept it. This is a classic Hanafi usul dispute highlighting the weight given to continuity of the chain.

Key Terms
انکار متوقف (inkar mutawaqqif): A hesitant denial by the shaykh, such as claiming not to know or not to remember the hadith.
انقطاع (inqita'): Disconnection in the chain of transmission due to the shaykh's denial, making the hadith munqati'.
اشبه بالحق (ashbah bi al-haqq): The author's preference for a view, indicating it is closer to the truth in his judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's preferred view, why is a hadith rejected when the shaykh gives a hesitant denial?
A) Because the shaykh is definitely lying.
B) Because the hadith becomes disconnected (munqati') due to the denial.
C) Because the narrator is unreliable.
D) Because the hadith contradicts the Quran.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a shaykh's hesitant denial breaks the chain (inqita'), rendering the hadith munqati' and non-actionable, a view favored by Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and al-Karkhi.

Effect of Narrator's Denial on Hadith Acceptance
Dispute over acting upon a hadith when the narrator denies it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to DISTINGUISH the two types of narrator denial and APPLY the Hanafi rule of inqita' to determine whether a hadith remains actionable.

Core Idea
A narrator's denial of his own narration breaks the chain's continuity — the hadith becomes inactionable unless the denial is merely an error of memory.

When a narrator later denies having narrated a hadith, does this make the hadith unreliable? This passage presents a key Hanafi usul dispute where the school's leading imams differ, and it traces the disagreement to a deeper legal principle about judicial memory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of narrator denial
The text distinguishes between denial that causes no effect (the narrator's other narrations remain acceptable) and suspended denial (the narrator says 'I do not know' or 'I do not remember').
Only the second type triggers ikhtilaf.
2
Locate the ikhtilaf on the second type
Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and a group of Hanafis say that action falls away due to inqita' (discontinuity). Imam Muhammad and others say the hadith is still acted upon because denial does not create jarh.
The author prefers the first view as 'ashbah bi al-haqq'.
3
Understand the Hanafi majority dalil (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
A hadith is only a hujja if it is connected (mutassil) to the Prophet. Denial breaks this connection, so the hadith cannot be acted upon.
This is a condition of acceptance in usul.
4
Understand the opposing dalil (Imam Muhammad, al-Shafi'i, Malik)
The narrator's denial does not impugn the hadith because the narrator may have forgotten. The chain remains valid in itself.
Forgetfulness does not render a chain munqati'.
5
See the practical examples
The text gives two hadith examples (Rabi'a from Sahl on judging by one witness and an oath; Sulayman ibn Musa from al-Zuhri on marriage without guardian) and a judge analogy from the Sahibayn.
These illustrate the thamarah al-khilaf.

سے دوسری احادیث میں عیب پیدا نہ ہوگا، پس اس راوی اور شیخ کی دوسری روایات قابل قبول ہیں۔ (۲) دوسرے یہ کہ انکار متوقف ہو جیسے شیخ کہے میں تو حدیث کو نہیں جانتا، یا مجھے یاد نہیں کہ میں نے تیرے سامنے یہ حدیث بیان کی ہو، انکار کی اس صورت میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے، ابوالحسن کرخی اور حنفیہ کی ایک جماعت کہتی ہے کہ اس پر عمل کرنا ساقط ہو جائے گا، اور امام جی اور متکلمین کی ایک جماعت کہتی ہے کہ اس حدیث پر عمل کیا جائے گا، مصنف نے پہلے قول کو اشبه بالحق فرما یا یعنی حق کے زیادہ مشابہ اور قریب ہے، کیونکہ حدیث اسی وقت حجت بنتی ہے جب وہ رسول اللہ لا یا یہ ہم تک متصل ہو اور انکار کے سبب انقطاع پیدا ہو گیا۔ بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ حدیث پر عمل کا ساقط ہونا امام ابو یوسف کا قول ہے، اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس حدیث پر عمل جائز ہوگا کیونکہ مروی عنہ یعنی شیخ کے توقف سے حدیث میں کوئی جرح نہیں پیدا ہوا لہذا حدیث قابل عمل ہے، یہی امام شافعی اور امام مالک کا مذہب ہے۔ وهو فرع اختلافهما : - صاحبین کے درمیان یہ اختلاف ایک دوسرے مسئلہ میں ان کا جو اختلاف ہوا ہے اس کی فرع ہے، وہ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے قاضی کے سامنے دعوی کیا کہ آپ نے میرے لئے میرے فریق مخالف پر دو ہزار روپے کی مالیت کا فیصلہ کیا ہے، قاضی کہتا ہے مجھے تو یہ فیصلہ یاد نہیں، تو مدعی نے دو گواہ پیش کر دئے جو گواہی دے رہے ہیں کہ قاضی نے دو ہزار کی مالیت کا فیصلہ کیا ہے، تو اس مسئلہ میں صاحبین میں اختلاف ہے، امام ابو یوسف کہتے ہیں کہ قاضی کے انکار کی وجہ سے دو گواہوں کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی، اور امام محمد کہتے ہیں کہ شہادت قبول ہوگی کیونکہ امکان ہے کہ قاضی اپنا فیصلہ بھول رہا ہو یہی اختلاف صاحبین کا حدیث کے باب میں ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک شیخ کے انکار کی صورت میں حدیث پر عمل جائز نہیں اور امام محمد کے نزدیک عمل جائز ہے،اس کی مثال ربيعه عن سهل عن أبي صالح عن ابي هريرة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى بشاهد ويمين - حضور صلی شما اینم نے ایک گواہ اور ایک قسم پر فیصلہ کیا، یہ حدیث ربیعہ روایت کرتے ہیں سہل سے لیکن جب سہل سے پوچھا گیا تو سہل نے کہا مجھے تو یاد نہیں تو یہ حدیث امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام یوسف کے نزدیک مروی عنہ یعنی شیخ کے انکار کی وجہ سے قابل عمل نہیں، لیکن امام شافعی نے اس حدیث پر عمل کیا ۔۔ اسی طرح ایک حدیث ہے سليمان بن موسى عن الزهري عن عروة عن عائشه ان النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ايما امرأة نكحت بغير اذن وليها فنكاحها باطل باطل باطل - ابن جریج نے زہری سے سوال کیا تو زہری اس حدیث کو پہچان نہ سکے۔ تو یہ حدیث امام ابو یوسف اور امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک شیخ کے انکار کی وجہ سے قابل عمل نہیں، اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ حدیث قابل عمل ہے۔
will not cause defects in other hadiths, so the other narrations of this narrator and shaykh are acceptable. (2) Second: that denial is suspended, like the shaykh saying 'I do not know the hadith' or 'I do not remember narrating this hadith to you.' In this case of denial, there is a difference of opinion among scholars: Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and a group of Hanafis say that acting upon it falls away; and Imam [al-Ji?] and a group of mutakallimin say that the hadith is acted upon. The author considered the first statement closer to the truth (ashbah bi al-haqq), because a hadith is only a proof when it reaches us from the Messenger of Allah continuously, and due to denial, discontinuity occurs. Some say that the fall of action is the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf, and according to Imam Muhammad, acting upon this hadith is permissible because the shaykh's hesitation does not create any jarh (impugnment) in the hadith, so it is actionable. This is also the madhhab of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik. And it is a branch of their difference (huwa far' ikhtilafihima): The difference between the two companions is a branch of another issue in which they differed: that issue is that a man claimed before a judge, 'You have decided in my favor against my opponent for two thousand rupees.' The judge says, 'I do not remember this judgment.' Then the claimant produces two witnesses who testify that the judge decided for two thousand. In this issue, the two companions differ: Imam Abu Yusuf says that due to the judge's denial, the testimony of the two witnesses is not accepted; Imam Muhammad says the testimony is accepted because it is possible that the judge forgot his judgment. This same difference appears in the chapter of hadith: according to Imam Abu Yusuf, when the shaykh denies, the hadith is not actionable; according to Imam Muhammad, it is actionable. An example: Rabi'a from Sahl from Abu Salih from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged by one witness and an oath. This hadith is narrated by Rabi'a from Sahl, but when Sahl was asked, he said 'I do not remember.' So this hadith according to Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf is not actionable due to the shaykh's denial, but Imam al-Shafi'i acted upon it. Similarly, a hadith: Sulayman ibn Musa from al-Zuhri from Urwa from Aisha that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Any woman who marries without her guardian's permission, her marriage is invalid, invalid, invalid.' Ibn Jurayj asked al-Zuhri, and al-Zuhri did not recognize this hadith. So this hadith according to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Abu Hanifa is not actionable due to the shaykh's denial, but according to Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i it is actionable.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical usul al-fiqh issue: when a shaykh (narrator) from whom a hadith is transmitted denies having narrated it, does this denial preclude acting upon the hadith? The text presents two main positions. (1) The position of Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and a group of Hanafis, which the author considers 'closer to the truth' (ashbah bi al-haqq), holds that the denial creates discontinuity (inqita') in the chain, thus the hadith is no longer a valid proof (hujja). (2) The position of Imam Muhammad and a group of mutakallimin holds that the denial does not create jarh (impugnment) because the shaykh may have simply forgotten, so the hadith remains actionable. The text then explains that this disagreement is a branch (far') of a more fundamental disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding a judge's denial of his judgment: if a judge denies having made a judgment, but witnesses testify to it, Abu Yusuf rejects the witnesses (analogous to rejecting the hadith), while Muhammad accepts them (analogous to accepting the hadith). Two concrete hadith examples are given: the hadith on judging by one witness and an oath (hadith al-shahid wa al-yamin) narrated by Rabi'a from Sahl, where Sahl denied it; and the hadith on marriage without a guardian narrated by Sulayman ibn Musa from al-Zuhri, where al-Zuhri did not recognize it. In both cases, the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that due to the shaykh's denial, the hadith is not acted upon, while Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i accept it.

Key Terms
مروی عنہ (marwiyyun 'anhu): The person from whom the hadith is narrated (i.e., the shaykh/narrator).
انقطاع (inqita'): Discontinuity in the chain of transmission caused by the narrator's denial.
صاحبین (sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa.
جرح (jarh): Impugnment or criticism that weakens a narrator's reliability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Imam Abu Yusuf when a shaykh denies having narrated a hadith?
A) The hadith is still acted upon because denial does not create jarh.
B) The hadith is not acted upon due to discontinuity (inqita').
C) The hadith is accepted only if the shaykh retracts his denial.
D) The hadith is considered mursal.

Key Takeaway
When a narrator denies his narration, the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rejects the hadith due to inqita', while Imam Muhammad and others accept it because denial does not constitute jarh.

Vague Criticism (Ta'n Mubham) Does Not Impugn a Narrator
Stating the rule that vague criticism of a narrator is not accepted as jarh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that vague criticism (ta'n mubham) of a narrator is not accepted as jarh, and identify when explicit agreed-upon criticism is required.

Core Idea
Vague criticism never impugns; only explicit, agreed-upon jarh from a reliable critic disqualifies a narrator.

This lesson explains a fundamental principle of jarh wa ta'dil in Hanafi usul: vague statements like 'this narrator is not reliable' do not suffice to reject a hadith. The author draws an analogy with witnesses and stresses that only explicit impugnments from trustworthy scholars can affect a narrator's credibility. Understanding this rule is crucial for evaluating hadith authenticity in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making a vague criticism (ta'n mubham) about a narrator. The ruling is that it does not establish jarh (impugnment), so the narrator remains trustworthy.
2
Apply the analogy with witness testimony
Just as vague criticism of a witness (e.g., 'he is not a good person') does not disqualify him in court, similarly vague criticism of a narrator does not disqualify him.
3
Recognize the exception: explicit, agreed-upon criticism
If the criticism is explicit (mufassar) and contains something that is unanimously considered jarh (e.g., 'liar', 'adulterer'), and the critic is reliable and unbiased, then the narrator is impugned and his narration is abandoned.
4
Understand the condition of the critic
The critic must be from the imams of hadith, known for sincerity and reliability (nasiha and ithqan), and free from partisanship (ta'assub) and enmity ('adawa). Criticisms from biased critics are not accepted.

وَالطَّعْنُ الْمُبْهُمْ لَا يُوْجِبْ جَرْحًا فِي الرَّاوِئ كَمَا لَا يُوْجِبُهُ فِي الشَّاهِدِ وَلَا يَمْنَعْ الْعَمَلَ بِهِ إِلَّا إِذَا وَقَعَ مُفَسَرًا بِمَا هُوَ جَرْحٌ مُتَفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ مِمَّنْ اِشْتَهَرَ بِالنَّصِيْحَةِ وَالْإِثْقَانِ دُونَ التَّعَصُّبِ وَالْعَدَاوَةِ مِنْ اَئِمَةِ الْحَدِيثِ. ترجمہ :۔ اور طعن مبہم نہیں ثابت کرے گا جرح کو راوی میں، جیسا کہ طعن مہم نہیں ثابت کرتا ہے جرح کو شاہد میں اور طعن مبہم حدیث پر عمل سے نہیں روکے گا ، مگر یہ کہ طعن واقع ہو مفسر اس چیز کے ساتھ جو متفق علیہ جرح ہو ( اور طعن واقع ہو ) ان حضرات کی جانب سے جو مشہور ہیں خیر خواہی اور پختگی میں، نہ کہ تعصب اور عداوت میں یعنی وہ ائمہ حدیث میں سے ہو۔ تشریح:- اگر ائمہ حدیث میں سے کوئی حدیث پر جرح کرتا ہے مگر مہم الفاظ میں جیسے یوں کہے کہ یہ حدیث مجروح ہے، ثابت نہیں ہے، یا منکر ہے یا کہے انه غیر ثابت کہ یہ حدیث ثابت نہیں ہے تو یہ طعن مہم راوی میں جرح کو ثابت نہیں کرتا ہے، اور نہ ایسا طعن اس حدیث پر عمل کرنے سے مانع ہے جیسا کہ ایسا مبہم طعن شاہد میں بھی جرح کو ثابت نہیں کرتا ہے، یعنی کوئی گواہ پر مبہم طریقہ پر طعن کرے کہ یہ اچھا آدمی نہیں ہے، بیکار آدمی ہے وغیرہ تو اس سے گواہ مجروح نہ ہوگا، لہذا طعن مبہم سے نہ راوی مجروح ہوگا نہ اس کی روایت قابل ترک ہوگی۔ ہاں اگر طعن مفسر ہو، واضح طریقہ پر ہو کہ یہ راوی کذاب ہے ، عادل نہیں ہے، یا زانی ہے، یا چور ہے تو یہ سب الفاظ ایسے ہیں جو بالا تفاق جرح ہیں، اس سے راوی مجروح ہوگا اور اس کی روایت قابل عمل نہ ہوگی ، بشرطیکہ طعن کرنے والا ائمہ حدیث میں سے ہو، خیر خواہی اور پختگی میں مشہور ہو، تعصب اور عداوت سے دور ہو۔ اور اگر ایسے الفاظ سے طعن کرے جو بالا تفاق جرح نہ ہوں بلکہ بعض کے نزدیک جرح ہوں ، بعض کے نزدیک جرح نہ ہوں جیسے یوں کہے کہ یہ روایت کرنے کا عادی نہیں ہے، یا مسائل فقہ بکثرت بیان کرتا ہے، وغیرہ تو ایسے طعن سے راوی مجروح نہ ہوگا، اور اس کی حدیث کو ترک نہیں کیا جائے گا، کیونکہ یہ چیزیں بعض تعصب والوں کے نزدیک تو جرح ہوں گی ،محققین کے نزدیک جرح نہ ہوں گی ، بقول صاحب نامی ابن الجوزی، مجدالدین فیروز آبادی ، خطیب بغدادی، محدثو دار قطنی وغیرہ متعصب طائن ہیں، لہذا ان کے طعن سے راوی مجروح نہ ہو گا۔
Vague criticism (al-ta'n al-mubham) does not establish impugnment (jarh) in the narrator, just as it does not establish it in the witness. And it does not prevent acting upon [the hadith] unless it occurs explicitly (mufassaran) with something that is an agreed-upon impugnment (jarh muttafaq 'alayh), from those who are well-known for sincerity (nasiha) and reliability (ithqan), not from those of partisanship (ta'assub) and enmity (adawa), among the imams of hadith. Translation: Vague criticism does not prove jarh in the narrator, just as vague criticism does not prove jarh in the witness. And vague criticism does not prevent acting upon the hadith unless it occurs explicitly with something that is an agreed-upon impugnment from those who are famous for sincerity and reliability, not from partisanship and enmity, i.e., from the imams of hadith. Explanation: If one of the imams of hadith criticizes a hadith but in vague words, such as saying 'this hadith is impugned,' 'not established,' 'munkar,' or 'ghayr thabit,' this vague criticism does not establish jarh in the narrator, and such criticism does not prevent acting upon the hadith. Just as such vague criticism does not establish jarh in a witness: if someone vaguely criticizes a witness saying 'he is not a good person,' 'useless person,' etc., the witness is not impugned. Thus, vague criticism neither impugns the narrator nor makes his narration worthy of abandonment. Yes, if the criticism is explicit (mufassar) in a clear way, such as saying 'this narrator is a liar,' 'not just,' 'an adulterer,' 'a thief,' these are words that are agreed-upon as jarh, then the narrator becomes impugned and his narration is not actionable, provided that the critic is from the imams of hadith, famous for sincerity and reliability, and free from partisanship and enmity. If someone criticizes with words that are not agreed-upon as jarh, but some consider jarh and others do not — like saying 'he is not accustomed to narrating,' 'he frequently discusses fiqh issues,' etc. — then from such criticism the narrator is not impugned, and his hadith is not abandoned. Because these things are considered jarh only by some biased people, not by the researchers (muhaqqiqin). According to the author, people like Ibn al-Jawzi, Majd al-Din Firozabadi, Khatib al-Baghdadi, and the muhaddith Dar Qutni are biased critics, so their criticism does not impugn a narrator.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage explains a key principle in jarh wa ta'dil: vague (mubham) criticism of a narrator is not sufficient to impugn him or to discard his narration. The author draws an analogy with witnesses in court: if a witness is vaguely criticized ('he is not a good person'), the court does not reject him; similarly, a narrator cannot be rejected based on vague statements like 'this hadith is weak' or 'not established.' Only explicit, agreed-upon impugnments (such as accusing the narrator of lying, adultery, theft, or being unjust) can disqualify a narrator, and only if the critic is a reliable hadith scholar known for sincerity and accuracy, not for bias or personal enmity. The text further notes that even some explicit criticisms may not be accepted if they are not universally agreed upon as jarh; for example, saying 'he is not accustomed to narrating' is considered jarh by some biased critics but not by the expert researchers (muhaqqiqin). The author lists specific scholars (Ibn al-Jawzi, Firozabadi, Khatib al-Baghdadi, Dar Qutni) as examples of biased critics whose criticism should not be accepted. This rule ensures that narrators are not unfairly disqualified and that the hadith corpus remains reliable.

Key Terms
طعن مبہم (ta'n mubham): Vague criticism without specifying the exact defect, such as 'this hadith is not thabit' or 'the narrator is not reliable.'
جرح (jarh): Impugnment or defect that disqualifies a narrator or witness, rendering their testimony or narration unacceptable.
مفسر (mufassar): Explicit or detailed criticism that clearly states the defect, e.g., 'liar' or 'adulterer.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does vague criticism (ta'n mubham) prevent acting upon a hadith?
A) Never; vague criticism is always rejected.
B) When the critic is a famous scholar like Ibn al-Jawzi.
C) Only if the criticism is explicit (mufassar) with an agreed-upon impugnment from a reliable critic.
D) When the narrator fails to defend himself.

Key Takeaway
Vague criticism (ta'n mubham) does not impugn a narrator or prevent acting upon his hadith; only explicit, agreed-upon jarh from a reputable, unbiased critic suffices.

Vague Impugnment Does Not Discredit a Narrator
Ruling on vague criticism of narrators and witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a vague impugnment, apply the Hanafi rule that it does not discredit a narrator, and evaluate when an explicit impugnment (from a reliable, impartial scholar) requires rejecting a narration.

Core Idea
Vague criticism of a narrator or witness carries no legal weight; only specific, agreed-upon defects from impartial experts disqualify.

In hadith criticism, not all criticism is equal. A vague statement like 'this narrator is not good' does not legally discredit him or require abandoning his narration. This lesson explains the Hanafi rule that only explicit, unanimously agreed-upon defects (e.g., lying, theft) from known reliable and impartial scholars can establish jarh (discrediting). The same principle applies to witnesses in court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
First, identify the central ruling: vague impugnment (ta'n mubham) does not establish jarh in a narrator or witness. This is the foundational claim.
The term 'ta'n mubham' means criticism that does not specify the actual defect.
2
Note the Analogy
Observe the analogy drawn: the ruling for a narrator is the same as for a witness. This shows the principle applies across different contexts.
The analogy reinforces that the rule is general in Islamic legal procedure.
3
Recognize the Exception
Identify the exception: vague impugnment does prevent action only if the criticism is explicit (mufassar) and concerns a defect that is unanimously agreed upon, coming from a scholar known for sincerity and precision, free from bias.
The exception requires both specificity of the defect and reliability of the critic.
4
Apply to Biased Critics
Understand that criticism from a biased or partisan scholar (e.g., one known for ta'assub) is not accepted, even if explicit, because impartiality is a condition for valid jarh.
This protects narrators from unfair attacks based on sectarian or personal animosity.

وَالطَّعْنُ الْمُبْهُمْ لَا يُوْجِبْ جَرْحًا فِي الرَّاوِئ كَمَا لَا يُوْجِبُهُ فِي الشَّاهِدِ وَلَا يَمْنَعْ الْعَمَلَ بِهِ إِلَّا إِذَا وَقَعَ مُفَسَرًا بِمَا هُوَ جَرْحٌ مُتَفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ مِمَّنْ اِشْتَهَرَ بِالنَّصِيْحَةِ وَالْإِثْقَانِ دُونَ التَّعَصُّبِ وَالْعَدَاوَةِ مِنْ اَئِمَةِ الْحَدِيثِ. ترجمہ :۔ اور طعن مبہم نہیں ثابت کرے گا جرح کو راوی میں، جیسا کہ طعن مہم نہیں ثابت کرتا ہے جرح کو شاہد میں اور طعن مبہم حدیث پر عمل سے نہیں روکے گا ، مگر یہ کہ طعن واقع ہو مفسر اس چیز کے ساتھ جو متفق علیہ جرح ہو ( اور طعن واقع ہو ) ان حضرات کی جانب سے جو مشہور ہیں خیر خواہی اور پختگی میں، نہ کہ تعصب اور عداوت میں یعنی وہ ائمہ حدیث میں سے ہو۔ تشریح:- اگر ائمہ حدیث میں سے کوئی حدیث پر جرح کرتا ہے مگر مہم الفاظ میں جیسے یوں کہے کہ یہ حدیث مجروح ہے، ثابت نہیں ہے، یا منکر ہے یا کہے انه غیر ثابت کہ یہ حدیث ثابت نہیں ہے تو یہ طعن مہم راوی میں جرح کو ثابت نہیں کرتا ہے، اور نہ ایسا طعن اس حدیث پر عمل کرنے سے مانع ہے جیسا کہ ایسا مبہم طعن شاہد میں بھی جرح کو ثابت نہیں کرتا ہے، یعنی کوئی گواہ پر مبہم طریقہ پر طعن کرے کہ یہ اچھا آدمی نہیں ہے، بیکار آدمی ہے وغیرہ تو اس سے گواہ مجروح نہ ہوگا، لہذا طعن مبہم سے نہ راوی مجروح ہوگا نہ اس کی روایت قابل ترک ہوگی۔ ہاں اگر طعن مفسر ہو، واضح طریقہ پر ہو کہ یہ راوی کذاب ہے ، عادل نہیں ہے، یا زانی ہے، یا چور ہے تو یہ سب الفاظ ایسے ہیں جو بالا تفاق جرح ہیں، اس سے راوی مجروح ہوگا اور اس کی روایت قابل عمل نہ ہوگی ، بشرطیکہ طعن کرنے والا ائمہ حدیث میں سے ہو، خیر خواہی اور پختگی میں مشہور ہو، تعصب اور عداوت سے دور ہو۔ اور اگر ایسے الفاظ سے طعن کرے جو بالا تفاق جرح نہ ہوں بلکہ بعض کے نزدیک جرح ہوں ، بعض کے نزدیک جرح نہ ہوں جیسے یوں کہے کہ یہ روایت کرنے کا عادی نہیں ہے، یا مسائل فقہ بکثرت بیان کرتا ہے، وغیرہ تو ایسے طعن سے راوی مجروح نہ ہوگا، اور اس کی حدیث کو ترک نہیں کیا جائے گا، کیونکہ یہ چیزیں بعض تعصب والوں کے نزدیک تو جرح ہوں گی ،محققین کے نزدیک جرح نہ ہوں گی ، بقول صاحب نامی ابن الجوزی، مجدالدین فیروز آبادی ، خطیب بغدادی، محدثو دار قطنی وغیرہ متعصب طائن ہیں، لہذا ان کے طعن سے راوی مجروح نہ ہو گا۔
And vague impugnment does not establish jarh in the narrator, just as it does not establish it in the witness. And it does not prevent acting upon it unless the impugnment is explicit (mufassaran) with something that is a unanimously agreed upon jarh from those who are known for sincerity and precision, not from partisanship and enmity, from the imams of hadith.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage states a key rule in hadith criticism: a vague attack on a narrator's credibility does not actually prove any defect, nor does it require us to abandon the hadith. The rule is illustrated by analogy to court witnesses: if someone vaguely says a witness is 'not good', the witness is not discredited. Only specific, agreed-upon accusations (like lying, adultery, theft) from reliable, impartial hadith scholars can disqualify a narrator. The commentary explains that if the critic is known for bias, his criticism is not accepted.

Key Terms
طعن مبهم (ta'n mubham): Vague impugnment that does not specify the defect.
جرح (jarh): Discrediting a narrator or witness, rendering their testimony or narration unacceptable.
مفسر (mufassar): Explicit, detailed explanation of the defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a vague impugnment (ta'n mubham) cause a narrator's hadith to be rejected?
A) Always, because any criticism raises doubt.
B) Only if the criticism is explicit and from a reliable, impartial scholar.
C) Only if it comes from a biased critic.
D) Never, because narrators are always trustworthy.

Key Takeaway
Vague impugnment does not discredit a narrator; only explicit, agreed-upon defects from impartial experts establish jarh.

The Pillar and Condition of Ta'arud
Defines rukn and shart of ta'arud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rukn (pillar) and shart (condition) of ta'arud and apply them to distinguish genuine conflict from apparent contradiction.

Core Idea
Ta'arud requires two equal-strength proofs on the same subject at the same time. Without equality or unity, there is no true conflict.

The author of al-Husami explains that not every contradiction between proofs is a genuine conflict (ta'arud). True ta'arud has a pillar (rukn) and a condition (shart) that must both be satisfied. Understanding these prevents the scholar from mistakenly claiming conflict where none exists, thereby ensuring correct legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rukn
The rukn of ta'arud is equality in strength (qawwa) between the two proofs. One proof must not surpass the other in essence or attribute; otherwise, the stronger is preferred and there is no conflict.
Examples: mutawatir vs. mashhur, mashhur vs. khabar wahid, 'amm vs. khass – these are not equal, so no ta'arud.
2
Identify the shart
The shart is that the two proofs establish opposite rulings on the same locus (mahall) at the same time (waqt). If time or locus differs, there is no ta'arud.
Example: wine was halal then haram – different times, no conflict. Marriage with mahram vs. non-mahram – different loci, no conflict.
3
Apply the rukn to a pair
Given two proofs, assess their strength categories. If they are not equal, the stronger is taken and no conflict exists.
Example: a mutawatir hadith and a mashhur hadith on the same ruling – the mutawatir is stronger, so tarjih (preference) is applied, not ta'arud.
4
Apply the shart to a pair
Check if both proofs address the exact same subject and time. If they refer to different subjects or different periods, they are not in ta'arud.
Example: one proof permits marrying non-mahram women, another prohibits marrying mahram women – the loci differ, so no conflict.
5
Distinguish from apparent contradiction
Many apparent contradictions are resolved by checking rukn and shart. A student must not rush to claim ta'arud without verifying these two elements.
This is a common error – assuming any contradiction is a conflict.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم التعارض انما يتحقق مصنف معارضہ کا حکم بیان کرنے کے بعد رکن اور شرط کو ایک ساتھ بیان کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ تعارض متحقق ہونے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ دو حجتیں قوت میں برابر ہوں، کوئی ایک حجت ذات وصفت میں دوسری حجت سے بڑھ کر نہ ہو، ورنہ تعارض نہیں کہا جائے گا، بلکہ قوی حجت کو ضعیف پر ترجیح ہوگی، لہذا خبر متواتر اور مشہور مشہور اور خبر واحد ، عام مخصوص منہ البعض اور خاص ، ان میں مساوات نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک دوسری پر ذات کے اعتبار سے بڑھی ہوئی ہے ، لہذا تعارض ثابت نہ ہوگا تو گویا دو مجنتوں میں تساوی فی القوة رکن معارضہ ہے۔

معارضہ کی شرط یہ ہے کہ دو حجتوں میں سے ایک حجت ایک حکم کو ثابت کرتی ہو اور دوسری اس کی ضد کو ثابت کرتی ہو، اور دونوں کا وقت بھی ایک ہو محل بھی ایک ہو، ورنہ تعارض ثابت نہ ہوگا، جیسے شراب ابتدائے اسلام میں حلال تھی ،ایک حجت سے، پھر حرام ہو گئی دوسری حجت سے ، تو حلت و حرمت دونوں ثابت ہیں، مگر ایک ہی وقت میں نہیں بلکہ الگ الگ وقت ہے تو اتحاد وقت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تعارض متحقق نہ ہوگا، اسی طرح غیر محرمات سے نکاح کی حلت یک دلیل و حجت سے ثابت ہے اور محرمات سے نکاح کی حرمت دوسری دلیل سے ثابت ہے، تو حلت وحرمت دونوں کا محل الگ الگ ہے، حلت کا مل غیر محرمات ہیں، اور حرمت کا عمل محرمات ہیں تو اتحاد مل نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے معارضہ ثابت نہ ہوگا۔

وَاخْتَلَفَ مَشَائِخْنَا فِي أَنَّ خَبَرَ النَّفْيِ هَلْ يُعَارِضُ خَبَرَ الْإِثْبَاتِ أَمْ لَا وَاخْتَلَفَ عَمَلُ أَصْحَابِنَا الْمُتَقَدِ مِينَ فِي ذَلِكَ فَقَدْ رُوِيَ أَنَّ بَرِيْرَةَ أَعْتِقَتْ وَزَوْجُهَا عَبْدٌ وَرُوِيَ أَنَّهَا أُعْتِقَتْ وَزَوْجُهَا حُرِّمَعَ اِتِّفَاقِهِمْ عَلَى إِنَّهُ كَانَ عَبْدًا فَأَصْحَابُنَا اَخَذَوْا بِالْمُثْبِت وَرُوِيَ أَنَّ رَسُوْلَ الله صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ تَزَوَجَ مَيْمُوْنَةَ وَهُوَ حَلَالٌ وَرُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ تَزَوَجَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمْ وَاتَّفَقَتِ الرِّوَايَاتُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي الْحِلِ الْاَصْلِي فَجَعَلَ أَصْحَابُنَا الْعَمَلَ بِالنَّافِي أَوْلَى وَقَالُو فِي الْجَرْح وَالتَّعْدِيْلِ اَنَّ الْجَرحَ أَوْلى وَهُوَ المُثبت. ترجمہ : ۔ اور ہمارے مشائخ نے اختلاف کیا ہے اس بارے میں کہ کیا نفی کی خبر اثبات کی خبر سے معارض ہوتی ہے یا نہیں؟ اور اس بارے میں ہمارے اصحاب متقدمین کا عمل مختلف ہے، پس روایت کی گئی کہ بریرہ آزاد کی گئی اس
Then ta'arud (conflict) is only realized – the author after stating the ruling of mu'arada states the rukn (pillar) and shart (condition) together. He says: For ta'arud to be realized, it is necessary that the two proofs be equal in strength; no proof surpass the other in essence or attribute; otherwise it is not called ta'arud, but rather the stronger proof is given preference over the weaker. Therefore, mutawatir and mashhur, mashhur and khabar wahid, 'amm and khas (with some specificity), and khas – there is no equality between them; rather, one exceeds the other in essence. Hence ta'arud is not established. So effectively, equality in strength is the rukn of mu'arada. 

The condition of mu'arada is that one of the two proofs establishes a ruling and the other establishes its opposite, and their time is one and their locus (mahall) is one. Otherwise ta'arud is not established. For example, wine was halal in early Islam by one proof, then became haram by another proof; both rulings (permissibility and prohibition) are established, but not at the same time – there is no unity of time, so ta'arud is not realized. Similarly, the permissibility of marriage with non-mahram women is established by one proof, and the prohibition of marriage with mahram women is established by another proof; the loci are different: the locus of permissibility is non-mahram women, and the locus of prohibition is mahram women. So due to lack of unity of locus, mu'arada is not established. 

And our mashayikh differed on whether a negative report (khabar al-nafi) contradicts a positive report (khabar al-ithbat) or not. And the practice of our early companions differed in that. For it is narrated that Barira was freed and her husband was a slave, and it is narrated that she was freed and her husband was free, with their agreement that he had been a slave. Our companions took the positive [report]. And it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) married Maymuna while he was halal (non-muhrim), and it is narrated that he married her while he was muhrim. The reports agreed that he was not in original halal. So our companions considered acting on the negative report as more appropriate, and they said in jarh and ta'dil that jarh is more appropriate, and it is the positive [report]. Translation: The Urdu translation of the Arabic passage.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on ta'arud by defining its rukn (pillar) and shart (condition). The rukn is equality in strength (qawwa) between the two proofs. If one is stronger, there is no ta'arud; the stronger is preferred. Examples: mutawatir is stronger than mashhur, mashhur stronger than khabar wahid; 'amm and khas are not equal because khas is more specific and thus stronger. The shart is that the two proofs establish opposite rulings on the same subject (mahall) at the same time (waqt). If time differs (e.g., wine initially halal then haram) or locus differs (marriage with mahram vs non-mahram), no conflict arises. 

The passage then addresses a specific dispute among Hanafi scholars: Can a negative report (report negating a ruling) conflict with a positive report (report affirming a ruling)? Our mashayikh differed, and early Hanafis had varying practices. Two examples are given: (1) Barira's emancipation: one report says her husband was a slave, another says he was free; our companions accepted the positive report (that he was a slave). (2) The Prophet's marriage to Maymuna: one says he was halal, another says he was muhrim; reports agreed he was not in original halal, so our companions gave preference to the negative report (that he was not halal, i.e., he was muhrim). This is compared to the principle in jarh wa ta'dil that jarh (impugning a narrator) is given preference over ta'dil (declaring him trustworthy), and jarh is positive (affirms a defect). Thus, the ruling is not absolute but depends on circumstances.

Key Terms
التعارض (al-taʿāruḍ): Conflict between two proofs that require opposite rulings on the same subject at the same time.
الركن (al-rukn): The essential pillar of ta'arud: equality in strength between the two proofs.
الشرط (al-sharṭ): The condition for ta'arud: that the two proofs establish opposite rulings on the same locus (mahall) at the same time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for ta'arud?
A) Equality in strength between the two proofs
B) Unity of time between the two rulings
C) Unity of locus (subject) between the two rulings
D) Both proofs must be from the Quran

Key Takeaway
Ta'arud only arises when two equally strong proofs conflict on the same subject at the same time; otherwise, it is a false conflict or a case of preference.

Negative vs Positive Reports: Do They Conflict?
Discusses dispute on negative vs positive reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether a negative report (khabar al-nafi) conflicts with a positive report (khabar al-ithbat), and apply the principle that no absolute rule exists, using case examples.

Core Idea
Hanafi scholars differ: a negative report may or may not conflict with a positive one; early practice shows case-by-case judgment.

After establishing the general conditions for ta'arud, the text raises a specific controversy: Does a report that negates a ruling (e.g., 'he was not married') contradict a report that affirms it (e.g., 'he was married')? The Hanafi mashayikh disagreed, and early companions sometimes preferred the positive, sometimes the negative. This lesson explores the evidence and practical consequences, showing that no single rule governs all cases.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
The question is whether a negative report (khabar al-nafi) is considered to be in ta'arud with a positive report (khabar al-ithbat). The Hanafi mashayikh differed on this.
This is an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf; no single madhhab position.
2
Examine the Barira case
In the Barira case, one report said her husband was a slave (positive), another said he was free (negative). The early companions took the positive report.
They preferred the affirming report in this instance.
3
Examine the Maymuna case
Regarding the Prophet's marriage to Maymuna, one report said he was halal (positive), another said he was muhrim (negative). Here the companions preferred the negative report.
This shows the opposite preference.
4
Compare with jarh wa ta'dil
In jarh wa ta'dil, the positive report (jarh) is preferred over the negative (ta'dil). This is an example where the positive is stronger, but it is not absolute.
This analogy is given but not applied universally.
5
Conclude on the Hanafi position
There is no fixed rule. A mufti must evaluate each case on its own merits, considering additional evidence and context.
The text reports the ikhtilaf without resolving it, leaving it to ijtihad.

ثم التعارض انما يتحقق مصنف معارضہ کا حکم بیان کرنے کے بعد رکن اور شرط کو ایک ساتھ بیان کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ تعارض متحقق ہونے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ دو حجتیں قوت میں برابر ہوں، کوئی ایک حجت ذات وصفت میں دوسری حجت سے بڑھ کر نہ ہو، ورنہ تعارض نہیں کہا جائے گا، بلکہ قوی حجت کو ضعیف پر ترجیح ہوگی، لہذا خبر متواتر اور مشہور مشہور اور خبر واحد ، عام مخصوص منہ البعض اور خاص ، ان میں مساوات نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک دوسری پر ذات کے اعتبار سے بڑھی ہوئی ہے ، لہذا تعارض ثابت نہ ہوگا تو گویا دو مجنتوں میں تساوی فی القوة رکن معارضہ ہے۔

معارضہ کی شرط یہ ہے کہ دو حجتوں میں سے ایک حجت ایک حکم کو ثابت کرتی ہو اور دوسری اس کی ضد کو ثابت کرتی ہو، اور دونوں کا وقت بھی ایک ہو محل بھی ایک ہو، ورنہ تعارض ثابت نہ ہوگا، جیسے شراب ابتدائے اسلام میں حلال تھی ،ایک حجت سے، پھر حرام ہو گئی دوسری حجت سے ، تو حلت و حرمت دونوں ثابت ہیں، مگر ایک ہی وقت میں نہیں بلکہ الگ الگ وقت ہے تو اتحاد وقت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تعارض متحقق نہ ہوگا، اسی طرح غیر محرمات سے نکاح کی حلت یک دلیل و حجت سے ثابت ہے اور محرمات سے نکاح کی حرمت دوسری دلیل سے ثابت ہے، تو حلت وحرمت دونوں کا محل الگ الگ ہے، حلت کا مل غیر محرمات ہیں، اور حرمت کا عمل محرمات ہیں تو اتحاد مل نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے معارضہ ثابت نہ ہوگا۔

وَاخْتَلَفَ مَشَائِخْنَا فِي أَنَّ خَبَرَ النَّفْيِ هَلْ يُعَارِضُ خَبَرَ الْإِثْبَاتِ أَمْ لَا وَاخْتَلَفَ عَمَلُ أَصْحَابِنَا الْمُتَقَدِ مِينَ فِي ذَلِكَ فَقَدْ رُوِيَ أَنَّ بَرِيْرَةَ أَعْتِقَتْ وَزَوْجُهَا عَبْدٌ وَرُوِيَ أَنَّهَا أُعْتِقَتْ وَزَوْجُهَا حُرِّمَعَ اِتِّفَاقِهِمْ عَلَى إِنَّهُ كَانَ عَبْدًا فَأَصْحَابُنَا اَخَذَوْا بِالْمُثْبِت وَرُوِيَ أَنَّ رَسُوْلَ الله صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ تَزَوَجَ مَيْمُوْنَةَ وَهُوَ حَلَالٌ وَرُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ تَزَوَجَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمْ وَاتَّفَقَتِ الرِّوَايَاتُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي الْحِلِ الْاَصْلِي فَجَعَلَ أَصْحَابُنَا الْعَمَلَ بِالنَّافِي أَوْلَى وَقَالُو فِي الْجَرْح وَالتَّعْدِيْلِ اَنَّ الْجَرحَ أَوْلى وَهُوَ المُثبت. ترجمہ : ۔ اور ہمارے مشائخ نے اختلاف کیا ہے اس بارے میں کہ کیا نفی کی خبر اثبات کی خبر سے معارض ہوتی ہے یا نہیں؟ اور اس بارے میں ہمارے اصحاب متقدمین کا عمل مختلف ہے، پس روایت کی گئی کہ بریرہ آزاد کی گئی اس
Then ta'arud (conflict) is only realized – the author after stating the ruling of mu'arada states the rukn (pillar) and shart (condition) together. He says: For ta'arud to be realized, it is necessary that the two proofs be equal in strength; no proof surpass the other in essence or attribute; otherwise it is not called ta'arud, but rather the stronger proof is given preference over the weaker. Therefore, mutawatir and mashhur, mashhur and khabar wahid, 'amm and khas (with some specificity), and khas – there is no equality between them; rather, one exceeds the other in essence. Hence ta'arud is not established. So effectively, equality in strength is the rukn of mu'arada. 

The condition of mu'arada is that one of the two proofs establishes a ruling and the other establishes its opposite, and their time is one and their locus (mahall) is one. Otherwise ta'arud is not established. For example, wine was halal in early Islam by one proof, then became haram by another proof; both rulings (permissibility and prohibition) are established, but not at the same time – there is no unity of time, so ta'arud is not realized. Similarly, the permissibility of marriage with non-mahram women is established by one proof, and the prohibition of marriage with mahram women is established by another proof; the loci are different: the locus of permissibility is non-mahram women, and the locus of prohibition is mahram women. So due to lack of unity of locus, mu'arada is not established. 

And our mashayikh differed on whether a negative report (khabar al-nafi) contradicts a positive report (khabar al-ithbat) or not. And the practice of our early companions differed in that. For it is narrated that Barira was freed and her husband was a slave, and it is narrated that she was freed and her husband was free, with their agreement that he had been a slave. Our companions took the positive [report]. And it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) married Maymuna while he was halal (non-muhrim), and it is narrated that he married her while he was muhrim. The reports agreed that he was not in original halal. So our companions considered acting on the negative report as more appropriate, and they said in jarh and ta'dil that jarh is more appropriate, and it is the positive [report]. Translation: The Urdu translation of the Arabic passage.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on ta'arud by defining its rukn (pillar) and shart (condition). The rukn is equality in strength (qawwa) between the two proofs. If one is stronger, there is no ta'arud; the stronger is preferred. Examples: mutawatir is stronger than mashhur, mashhur stronger than khabar wahid; 'amm and khas are not equal because khas is more specific and thus stronger. The shart is that the two proofs establish opposite rulings on the same subject (mahall) at the same time (waqt). If time differs (e.g., wine initially halal then haram) or locus differs (marriage with mahram vs non-mahram), no conflict arises. 

The passage then addresses a specific dispute among Hanafi scholars: Can a negative report (report negating a ruling) conflict with a positive report (report affirming a ruling)? Our mashayikh differed, and early Hanafis had varying practices. Two examples are given: (1) Barira's emancipation: one report says her husband was a slave, another says he was free; our companions accepted the positive report (that he was a slave). (2) The Prophet's marriage to Maymuna: one says he was halal, another says he was muhrim; reports agreed he was not in original halal, so our companions gave preference to the negative report (that he was not halal, i.e., he was muhrim). This is compared to the principle in jarh wa ta'dil that jarh (impugning a narrator) is given preference over ta'dil (declaring him trustworthy), and jarh is positive (affirms a defect). Thus, the ruling is not absolute but depends on circumstances.

Key Terms
خبر النفي (khabar al-nafī): A report that negates a ruling or state.
خبر الإثبات (khabar al-ithbāt): A report that affirms a ruling or state.
الجرح والتعديل (al-jarḥ wa al-taʿdīl): The science of impugning and validating narrators in hadith criticism.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mashayikh, how should a mufti decide between a negative report and a positive report?
A) Always prefer the positive report.
B) Always prefer the negative report.
C) There is no fixed rule; it depends on the case.
D) Prefer the report with more narrators.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not have a uniform rule on whether negative reports conflict with positive ones; each case must be assessed individually.

Prophetic Silence as Expression by Necessity
Defines second type of expression by necessity through speaker's state

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the second type of bayān bi al-ḍarūra (by speaker's state) and apply the principle that the Prophet's silence on an action indicates its permissibility in Hanafi uṣūl.

Core Idea
The Prophet's silence is proof of permissibility when he would have spoken if it were wrong.

In this lesson, we explore the second type of expression by necessity, which is derived from the state of the speaker rather than his words. The most important instance is the Prophet's (ﷺ) silence upon witnessing an action. Hanafi jurists treat this tacit approval (taqrīr) as a valid source of law, establishing the permissibility of customary transactions and practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of bayān
The passage distinguishes two types of bayān bi al-ḍarūra. The second type depends on the speaker's state (ḥāl al-mutakallim). Recognize that here the speaker is the Lawgiver (the Prophet ﷺ).
The first type (not discussed here) relies on the necessity of the context itself; this type relies on observable behavior.
2
Recognize the key scenario
The Prophet (ﷺ) sees people engaging in transactions—buying, selling, eating, drinking—and remains silent. Note that he did not disapprove or order changes.
The silence occurs in a context where he is present and capable of speaking.
3
Understand the legal inference
His silence, given his role as a lawgiver obligated to correct error, proves that the actions are permissible (mubāḥ) and not wrong. This is the core legal reasoning: if they were invalid, he would have intervened.
This reasoning is based on the principle that the Prophet does not remain silent on falsehood.
4
Apply the principle generally
Generalize: prophetic silence in contexts where disapproval would be expected indicates ibāḥa (permissibility). This applies to any action witnessed by the Prophet without his objection.
Hanafi uṣūl treats this as a type of sunnah taqrīriyya—the Prophet's tacit approval.
5
Note the condition for validity
The silence must occur in a context where the Prophet would have spoken if the action were prohibited or invalid. Not all silences are proof; the context must demand a response if the action were wrong.
This condition distinguishes valid taqrīr from mere neglect or ignorance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنه ما يثبت - بیان ضرورت کی دوسری قسم یہ ہے کہ متکلم کی حالت کی دلالت سے وہ بیان مفہوم ہو جیسے شارع کا کسی فعل کو دیکھ کر سکوت کرنا اور اس پر نکیر نہ کرنا یہ دلیل و بیان ہے اس بات کا کہ یہ فعل مباح ہے ، غلط نہیں ہے، مثلاً آپ سلیم کا لوگوں کو خرید وفروخت ، کھانے پینے وغیرہ معاملات کرتے دیکھنا اور آپ صلی الہ سلم کی اس پر سکوت کرنا، تغیر و تبدل اور نکیر نہ کرنا یہ دلیل ہے ان معاملات کے درست ہونے کی ، اگر درست نہ ہوتے تو آپ نکیر فرماتے ، تبد یلی فرماتے ، غرض اس طرح کا سکوت بیان سمجھا جائے گا۔
And from it is that which is established; the second type of expression by necessity is that the meaning is understood by the indication of the speaker's state, such as the Lawgiver's silence upon seeing an action and not disapproving it. That is proof and expression that the action is permissible, not wrong. For example, the Prophet (peace be upon him) seeing people doing transactions like buying, selling, eating, drinking, and his silence upon that, not changing or disapproving, is proof of the correctness of these transactions. If they were not correct, he would have disapproved and changed. So such silence is considered expression.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage defines the second type of expression by necessity (بیان ضرورت), which is based on the state or conduct of the speaker (in this case, the Lawgiver – the Prophet ﷺ). The Prophet's silence when witnessing customary transactions (buying, selling, etc.) is taken as an indication that those actions are permissible and correct. This is a well-known principle in Hanafi usul: 'the Prophet's silence on an action in his presence is evidence of its permissibility' (sukūt al-nabī ʿalā al-fiʿl dalīl al-ibāḥa). The reasoning is that if the action were prohibited or invalid, the Prophet would have spoken up and corrected it. This type of expression is called 'by the speaker's state' because the meaning is derived not from explicit words but from the Lawgiver's observable behavior and tacit approval.

Key Terms
حال المتكلم (ḥāl al-mutakallim): The state or condition of the speaker that indicates a ruling, e.g., silence or action.
دلالة الحال (dalālat al-ḥāl): Indication by the context of the situation rather than explicit text.
سكوت (sukūt): Silence; here, the Prophet's silence when witnessing actions, which is evidence of permissibility when he would have spoken if it were wrong.
تقرير (taqrīr): Tacit approval; the Prophet's silence or lack of objection to an action, considered a type of sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the Prophet's silence on people's transactions indicate?
A) The transactions are invalid
B) The transactions are permissible
C) The transactions require further evidence
D) The transactions are obligatory

Key Takeaway
The second type of expression by necessity, derived from the speaker's state (prophetic silence), is a valid Hanafi source establishing permissibility.
