Classification of Prophet's Actions in Hanafi Usul
Describes the four categories of Prophet's actions with Hanafi classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of the Prophet's actions (mubah, mustahab, wajib, fard) and explain the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib based on evidence certainty.

Core Idea
Prophet's actions vary in legal weight: fard (certain proof) vs wajib (speculative proof) impacts obligation for the ummah.

In this passage from a Hanafi usul commentary, the author explains that the actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) are classified into four categories—mubah, mustahab, wajib, and fard—based on their evidentiary strength and the resulting obligation on the community. A fifth category, zallah (lapse), is excluded from emulation. This classification is crucial for understanding how prophetic actions become legal sources, specially the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four main categories
List the four categories: mubah (permissible), mustahab (recommended), wajib (obligatory with zanni proof), fard (obligatory with qat'i proof).
Wajib is distinct from fard in Hanafi usul.
2
Understand the basis for each category
Mubah: acts like eating, drinking; no reward or sin. Mustahab: acts like saying Bismillah in wudu; reward for doing, no sin for leaving. Wajib: acts like sujud al-sahw; proven by speculative evidence. Fard: acts like the pillars of prayer; proven by definitive evidence.
The evidence strength determines the level of obligation.
3
Explain the Hanafi fard/wajib distinction
Fard is proved by qat'i (certain) evidence (e.g., Quran, mutawatir hadith); wajib by zanni (speculative) evidence (e.g., ahad hadith). This distinction is unique to Hanafis; other schools often treat them as synonymous.
This affects the ruling: missing a fard requires repeating the act, missing a wajib requires compensation (e.g., sujud al-sahw).
4
Recognize the status of zallah
Zallah are unintentional lapses (e.g., the Prophet falling while walking) that are not to be emulated. They are always accompanied by an indication that they are lapses.
They are not a legal source.
5
Address the objection: why four categories instead of three?
Some usulis classify actions as mubah, mustahab, and fard only, including wajib in fard. The Hanafi response: the classification is from the ummah's perspective; for us, some actions are proven by zanni evidence, so wajib is a separate category.
The Prophet's own actions are all certain, but their evidentiary value for us differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالَّذِي يَتَّصِلُ بِالسُّنَنِ أَفْعَالُ رَسُوْلِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَهِيَ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسَامٍ مُبَاحٌ وَمُسْتَحَبْ وَوَاجِبْ وَفَرْضٌ وَفِيهَا قِسْمْ أخَرُ وَهُوَ الزَّلَةُ لكِنَّهُ لَيْسَ مِنْ هَذَا الْبَابِ فِي شَيْءٍ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَصْلَحُ لِلْاِقْتِدَاءِ وَلَا يَخْلُوْا عَنِ الْإِقْتِرَانِ بِبَيَانٍ أَنَّهُ زَلَةٌ ترجمہ :۔ اور وہ جو متصل ہیں سنن قولیہ کے ساتھ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے افعال ہیں ، اور وہ چار قسم پر ہیں ، مباح، مستحب ، واجب اور فرض ، اور ان افعال میں ایک دوسری قسم بھی ہے، اور وہ زلت ( چوک لغزش ) ہے، لیکن یہ قسم کسی بھی حکم میں اس باب سے یعنی باب اقتدا سے نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ یہ قسم اقتدا کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی ہے، اور یہ قسم اس بات کے بیان کے متصل ہونے سے خالی نہیں ہے کہ یہ ذلت ہے۔ تشریح:- مصنف سنن قولیہ کے بیان سے فارغ ہو کر سفن فعلیہ کو بیان کر رہے ہیں، سنن فعلیہ کا درجہ سنن قولیہ کے بعد ہے، اس لئے اس کو سنن قولیہ کے بعد بیان کیا، افعال رسول سے وہ افعال مراد ہیں جو آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے بالقصد صادر ہوئے ہوں، حالت نوم میں یا سہو صدور ہوا ہو تو اس کی اقتدا نہ ہوگی، اور نہ وہ فعل حسن و قبیح سے متصف ہوگا۔ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے افعال چار طرح کے ہیں، (۱) مباح جیسے کھانا، پینا، لباس و غیره (۲) مستحب جیسے تسمیہ فی الوضوء ڈاڑھی کا خلال کرنا، (۳) واجب جیسے سجدہ سہو (۴) فرض جیسے، فرائض ، نماز ، روزہ وغیرہ۔ یہاں یہ شبہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ تمام اصولیین نے افعال کی تین قسمیں، مباح، مستحب اور فرض بیان کی ہیں، واجب کو فرض میں شامل کیا ہے، کیونکہ واجب اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کا ثبوت ایسی دلیل سے ہو جس میں شبہ اور اضطراب ہو اور آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے کسی بھی فعل میں شبہ کا حق نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ تقسیم ہمارے اعتبار سے ہے نبی علیہ السلام کے اعتبار سے نہیں ہے، اور ہمارے حق میں بعض افعال دلیل ظنی سے ثابت ہیں، لہذا ہمارے حق میں واجب متحقق ہوگا۔ مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ ان مذکورہ چار قسموں کے علاوہ ایک قسم اور ہے جس کو ذلت کہتے ہیں، یعنی چوک ہو جانا، لغزش ، وہ یہ کہ کسی کام کے کرنے کا ارادہ نہ ہو اور بلا قصد ہو جائے اور وہ اس پر ثابت نہ رہے جیسے راستہ چلتے ہوئے گر پڑا، گرنے کا ارادہ نہ تھا، مگر گر پڑا پھر کھڑا ہو گیا، پڑا نہیں رہا، یہ زلت کہلاتا ہے جیسے موسیٰ علیہ السلام نے گھونسہ مارا،
And that which is connected to the verbal sunnahs are the actions of Allah's Messenger, peace be upon him, and these are four categories: permissible, recommended, obligatory, and mandatory. There is another category: the lapse, but it does not belong to this chapter at all because it is not suitable for emulation and it does not lack being accompanied by a statement that it is a lapse. Translation: And that which is connected to the verbal sunnahs are the actions of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and they are four types: permissible, recommended, obligatory, and mandatory. And among these actions there is another type, called zallah (mistake/lapse), but this type is in no ruling from this chapter, i.e., the chapter of emulation, because this type does not possess the capacity for emulation, and it does not lack being accompanied by a statement that it is a lapse. Commentary: The author, after finishing the discussion of verbal sunnahs, is now discussing the practical sunnahs. The status of practical sunnahs is after verbal sunnahs, so he mentioned them after. The actions of the Messenger refer to those actions that he performed intentionally; actions done in sleep or forgetfulness cannot be emulated and are not characterized as good or bad. The actions of the Prophet are of four kinds: (1) permissible, like eating, drinking, clothing, etc.; (2) recommended, like saying tasmiya in wudu, combing the beard; (3) obligatory, like prostration of forgetfulness; (4) mandatory, like the obligatory parts of prayer, fasting, etc. Here a doubt may arise: All usul scholars mention three kinds: permissible, recommended, and mandatory; they include wajib in fard, because wajib is that which is proven by a proof containing doubt and uncertainty, and the Prophet's actions cannot contain doubt. The answer is that this division is from our perspective, not from the Prophet's perspective; for us, some actions are proven by speculative evidence, so for us wajib is realized. The author says that besides these four kinds, there is another kind called zallah, i.e., a mistake. For example, when an action is not intended but happens unintentionally and he does not persist in it, like while walking one falls without intending, then gets up; this is called zallah, like Musa (peace be upon him) striking a blow.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage defines the categories of actions of the Prophet (saw) from a Hanafi usul perspective. The author states that after verbal sunnahs (qawliyya), we consider actions (fi'liyya). The Prophet's actions are divided into four types: mubah (permissible, e.g., eating), mustahab (recommended, e.g., saying Bismillah in wudu), wajib (obligatory, e.g., sujud al-sahw), and fard (mandatory, e.g., the pillars of prayer). A fifth category, zallah (lapse), is actions done unintentionally or in error; these are not to be emulated. The text addresses an objection: some usulis only list three categories (mubah, mustahab, fard) because they consider wajib subsumed under fard, since wajib is proven by zanni (speculative) evidence, while the Prophet's actions are certain. The answer given is that the classification is from the perspective of the ummah, not the Prophet himself. For the Prophet, all his intentional actions are certain, but for us, the evidentiary value may differ, so we distinguish between wajib (zanni proof) and fard (qat'i proof). This is a classic Hanafi distinction. The passage concludes by explaining zallah with examples. Notably, the Hanafi school uses this division to determine fiqh rulings, e.g., whether an action is necessary or recommended for followers. Authority weight: This is from the Husami commentary, representing later Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
مباح (mubah): An action of the Prophet that is permissible; doing it is not rewarded nor sinful.
مستحب (mustahab): An action of the Prophet that is recommended; doing it brings reward, leaving it is not sinful.
واجب (wajib): An action of the Prophet proven by zanni evidence, obligatory for the ummah but sub-fard.
فرض (fard): An action of the Prophet proven by qat'i evidence, mandatory for the ummah.
زلة (zallah): An unintentional lapse or mistake by the Prophet, not to be emulated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, which of the following is an example of a wajib action of the Prophet?
A) Eating and drinking
B) Saying Bismillah in wudu
C) Prostration of forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw)
D) Performing the five daily prayers

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's intentional actions are divided into four categories for the ummah based on evidence strength: mubah, mustahab, wajib (zanni) and fard (qat'i); zallah is excluded from emulation.

Categories of the Prophet's Actions (Sunan Fi'liyyah)
Classifying the Prophet's actions into four categories plus zallah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five categories of the Prophet's actions (mubah, mustahab, wajib, fard, zallah) and apply the Hanafi principle that iqtida' only applies to the first four, while explaining the rationale for the inclusion of wajib as a separate category.

Core Idea
The Prophet's actions are of four types for emulation; a fifth, zallah, is a slip never to be followed.

In this lesson, we examine the classification of the Prophet's (PBUH) actions according to Hanafi usul. Understanding these categories is crucial because not every action of the Prophet is equally binding; some are merely permissible, while others are recommended or obligatory. We will also address the unique concept of 'zallah' – an unintentional slip that carries no legal weight for emulation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main classification
The passage states that the Prophet's actions are of four types: mubah (permissible), mustahab (recommended), wajib (obligatory), and fard (compulsory). Note that later it mentions a fifth, zallah, which is not for iqtida'.
Only intentional actions are considered; actions in sleep or forgetfulness have no ruling.
2
Distinguish the basis for inclusion of wajib
The author includes wajib separately from fard even though many usul scholars combine them. The reason given: the division is from our perspective. For us, actions proven by speculative (zanni) evidence are wajib, even though from the Prophet's side they are all equally practiced. This answers the doubt about why wajib is a separate category.
This reflects the Hanafi position on the epistemological status of proofs.
3
Understand the concept of zallah
Zallah is an unintentional slip, like falling or an unintended mistake. It is not suitable for iqtida' because it lacks intention and is accompanied by a declaration that it was a slip. Examples include Musa (AS) striking the Copt and the fall of a person while walking.
The declaration can come from the prophet himself or from Allah.
4
Address the absence of haram and makruh
The passage explains why haram and makruh are not listed: prophets are protected from sin (major and minor per Maturidis), so such actions do not occur from them. Therefore, they are not categories of the Prophet's actions.
This is based on the doctrine of 'isma (infallibility).
5
Apply the classification
Given a specific action of the Prophet, determine which category it falls into. This requires knowing the evidence for the action and whether it was done intentionally and consistently.
For example, eating is mubah; saying bismillah in wudu is mustahab; sajdah sahw is wajib; performing salah is fard.

And that which is connected to the verbal sunnahs are the actions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and they are four categories: permissible, recommended, obligatory, and compulsory. And among them is another category, which is the slip (zallah), but it is not at all from this chapter because it is not suitable for following, and it is never free from being accompanied by an indication that it is a slip. Translation: And that which is connected to the verbal sunnahs are the actions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and they are four types: permissible, recommended, obligatory, and compulsory. And among these actions there is another type, and that is the slip (error), but this type is not in any ruling from this chapter, i.e., the chapter of following, because this type does not possess the capacity for following, and this type is never free from being accompanied by an indication that it is a slip. Explanation: The author, after finishing the explanation of the verbal sunnahs, is explaining the practical sunnahs. The status of the practical sunnahs is after the verbal sunnahs, therefore it is mentioned after the verbal sunnahs. By 'actions of the Messenger' are meant those actions that issued from him (peace be upon him) intentionally; if they occurred in a state of sleep or forgetfully, then following them is not permissible, nor are those actions characterized as good or bad. The actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) are of four types: (1) permissible, like eating, drinking, clothing, etc.; (2) recommended, like saying bismillah in ablution, combing the beard; (3) obligatory, like the prostration of forgetfulness; (4) compulsory, like the pillars of prayer, fasting, etc. Here a doubt may arise: all usuliyyin have mentioned three types of actions: permissible, recommended, and compulsory, and they have included obligatory in compulsory, because obligatory is that which is established by a proof that contains doubt and uncertainty, and in any action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) doubt cannot occur. The answer to this is that this division is from our perspective, not from the perspective of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and some actions are established for us by a speculative proof, therefore for us obligatory is realized. The author says that besides the mentioned four types, there is another type called 'zillah' (slip), i.e., a mistake, a lapse, meaning that there was no intention to do something and it happened unintentionally, and it is not persisted upon, like a person falling while walking – he did not intend to fall, but fell and then stood up, not remaining fallen. This is called zallah, like when Moses (peace be upon him) struck a blow and the Copt died, but Moses (peace be upon him) did not intend to kill. The author says that zallah is not from the chapter of following, i.e., if an action occurs from the Prophet (peace be upon him) as a slip, then the ummah will not follow him in that action; rather, it is necessary that such an indication be attached to the slipful action that declares it to be a slip. This indication sometimes comes from the doer himself, as when Moses (peace be upon him) said, 'This is from the work of Satan,' as if Moses regretted his action and sought forgiveness; and sometimes this indication comes from Allah, as when a slip of eating from the tree occurred from Adam (peace be upon him), so Allah said, 'And Adam disobeyed his Lord, so he went astray,' and 'And Adam forgot, and We did not find in him determination.' Here a question may arise: the author mentioned the four types that are followed, and also mentioned the action that is not followed, like zallah, so the author should also have mentioned haram and makruh, because like zallah, they are also not followed. The answer to this is that haram and makruh are not found in the actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him), because the prophets (peace be upon him) are, according to the majority of Muslims, protected from major sins, and according to us, i.e., the Maturidis, they are protected from minor sins as well, contrary to the Ash'aris. And haram and makruh fall under major and minor sins. In short, their occurrence from prophets is impossible. Therefore, there was no need to mention them.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the categories of the Prophet's actions (sunan fi'liyyah). The author first states the principle: the actions of the Prophet that are connected to the verbal sunnah are of four types—mubah (permissible), mustahab (recommended), wajib (obligatory), fard (compulsory)—and a fifth type, zallah (slip). However, zallah is not from the chapter of iqtida (following) because it cannot be followed; it must be accompanied by a declaration that it was a slip. The commentary then clarifies that practical sunnahs follow verbal sunnahs in rank. Actions from the Prophet are considered only if done intentionally; actions in sleep or forgetfully have no ruling. The four types are exemplified: mubah like eating, mustahab like saying bismillah in wudu, wajib like sajdah sahw, fard like the pillars of salah. A doubt is raised: why did the author include wajib as a separate category when most usul scholars only list three (mubah, mustahab, fard)? The answer: the division is from our perspective; actions known by speculative proofs become wajib for us, though from the Prophet's perspective they are all practiced. The author then explains zallah with examples: Moses unintentionally killing a Copt and falling while walking. Such actions are not to be emulated and require a declaration (either from the prophet or from Allah) that it was a slip. Finally, a question about why haram and makruh are not listed is answered: prophets are protected from all sin (major and minor according to Maturidis), so these categories do not apply to their actions.

Key Terms
سنت فعلیہ (sunnah fi'liyyah): The actions of the Prophet that he did intentionally and are suitable for emulation.
زلة (zallah): An unintentional slip or error from the Prophet that is not to be followed and must be accompanied by a declaration that it was a mistake.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the Prophet's actions for religious practice; only acts from the first four categories (mubah, mustahab, wajib, fard) are followed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is 'zallah' not included in the categories of the Prophet's actions that are to be emulated?
A) Because it is a prohibited act.
B) Because it is an unintentional slip and is accompanied by a declaration that it was a mistake, making it unsuitable for emulation.
C) Because it is a type of wajib action that is only for prophets.
D) Because it occurs only in sleep.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's actions are of four types for emulation; slips (zallah) are not to be followed and must be declared as such.

Al-Jassas' Principle on Following the Prophet's Actions
Resolving the dispute on following the Prophet's actions using al-Jassas' principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply al-Jassas' principle to determine the ruling of performing a prophetic action when the manner is unknown.

Core Idea
Follow the Prophet in known manner; default to ibahah when manner is unknown.

This lesson resolves a key usul dispute: how should we emulate the Prophet's actions when we are unsure of the legal rank (wajib, mandub, mubah) with which he performed them? Imam al-Jassas, a leading Hanafi usuli, provides a clear principle that balances adherence to the sunnah with avoiding unnecessary obligation. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying the sunnah fi'liyyah in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action and its known/unknown manner
Distinguish whether the Prophet's manner of performing the action is known. 'Manner' (jihah) refers to the specific legal category (wajib, mustahab, mubah) in which he performed it.
If the manner is known from a clear textual indication (e.g., a command), it is known.
2
Apply the first part of al-Jassas' rule
If the manner is known, we must follow the Prophet in that exact manner. For example, if he performed wudu in a particular sequence, we follow that sequence.
This ensures precise emulation of the sunnah.
3
Apply the second part of the rule
If the manner is unknown, we default to the lowest rank among the Prophet's actions, which is permissibility (ibahah).
This prevents assuming obligation without proof.
4
Recall the rationale
The reason for this default is that following the Prophet (itiba') is the established default principle. We cling to it as far as possible, but only a specific proof (dalil khhusus) can raise the action from ibahah to a higher rank.
The burden of proof is on those claiming obligation.
5
Recognize the practical difference (thamarah)
Al-Jassas' view avoids burdening the ummah with unnecessary obligations. For example, if the Prophet wore a garment but we do not know whether he did so as wajib or mubah, the Hanafi ruling is that wearing it is mubah.
Other schools may require investigation or assume a higher rank.

وَاخْتُلِفَ فِي سَائِرِ اَفْعَالِهِ وَالصَّحِيحُ مَا قَالَهُ الْجَصَّاصُ اَنَّ مَا عَلِمْنَا مِنْ أَفْعَالِ الرَّسُوْلِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَاقِعَا عَلَى جِهَةٍ نَقْتَدِئُ بِهِ فِي اِيْقَاعِهِ عَلَى تِلْكَ الْجِهَةِ وَمَالَمْ نَعْلَمْهُ عَلَى أَي جِهَةٍ فَعَلَهُ فَلَنَا فِعْلُهُ عَلَى أَدْنَى مَنَازِلِ أَفْعَالِهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَهُوَ الْإِبَاحَة لِاَنَّ الْإِتَبَاعَ أَصْلٌ فَوَجَبَ التَّمْشُكَ به حَتَّى يَقُومَ دَلِيْلُ خُصُوصِهِ بِه - ترجمہ:۔ اور نبی علیہ السلام کے تمام افعال کی اقتدا میں اختلاف کیا گیا ہے، اور صحیح بات وہ ہے جو ابوبکر جصاص نے کہی ہے کہ جن افعال رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو ہم جانتے ہیں کہ کس جہت پر واقع ہیں تو ہم بھی اس فعل کو اس طریقہ پر کرنے میں آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی اقتدا کریں گے، اور جس فعل کو نہیں جانتے ہیں کہ کس طریقہ پر آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس کو کیا ہے تو ہمارے لئے اس فعل کو آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے افعال کے درجات میں ادنی درجہ پر کرنا جائز ہے، اور ادنی درجہ اباحت ہے۔
And there is disagreement concerning the rest of his actions. And the correct view is what al-Jassas said: that what we know of the actions of the Messenger (peace be upon him) to have occurred in a particular manner, we follow him in performing it in that manner. And what we do not know in what manner he did it, then we are permitted to do it at the lowest of the ranks of his actions (peace be upon him), which is permissibility (ibahah), because following is the default, so clinging to it became obligatory until a proof for its specificity stands. Translation: And there is disagreement concerning the rest of his actions. And the correct statement is what Abu Bakr al-Jassas said: that the actions of the Messenger (peace be upon him) which we know in what manner they occurred, we will follow him in performing that action in that manner. And the action which we do not know in what manner the Prophet (peace be upon him) did it, then for us it is permissible to do that action at the lowest level of the ranks of his actions (peace be upon him), and the lowest level is permissibility (ibahah).
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage addresses the ikhtilaf (disagreement) among scholars regarding how to follow the Prophet's actions (af'al) that are not clearly categorized as obligatory or recommended. The correct position, according to the author, is that of Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas (a prominent Hanafi usuli). His principle: when we know the precise manner (jihah) in which the Prophet performed an act, we must follow him in that exact manner. For example, if we know he performed wudu in a specific sequence, we follow that sequence. However, if we are uncertain about the manner—whether he did it as wajib, mustahab, or simply as mubah—then we are free to perform the action at the lowest rank of his actions, which is ibahah (permissibility). The reason: following the Prophet (itiba') is the default principle, and we adhere to it as far as possible. A proof of specificity (dalil khhusus) would be needed to raise the action from ibahah to a higher rank. This ruling is significant for Hanafi usul as it provides a methodology for emulating the Prophet's sunnah fi'liyyah when the exact legal nature of the act is unknown, ensuring that the act remains permissible rather than assuming obligation.

Key Terms
جہت (jihah): The specific manner or way in which the Prophet performed an action, e.g., as wajib, mustahab, or mubah.
ادنی منازل (adna manazil): The lowest rank among the categories of the Prophet's actions, which is ibahah (permissibility).
التبع (al-itiba'): Following the Prophet; the default principle that requires emulation of his actions unless excused.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Jassas, what is the ruling on performing an action of the Prophet when we do not know the manner in which he did it?
A) It is wajib because following is required.
B) It is mubah because the default is permissibility.
C) It is haram because we might do it incorrectly.
D) It is mustahab because it is a sunnah.

Key Takeaway
When the Prophet's manner in an action is unknown, the Hanafi default is permissibility (ibahah) until a specific proof indicates otherwise.
